Chapter of Option. Separate discussion on the Option of Stipulation. His statement: 'Chapter of Option'; know that sale may be binding, which is that in which there is no option after the existence of its conditions, and it may be non-binding, which is that in which there is an option. Since the first is stronger in being a sale, the author presented it and brought this chapter for the second. The types of option, even if they reach seventeen as detailed by the author of 'al-Ashbah', but three of them are presented independently: the option of stipulation, the option of sight, and the option of defect due to the abundance of their rulings and the magnitude of their issues. So the author presented the option of stipulation because it prevents the beginning of the ruling, then the option of sight because it prevents the completion of the ruling, then the option of defect because it prevents the binding of the ruling. Option means choice. He said in 'al-Misbah al-Munir': 'Option is choice, and from it is said: option of sight.' End. The expression 'You have the option' means choice, whatever you want. And in 'Muntaha' end. His statement: 'Know that option is established by text contrary to analogy because He forbade a sale and a condition, but the text came with it.' And it is what al-Hakim narrated in 'al-Mustadrak' from Ibn 'Umar who said: 'Habban ibn Munqidh, and he was among those who witnessed Uhud, and he was a weak man whose head was struck with an ulmameh - meaning a head wound reaching the membrane of his brain - so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave him the option in what he bought for three days, and his tongue had become heavy, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to him: Sell and say: No cheating - meaning no deception - and he used to buy something and bring it to his family and they would say: This is expensive, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would say: He gave me the option in the sale.' Thus mentioned by 'Allama al-Tahawi from 'Allama Nuh. [11] His statement: 'Option of stipulation'; meaning the choice to rescind or ratify due to its stipulation, even after the sale, so the addition is of the type of adding the ruling to its cause, and this addition is common: so it does not occur that the appropriate is the stipulation of the option. [2] His statement: 'For each of the two contracting parties.' Sufyan al-Thawri and Ibn Shubruma said: It is valid for the buyer, not for the seller; because it is established contrary to analogy, so it is confined to the subject of the text, which is the buyer, based on what al-Hakim narrated from the earlier hadith. And ours: The option of stipulation is permitted due to people's need for it to prevent deception by deliberation, and that is equal for the seller and buyer, and also the wording of Ibn Majah: 'When you sell' (idha ba'ata) includes selling and buying. [3] His statement: 'And for them' is connected to his statement 'for each': meaning it is valid for each singly, or for both together, or it is a new statement to clarify the duration of the option, and the first is more appropriate. [4] His statement: 'Three days' is accusative as an adverbial: meaning the option is in three days, or nominative as a predicate, so the subject is his statement 'the option'; meaning the duration of the option is three days, and the first is more appropriate. The option of stipulation is for each of the two contracting parties, and for them three days or less, not more.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the scope and duration of Khayar al-Shart (the option of stipulation) in sales. The author begins by defining the chapter: sale can be binding (lazim) or non-binding due to an option. Among the many types of option, three are primary: option of stipulation, option of sight, and option of defect. The option of stipulation is presented first because it prevents the initial conclusion of the sale (i.e., the sale remains suspended until the option period ends). The word 'khayar' means choice. The author then establishes that the option is proven by textual evidence (nass) contrary to the general prohibition of combining a sale with a condition, citing the hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh narrated by al-Hakim. In that hadith, the Prophet gave Habban a three-day option due to his weakness. The matn (core ruling) states: 'Khayar al-Shart is for each of the two contracting parties, and for them three days or less, not more.' The commentator explains that 'for each' means both buyer and seller, singly or together. Then a dispute is presented: Sufyan al-Thawri and Ibn Shubruma hold that the option is only for the buyer, arguing that since it is contrary to analogy, it must be limited to the specific case mentioned in the hadith (the buyer). The Hanafi response (li-na) is that the option was legislated due to people's need to prevent being cheated, and this need applies equally to buyer and seller. Moreover, the wording in Ibn Majah's version ('When you sell' – idha ba'ata) covers both selling and buying, indicating it applies to both parties. The commentator also clarifies the duration: the option period is three days or less, not more. The 'three days' is an adverbial or predicate; the first interpretation (adverbial) is preferred.

Key Terms
خيار (khayar): The right to choose between rescinding or ratifying a contract; equivalent to option in law.
خيار الشرط (khayar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract giving one or both parties the right to rescind within a specified period (max. three days).
ثلاثة أيام (thalathat ayyam): The maximum duration for khayar al-shart; three days or less.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the buyer
B) Only the seller
C) Both buyer and seller
D) Neither party

Key Takeaway
Khayar al-shart is a valid option for both parties up to three days, established by the hadith of Habban and extended to the seller by the common need to prevent deception.

The Option of Stipulation (Khiyar al-Shart): Duration and Parties
Ruling on khiyar al-shart with duration and opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart, identify the evidence, and explain the disputes regarding duration and parties.

Core Idea
The seller and buyer may stipulate an option up to three days; exceeding that invalidates the sale unless ratified within three.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents the Hanafi ruling on the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). It establishes that both contracting parties may stipulate an option for up to three days, and any longer period invalidates the sale unless the option is exercised within the three-day limit. The author then rebuts opposing views from within and outside the Hanafi school, grounding the ruling in textual proof and rational necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening statement: the option is for each of the two contracting parties, and the maximum duration is three days or less. This is the established Hanafi position.
Note the phrase 'لا أكثر' (not more) which is the basis of the limitation.
2
Examine the evidence for both parties
The text provides a hadith from Ibn Majah: 'When you sell' (إذا بايعت) which includes both seller and buyer. Also, necessity (hajah) applies equally to both parties to prevent being cheated through deliberation.
Consider why the Hanafi school rejects the view restricting the option to the buyer only (Sufyan al-Thawri and Ibn Shubruma).
3
Understand the intra-madhhab dispute on duration
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) allow any specified duration, citing Ibn 'Umar's incident and rational need. Abu Hanifa insists on three days because the option contradicts the default bindingness of the contract and is permitted only by text limited to three days.
This is a classic Hanafi usul conflict: textual restriction vs. general need.
4
Evaluate the rebuttals
The commentary refutes the opposing views: Ibn 'Umar's case likely refers to khiyar al-ru'y or al-'ayb, not khiyar al-shart. Long durations introduce gharar (deception). The analogy to deferment of the price is incorrect because deferment serves a different purpose (ability to pay).
Notice how the author systematically addresses each objection.
5
Apply the exception clause
If a longer option is stipulated, the sale is invalid unless the party with the option ratifies within three days. This exception preserves the maximum limit while allowing a practical remedy.
The exception is a key nuance often overlooked by students.

كتاب البيع باب الخيار - خيار الشرط -
خيارُ الشَّرْط لكل من العاقدين، ولهما ثلاثة أيام أو أقل لا أكثر

وقل : لا خلابه - أي لا خداع - وكان يشتري الشيء ويجيء به إلى أهله فيقولون: هذا غال، فيقول رسول الله الله خيرني في بيع . كذا ذكره العلامة الطحطاوي له عن العلامة نوح . قوله : خيار الشرط ؛ أي الاختيار للفسخ أو الإجازة بسبب شرطه، ولو بعد البيع، فالإضافة من قبيل إضافة الحكم إلى سببه ، وهذه الإضافة شائعة : فلا يَرِدُ أن المناسب شرط الخيار. قوله : لكل من العاقدين، وقال سفيان الثوري وابن شبرمة : يجوز للمشتري لا للبائع ؛ لأنه ثبت على خلافِ القياس، فيقتصر على موردِ النص، وهو المشتري بما أخرجه الحاكم من حديث مذكور سابقاً. ولنا : إن خيار الشرط إنما جاز ؛ لحاجة الناس إليه ؛ لدفع الغبن بالتروي، وذلك يستوي فيه البائع والمشتري، على أن لفظ ابن ماجه: «إذا بايعت»)، وهو يشمل البيع والشراء. قوله : ولهما ؛ معطوف على قوله : «لكلّ»: أي صح لكل منهما منفرد، أو لهما معاً، أو كلام مبتدأ ؛ لبيان مدة الخيار، والأول أولى. قوله : ثلاثة أيام ؛ منصوب على الظرفية : أي الخيار في ثلاثة أيام أو مرفوع على الخبرية ، فكان المبتدأ قوله : «الخيار» ؛ أي مدة الخيار ثلاثة أيام، والأول أولى.

إلا أنه يجوز إن أجاز في الثلاث : أي إذا بيع وشُرِطَ الخِيارُ أكثر من ثلاثةِ أيامٍ لا يجوز البيع خلافا لهما

قوله : إلا أنه ... الخ ؛ استثناء من قوله: «لا أكثر» ؛ أي إن ذكر الأكثر من ثلاثة أيام وأجاز مَن له الخيار في الثلاث جاز.
قوله : خلافاً لهما ؛ فإنّهما قالا : يجوز إذا سمّى مدة معلومة شهراً كان أو سنةً أو أكثر منها نقلاً وعقلاً:
أما النقلُ : فحدث ابن عمر له أنه أجاز الخيار إلى شهرين. وأما العقل : فالخيار إنما شرع للحاجة إلى التّروّي والتفكير؛ ليندفع الغبن، وقد تمس الحاجة إلى الأكثر فصار كالتأجيل.
والجواب عن النقل: أنَّ حديث ابن حبان مشهور، فلا يعارضه حكاية حال ابن عمر، على أن في الحديث المذكور أن ابن عمر له أجاز الخيار، وليس فيه خيار الشرط، فيمكن أن يراد به خيار الرؤية أو العيب.
والجواب عن العقل : أنّ كثير المدَّة ليس كقليلها، فإن في الكثير معنى الغرور زائد، والقياس على التأجيل في الثمن غير صحيح؛ لأنَّ الأجل يشترط للقدرة على الأداء، وهي إنما تكون بالكسب، وهو لا يحصل في كل مدة، فقد يُحتاجُ إلى مدة طويلة.
وقال مالك : مدة الخيار ما يمكن اختيار المبيع في مثله، فإن كان المبيع مما لا يبقى أكثر من يوم كالفاكهة لم يجز أن يشترط في أكثر من يوم، وإن كان فيه صنعة لا يمكن الوقوف عليها في ثلاثةِ أَيَّام يجوز أن يشترط فيه أكثر من ثلاثة أيام ؛ لأنه شرع للحاجة إلى التروي ، وهي تندفع بذلك. ذكره في «كمال الدراية»).
ولأبي حنيفة : لأن مقتضى العقد، وهو اللّزوم وخيار الشرط يُخالفه، لكن جوزناه بالنص فيقتصر على ما هو المذكور فيه، وهو ثلاثة أيام.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Options: Option of Stipulation. The option of stipulation is for each of the two contracting parties, and they have three days or less, not more. And he said: It is for no deceit—i.e., no trickery—and he used to buy something and bring it to his family, and they would say: This is expensive, so the Messenger of Allah ﷺ would say: Give me the option in the sale. Thus mentioned by Allamah al-Tahawi from Allamah Nuh. His statement: Option of stipulation means the choice to rescind or ratify due to its stipulation, even after the sale, so the addition is of the type of attributing the ruling to its cause, and this addition is common, so it is not objected that the appropriate thing is the stipulation of the option. His statement: For each of the two contracting parties. Sufyan al-Thawri and Ibn Shubruma said: It is permissible for the buyer, not for the seller, because it is established contrary to analogy, so it is restricted to the textual instance, which is the buyer, based on what al-Hakim extracted from a hadith mentioned previously. And we have that the option of stipulation is only permitted due to people's need for it to prevent being cheated by deliberation, and that applies equally to the seller and the buyer, especially since the wording of Ibn Majah: 'When you sell' includes both selling and buying. His statement: And they have—it is conjoined to his statement: 'For each' meaning it is valid for each individually, or for both together, or it is a new sentence to explain the duration of the option, and the first is more appropriate. His statement: Three days—it is in the accusative expressing duration, i.e., the option is for three days, or it is in the nominative as predicate, so the subject is his statement: 'The option', i.e., the duration of the option is three days, and the first is more appropriate. Except that it is permissible if he ratifies within the three, i.e., if the sale is made and the option is stipulated for more than three days, the sale is not permissible, contrary to them (the two companions). His statement: Except that... etc. is an exception from his statement: 'Not more', i.e., if he mentions more than three days and the one with the option ratifies within the three, it is permissible. His statement: Contrary to them, for they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is permissible if he specifies a known duration, whether a month or a year or more, based on transmission and reason. As for transmission: The incident of Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he allowed the option up to two months. As for reason: The option is only legislated for the need of deliberation and reflection to prevent being cheated, and the need may demand more, so it is like deferment. The response to the transmission: The hadith of Ibn Hibban is well-known, so the incident of Ibn 'Umar does not contradict it, especially since in the mentioned hadith Ibn 'Umar allowed the option, and there is no stipulation of option in it, so it is possible that what is meant is the option of inspection or defect. The response to reason: A long duration is not like a short one, for in the long there is an additional element of deception, and analogy to deferment of the price is incorrect because deferment is required for ability to pay, which is achieved by earning, and that is not obtained in every duration, so a long duration may be needed. Malik said: The duration of the option is according to what enables inspection of the sold item in its like; if the sold item does not last more than a day, like fruits, it is not permissible to stipulate more than a day; if it involves craftsmanship that cannot be ascertained in three days, it is permissible to stipulate more than three days, because it is legislated for the need of deliberation, and that is achieved thereby. This was mentioned in 'Kamal al-Dirayah'. And for Abu Hanifa: Because the requirement of the contract is bindingness, and the option of stipulation contradicts it, but we permitted it based on text, so it is restricted to what is mentioned in it, which is three days.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, presents the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in sales. The passage type is a ruling with proofs, followed by intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab disputes. The author begins by stating the core ruling: the option of stipulation is available to both the buyer and the seller, and its maximum duration is three days or less, not more. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi). The commentary immediately clarifies that the term 'khiyar al-shart' refers to the choice to rescind or ratify the contract, made conditional by the parties, even after the sale. The phrase 'for each of the two contracting parties' is interpreted to mean that either party alone or both together may stipulate the option. The duration of 'three days' is explained as the maximum period; the option may be for a shorter time. Next, the author addresses opposing views. Sufyan al-Thawri and Ibn Shubruma restrict the option to the buyer only, arguing that khiyar is exceptional and should be limited to the textual precedent. The Hanafi response, based on necessity ('hajat al-nas'), is that both parties equally need protection against being cheated through deliberation, and the hadith of Ibn Majah ('When you sell') covers both seller and buyer. The main intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the duration: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions) permit any specified period, even months or years, based on the incident of Ibn 'Umar allowing a two-month option and the rational need for longer deliberation. Abu Hanifa restricts it to three days because the contract's default is bindingness ('luzum'), and the option is a dispensation based solely on the text, which mentions three days. The commentary systematically refutes the two companions' arguments: the transmission from Ibn 'Umar is not specifically about khiyar al-shart but may refer to the option of inspection or defect; rationally, a long period involves increased uncertainty ('gharar'), and the analogy to deferment of payment fails because deferment is for ability to pay, not for deliberation. Finally, Imam Malik's position is mentioned: the option period varies with the nature of the item—up to one day for perishables, longer for items requiring inspection. This passage highlights the Hanafi commitment to textual limitation, the use of istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity, and the systematic rebuttal of rival views through hadith analysis and rational argument.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The right to rescind or ratify a contract due to a stipulation inserted in the contract, typically for a specified period.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'y): The option of inspection, where a buyer can rescind upon seeing the item if it was unseen at contract.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to rescind due to a defect in the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a seller and buyer stipulate an option of ten days?
A) The sale is valid with the full ten-day option.
B) The sale is invalid unless they reduce it to three days before concluding.
C) The sale is invalid unless the party with the option ratifies within three days.
D) The sale is valid but the option defaults to three days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) limits khiyar al-shart to three days for both parties, with an exception permitting validation if the option is exercised within that period.

Khiyar al-Naqd: Ruling and Its Mechanism
Ruling and justifications for khiyar al-naqd with a time limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-naqd with a three-day limit and explain why dropping the extra day before it takes effect validates the contract.

Core Idea
In khiyar al-naqd, dropping the extra day before it attaches removes the defect from the contract.

This lesson unpacks the core ruling on khiyar al-naqd, where a buyer stipulates payment within a set period or the sale is void. The text presents the Hanafi position that a three-day limit is valid, and if the buyer pays within three days, the contract becomes sound. We will explore why dropping the extra day before it is effective cures the initial defect, and contrast the rebuttal to Zufar's opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on three-day vs four-day conditions
Read the base ruling: if the condition is three days, the sale is valid if paid within three; if four days, it is initially invalid but becomes valid if paid within three. Understand the legal hukm.
The difference hinges on the duration of the stipulated option.
2
Analyze the mechanism of validation
Study the two justifications (Iraq and Khurasan): either the defect is removed by dropping the extra day before it takes effect, or the contract is suspended on the extra day. Grasp how the contract turns from defective to valid.
Both justifications ensure the invalidating element never attaches to the contract.
3
Examine Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response
Zufar argues the contract is void ab initio and cannot be rectified, analogizing to a riba sale. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the defect here is not inherent but due to the future condition, which can be dropped.
This sharpens the understanding of what constitutes a curable defect vs an incurable one.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the buyer pays within three days, the sale is valid under Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but remains invalid under Zufar. This difference affects actual transactions.
The mufta bihi is the three-day limit, following the majority.

Source Text

فإن اشترى على أنه إن لم يَنْقُدِ الثَّمَنَ إلى ثلاثة أيام فلا بيع صح، وإلى أربعة لا ، فَإِنْ نَقَدَ فِي الثَّلَاث جاز) : وإنما أدخل لفظة الفاء في قوله : فإن اشترى [١] قوله : جاز البيع ؛ لأنّ من له الخيار أسقط المفسد في إجازته في الثلاثة قبل تقرره، فصار كما لو باع جذعاً في سقف، ثمّ نزعه وسلّمه إليه ؛ وذلك لأنه انعقد فاسداً ؛ إذ الظاهر دوامهما على الشرط ، فإذا أسقطا الزَّائدَ قبل مجيئه تبيَّنَ أَنَّ الأمر على خلاف ذلك، فانقلب صحيحاً، وهذا قول مشايخ العراق. أو لأن المفسد اتصال اليوم الرابع بالمدّة ، فإذا أجاز من له الخيار قبله لم يتصل المفسد بالعقد، وصار كأنه لم يشترط الخيار في الرابع ، وهذا عند مشايخ خُراسان : فإنَّ عندهم العقد موقوف على إسقاط الزائد، فإذا مضى جزء من الرابع فسد العقد، ذكره في «كمال الدراية»). [٢]قوله : خلافاً لزفر ؛ فإنّ عنده لا يجوز ؛ لأنَّ العقد انعقد فاسداً بفساد الشرط الثابت فيه، فلا ينقلب صحيحاً بإسقاطه، كما لو باع درهماً بدرهمين، ثمَّ أسقط الدرهم الزائد. [٣] قوله : صح ؛ والأصلُ في خيارِ النّقدِ أنه بمعنى شرط الخيار ؛ لأن معنى الخيار نقد الثمن على تقدير إجازة البيع وعدم نقده على تقدير فسخ البيع، فكذا هاهنا إن شاء نقد الثّمن فتم البيع، وإن شاء لم ينقد، فانفسخ البيع ؛ إذ الحاجة مست إلى الانفساخ عدم السد احترازا عن المماطلة في الفسخ ، فيلحق خيار النقد بخيار الشرط. [٤]قوله : وإلى أربعة لا ؛ أي لا يصح البيع عند أبي حنيفة له وأبي يوسف الله عند وقال محمد ه : يجوز إلى أربعة أيام أو أكثر. (٥) قوله : إنما أدخل ؛ هذا تصوير التفريع، ودفع ما يتوهم أن ما سبق كان مسألة شرط الخيار، والمذكور هاهنا خيارُ النّقدِ فما وجه التفريع، وحاصل الدفع أن المذكور لأنه فرع مسألة خيارِ الشَّرط ؛ لأَنَّ خِيارَ الشَّرْطِ إِنما شُرعَ ليدفع بالفَسْخِ الضَّرَرَ عن نفسه سواء كان الضَّرَر تأخير أداءِ الثَّمَن ، أو غيره. فإذا كان الخيار لضررِ التَّأْخِيرِ من صُورِ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ فالتصريح به يكونُ من فُرُوع خيارِ الشَّرطِ ، وهذا الذي ذُكِرَ قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد له ، فإِنَّهُ يَجُوز في الأكثر ، فهو جَرَى على أصلِهِ في التجويز في الأكثر، وأبو حنيفة له جَرَى على أصْلِهِ في عدم التجويز في الأكثر ، أما أبو يوسف له إِنَّما لم يُجَوِّزْ هاهنا جرياً على القياس، وجَوَّزَهُ ثَمة لأثرِ ابنِ عُمَرَ له فإِنَّهُ جوزهُ إلى شهرين. هاهنا من صور خيار الشرط ؛ لأنّ الشَّارِعَ إِنّما وضعه لدفع الضررِ – بالفتح - والضرر أعم من أن يكون تأخير أداءِ الثَّمن وغيره، فالمذكور يكون من فروع خيار الشرط. [١] قوله : فإنه يجوز ؛ أي فإنه قال بجواز خيار الشرط في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام ومسألة خيار النقد من فروع خيارِ الشَّرط فجرى على أصله هاهنا في تجويزه أيضاً في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام. [٢]قوله : جرى ؛ فإنّه قال بعدم جواز خيارِ الشَّرط في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام. [٣] قوله : أما أبو يوسف له حاصله : أنه أخذ في الأصل يعني في خيارِ الشَّرط بأثر ابن عمر له ، وهو أنه أجاز الخيار إلى شهرين وأخذ في خيار النقد بالقياس؛ لأنَّ القياس في خيار الشرط ما قاله الإمام ، وإنما تركه صاحباه بالأثر المذكور، ولا أثر هاهنا فبقى هذه الصورة على القياس
If he buys on condition that if he does not pay the price within three days, then no sale, it is valid; and for four days, it is not. So if he pays within three, the sale is valid. [Commentary] He said: 'It is valid' because the one who has the option drops the invalidating element (mufsid) by his acceptance within three days before it takes effect. It is like selling a beam in a roof and then removing it and delivering it. This is because the contract is concluded as defective, as the apparent situation is that they both persist on the condition. So if they drop the extra period before its arrival, it becomes clear that the matter was otherwise, and it turns into a valid contract. This is the view of the scholars of Iraq. Or because the invalidating element is the connection of the fourth day to the term. So if the one with the option accepts before it, the invalidating element does not connect to the contract, and it becomes as if he did not stipulate the option for the fourth. This is according to the scholars of Khurasan: with them, the contract is suspended on dropping the extra. So if part of the fourth passes, the contract becomes void. Mentioned in Kamil al-Dirayah. [2] He said: 'Contrary to Zufar' because with him it is not valid, as the contract is concluded defective due to the defective condition established in it, so it cannot turn into a valid contract by dropping it, just as if he sold a dirham for two dirhams and then dropped the extra dirham. [3] He said: 'Valid'. The principle of khiyar al-naqd is that it is in the meaning of khiyar al-shart, because the meaning of the option is to pay the price if the sale is accepted and not to pay if the sale is rescinded. So here, if he wishes, he pays the price and the sale is completed; if he wishes, he does not pay and the sale is rescinded. There is a need for rescission to avoid procrastination in rescission. So khiyar al-naqd is annexed to khiyar al-shart. [4] He said: 'And for four days, no', meaning the sale is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is valid for four days or more. (5) He said: 'Indeed he introduced' – this is a depiction of the branching, and a rebuttal to the misunderstanding that the preceding was a case of khiyar al-shart, and here it is khiyar al-naqd, so what is the aspect of branching? The summary of the rebuttal is that the mentioned case is a branch of khiyar al-shart, because khiyar al-shart was legislated to repel harm by rescission, whether the harm is delay in paying the price or something else. So if the option is for harm of delay, it is among the forms of khiyar al-shart, so explicating it falls under the branches of khiyar al-shart. This mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. Indeed, he (Muhammad) permits it in the greater (number of days), so he followed his principle of allowing in the greater. Abu Hanifa followed his principle of not allowing in the greater. As for Abu Yusuf, he did not allow here, following analogy, but allowed there (in khiyar al-shart) due to the athar of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), as he permitted the option up to two months. Here, the option is a form of khiyar al-shart, because the Lawgiver only placed it to repel harm – with fatha – and harm is general: it may be delay in paying the price or otherwise. So the mentioned case becomes a branch of khiyar al-shart. [1] He said: 'Indeed he permits' – he (Muhammad) said by the permissibility of khiyar al-shart for more than three days, and the case of khiyar al-naqd is a branch of khiyar al-shart, so he followed his principle here in permitting it also for more than three days. [2] He said: 'He followed' – he (Abu Hanifa) said by non-permissibility of khiyar al-shart for more than three days. [3] He said: 'As for Abu Yusuf' – its summary: he took in the original (i.e. in khiyar al-shart) the athar of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), that he permitted the option up to two months, and took in khiyar al-naqd by analogy, because analogy in khiyar al-shart is what the Imam (Abu Hanifa) said, and his two companions only left it due to the mentioned athar. And there is no athar here, so this case remains on analogy.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-naqd (option of payment). The base ruling: if a buyer stipulates that he must pay the price within three days or the sale is void, the sale is valid. If he stipulates four days, it is invalid. However, if he pays within three days, the sale becomes valid. The commentator explains two justifications from the scholars of Iraq and Khurasan: either the defect is removed by dropping the extra day before it attaches, or the contract is suspended. Then a dispute with Zufar: he holds the contract is void from inception and cannot be corrected, akin to a riba-based sale. The main ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the option limited to three days; Muhammad allows more. The commentator links khiyar al-naqd to khiyar al-shart: the option of payment is a branch of the option of condition because both aim to avoid harm. Abu Yusuf followed the athar of Ibn Umar in khiyar al-shart (allowing up to two months) but applied qiyas to khiyar al-naqd due to lack of textual evidence, thus restricting it to three days. The relied-upon position is the three-day limit.

Key Terms
خيار النقد (khiyar al-naqd): The option of payment, where the buyer has the choice to pay the price or rescind the sale within a specified period.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract, exercised by the party holding the option.
مفسد (mufsid): The invalidating element that must be dropped before it takes effect to preserve the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the Hanafi ruling if a buyer stipulates payment within four days but pays on the third day?
A) The sale is invalid because the condition was for four days.
B) The sale is valid because the extra day is dropped before it takes effect.
C) The sale is suspended until the fourth day.
D) The sale is valid only if the seller agrees.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar al-naqd, a condition exceeding three days is initially invalid, but the sale becomes valid if payment is made within three days, as the extra period is dropped before it takes effect.

Khiyar al-Naqd as a Branch of Khiyar al-Shart
Link between khiyar al-naqd and khiyar al-shart, and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why khiyar al-naqd is considered a branch of khiyar al-shart and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the time limit.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-naqd is annexed to khiyar al-shart because both options aim to prevent harm from delayed payment.

This lesson dives into the conceptual link between khiyar al-naqd (option of payment) and khiyar al-shart (option of condition). The text explains that the option of payment is essentially a form of option of condition because both are designed to allow rescission to avoid harm, particularly from non-payment. We will then examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the permissible duration, tracing how each imam's stance on khiyar al-shart influences their ruling on khiyar al-naqd.

Guided Path
1
Understand the annexation (ilhaq) of khiyar al-naqd to khiyar al-shart
Read the passage that states: 'The principle of khiyar al-naqd is that it is in the meaning of khiyar al-shart, because the meaning of the option is to pay the price if the sale is accepted and not to pay if the sale is rescinded.' Grasp that both options give a party the right to withdraw to avoid harm.
The annexation is based on the common illa: preventing harm from delayed payment or other defects.
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi positions on the time limit
Identify each imam's view: Abu Hanifa restricts to three days in both khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-naqd. Muhammad allows more than three days in both. Abu Yusuf allows more than three days in khiyar al-shart (due to athar) but restricts khiyar al-naqd to three days (due to qiyas).
Note the asymmetry in Abu Yusuf's positions: he follows textual evidence (athar) in khiyar al-shart but reverts to analogy in khiyar al-naqd.
3
Analyze the role of the athar of Ibn Umar
The passage mentions the athar of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that permits the option of condition up to two months. Abu Yusuf relied on this athar to extend the period in khiyar al-shart, but for khiyar al-naqd, no such text exists, so he applies qiyas, returning to the three-day limit.
This shows how textual evidence can override qiyas when available.
4
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah)
If a buyer stipulates a 10-day payment option, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf would say the condition is invalid, but payment within three days validates the sale. Muhammad would deem the whole condition valid. The mufta bihi is the three-day limit.
The thamarah affects how a mufti advises parties in such transactions.

[١] قوله : فإنه يجوز ؛ أي فإنه قال بجواز خيار الشرط في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام ومسألة خيار النقد من فروع خيارِ الشَّرط فجرى على أصله هاهنا في تجويزه أيضاً في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام. [٢]قوله : جرى ؛ فإنّه قال بعدم جواز خيارِ الشَّرط في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام. [٣] قوله : أما أبو يوسف له حاصله : أنه أخذ في الأصل يعني في خيارِ الشَّرط بأثر ابن عمر له ، وهو أنه أجاز الخيار إلى شهرين وأخذ في خيار النقد بالقياس؛ لأنَّ القياس في خيار الشرط ما قاله الإمام ، وإنما تركه صاحباه بالأثر المذكور، ولا أثر هاهنا فبقى هذه الصورة على القياس
If he buys on condition that if he does not pay the price within three days, then no sale, it is valid; and for four days, it is not. So if he pays within three, the sale is valid. [Commentary] He said: 'It is valid' because the one who has the option drops the invalidating element (mufsid) by his acceptance within three days before it takes effect. It is like selling a beam in a roof and then removing it and delivering it. This is because the contract is concluded as defective, as the apparent situation is that they both persist on the condition. So if they drop the extra period before its arrival, it becomes clear that the matter was otherwise, and it turns into a valid contract. This is the view of the scholars of Iraq. Or because the invalidating element is the connection of the fourth day to the term. So if the one with the option accepts before it, the invalidating element does not connect to the contract, and it becomes as if he did not stipulate the option for the fourth. This is according to the scholars of Khurasan: with them, the contract is suspended on dropping the extra. So if part of the fourth passes, the contract becomes void. Mentioned in Kamil al-Dirayah. [2] He said: 'Contrary to Zufar' because with him it is not valid, as the contract is concluded defective due to the defective condition established in it, so it cannot turn into a valid contract by dropping it, just as if he sold a dirham for two dirhams and then dropped the extra dirham. [3] He said: 'Valid'. The principle of khiyar al-naqd is that it is in the meaning of khiyar al-shart, because the meaning of the option is to pay the price if the sale is accepted and not to pay if the sale is rescinded. So here, if he wishes, he pays the price and the sale is completed; if he wishes, he does not pay and the sale is rescinded. There is a need for rescission to avoid procrastination in rescission. So khiyar al-naqd is annexed to khiyar al-shart. [4] He said: 'And for four days, no', meaning the sale is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is valid for four days or more. (5) He said: 'Indeed he introduced' – this is a depiction of the branching, and a rebuttal to the misunderstanding that the preceding was a case of khiyar al-shart, and here it is khiyar al-naqd, so what is the aspect of branching? The summary of the rebuttal is that the mentioned case is a branch of khiyar al-shart, because khiyar al-shart was legislated to repel harm by rescission, whether the harm is delay in paying the price or something else. So if the option is for harm of delay, it is among the forms of khiyar al-shart, so explicating it falls under the branches of khiyar al-shart. This mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. Indeed, he (Muhammad) permits it in the greater (number of days), so he followed his principle of allowing in the greater. Abu Hanifa followed his principle of not allowing in the greater. As for Abu Yusuf, he did not allow here, following analogy, but allowed there (in khiyar al-shart) due to the athar of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), as he permitted the option up to two months. Here, the option is a form of khiyar al-shart, because the Lawgiver only placed it to repel harm – with fatha – and harm is general: it may be delay in paying the price or otherwise. So the mentioned case becomes a branch of khiyar al-shart. [1] He said: 'Indeed he permits' – he (Muhammad) said by the permissibility of khiyar al-shart for more than three days, and the case of khiyar al-naqd is a branch of khiyar al-shart, so he followed his principle here in permitting it also for more than three days. [2] He said: 'He followed' – he (Abu Hanifa) said by non-permissibility of khiyar al-shart for more than three days. [3] He said: 'As for Abu Yusuf' – its summary: he took in the original (i.e. in khiyar al-shart) the athar of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), that he permitted the option up to two months, and took in khiyar al-naqd by analogy, because analogy in khiyar al-shart is what the Imam (Abu Hanifa) said, and his two companions only left it due to the mentioned athar. And there is no athar here, so this case remains on analogy.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-naqd (option of payment). The base ruling: if a buyer stipulates that he must pay the price within three days or the sale is void, the sale is valid. If he stipulates four days, it is invalid. However, if he pays within three days, the sale becomes valid. The commentator explains two justifications from the scholars of Iraq and Khurasan: either the defect is removed by dropping the extra day before it attaches, or the contract is suspended. Then a dispute with Zufar: he holds the contract is void from inception and cannot be corrected, akin to a riba-based sale. The main ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the option limited to three days; Muhammad allows more. The commentator links khiyar al-naqd to khiyar al-shart: the option of payment is a branch of the option of condition because both aim to avoid harm. Abu Yusuf followed the athar of Ibn Umar in khiyar al-shart (allowing up to two months) but applied qiyas to khiyar al-naqd due to lack of textual evidence, thus restricting it to three days. The relied-upon position is the three-day limit.

Key Terms
خيار النقد (khiyar al-naqd): The option of payment, where the buyer has the choice to pay the price or rescind the sale within a specified period.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of condition, where a party stipulates the right to rescind the contract within a specified period (default three days in Hanafi).
أثر ابن عمر (athar Ibn Umar): A narration from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) allowing the option of condition up to two months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Yusuf allow a longer period in khiyar al-shart but not in khiyar al-naqd?
A) He followed qiyas in both.
B) He found an athar from Ibn Umar for khiyar al-shart but not for khiyar al-naqd.
C) He considered khiyar al-naqd more harmful.
D) He believed the three-day limit is absolute for all options.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-naqd is annexed to khiyar al-shart, but the duration rule may differ based on available evidence; the relied-upon position restricts khiyar al-naqd to three days.

Seller's Ownership During the Option Period
Ruling with proof on seller's ownership during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the seller retains ownership during khiyar and explain the legal reasoning (talil) based on the seller's incomplete satisfaction.

Core Idea
During the option period, the sold item remains the seller's property — his satisfaction is incomplete.

This lesson examines a foundational rule in Hanafi sales law: the seller retains ownership of the sold item during the option period (khiyar). The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains why this is the case and what legal consequences follow. Understanding this ruling is crucial for distinguishing when ownership transfers in a sale and the seller's rights during the option.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact legal statement: the sold item does not leave the seller's ownership during his khiyar.
This is a clear rule; commit it to memory.
2
Identify the legal cause (illah)
Examine the reasoning: the seller's satisfaction (rida) is not complete because the option implies potential dissatisfaction with the transfer of ownership.
The illah is incomplete rida; it is a rational (talil) proof.
3
Apply the ruling to dispositions
Determine the effect: the seller's actions as owner (gifting, freeing a slave, intercourse) are valid and constitute rescission (faskh) of the sale.
Any act inconsistent with ownership transfer is considered a rescission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخرج مبيع عن ملك بائعه مع خياره زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية [٤]قوله : ولا يخرج ؛ لأن خروجه إنما يكون برضاء البائع، ولا يتم الرضاء مع الخيار ؛ لأنه يفيد عدم الرّضاء بزوال ملكه فلا يخرجُ المبيع عن ملكه، ويصح تصرف البائع في البيع في مدة الخيار : كتصرُّف الملاك من الهبة والعتق والوطء وغيرها، ويصير فسخا للبيع.
And the sold item does not leave the seller's ownership during his option. [Heading: Zubdat al-Nihayah li 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah] [4] He said: 'And it does not leave' because its removal is only by the seller's satisfaction, and satisfaction is not complete with the option, because it (the option) indicates lack of satisfaction with the removal of his ownership. So the sold item does not leave his ownership, and the seller's dispositions in the sale during the option period are valid: like the dispositions of owners such as gifting, freeing (a slave), sexual intercourse, and others. And these become a rescission of the sale.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental Hanafi rule: during the khiyar (option) period, the sold item remains in the ownership of the seller. The reason is that the seller's complete satisfaction (rida) with the transfer of ownership is not present because the option implies that he may not be satisfied with losing ownership. As a result, ownership does not transfer to the buyer. Consequently, any action the seller takes regarding the item during the option period—such as gifting it to someone, freeing a slave (if the item is a slave), or having intercourse with a female slave—is valid as an owner's disposition. Importantly, such actions are considered a rescission (faskh) of the sale contract, as they are inconsistent with the continued existence of the sale. This ruling distinguishes the Hanafi school from others; for example, in the Shafi'i school, the item is considered to have transferred to the buyer subject to the option.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): An option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period; in this context, the seller's option.
ملك (milk): Ownership; here it refers to the seller's legal ownership of the sold item.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; the seller's actions that are inconsistent with the sale effectively rescind the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
During the khiyar (option) period, what is the legal effect of the seller gifting the sold item to a third party?
A) The gift is void because the item is already sold.
B) The gift is valid and acts as a rescission of the sale.
C) The gift is valid only if the buyer consents.
D) The gift is suspended until the option period ends.

Key Takeaway
During the option period, the seller retains ownership, and his dispositions are valid as rescission of the sale.

Ownership Retention During the Seller's Option and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Khiyar al-Naqd
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-naqd and ownership retention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ownership retention during the seller's option and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the extension of khiyar al-naqd beyond three days.

Core Idea
The sold item remains in seller's ownership during his option period, but the permissible duration of different option types divides the Hanafi school.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah establishes a key fiqh ruling: when a seller has an option (khiyar), ownership of the sold item does not transfer to the buyer. The passage then examines a derivative issue: the option of payment (khiyar al-naqd). While Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf limit it to three days, Imam Muhammad permits a longer period. We will explore the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the core ruling: the sold item does not leave the seller's ownership during his option period. Understand the rationale: the option is to prevent harm, and the seller's consent to transfer ownership is incomplete during the option.
2
Identify the derivative issue
Recognize that khiyar al-naqd (option of payment) is a branch of khiyar al-shart (option of condition). The harm being prevented here is delay in payment.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not permit khiyar al-naqd for more than three days, while Imam Muhammad permits it for more than three days.
This is the point of disagreement within the school.
4
Trace each imam's usul
Analyze the bases: Abu Hanifa follows his general principle of not extending khiyar al-shart beyond three days. Abu Yusuf follows the athar of Ibn Umar in khiyar al-shart (allowing up to two months) but applies qiyas in khiyar al-naqd due to the absence of a specific athar. Muhammad follows his principle of permissibility in the majority.
Abu Yusuf's position shows a shift between usul and sub-issue based on available evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Muhammad's view, the buyer may have more than three days to pay; under the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), payment must be made within three days or the sale is void.
The practical difference is the time allowed for payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخرج مبيع عن ملك بائعه مع خياره لأنه فرع مسألة خيار الشرط; لأن خيار الشرط إنما شرع ليدفع بالفسخ الضرر عن نفسه سواء كان الضرر تأخير أداء الثمن أو غيره. فإذا كان الخيار لضرر التأخير من صور خيار الشرط فالتصريح به يكون من فروع خيار الشرط، وهذا الذي ذكر قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد، فإنه يجوز في الأكثر، فهو جرى على أصله في التجويز في الأكثر، وأبو حنيفة جرى على أصله في عدم التجويز في الأكثر، أما أبو يوسف فإنما لم يجز هاهنا جرياً على القياس، وجوزه ثمة لأثر ابن عمر فإنه جوزه إلى شهرين. ثم قال: (ولا يخرج مبيع عن ملك بائعه مع خياره) هاهنا من صور خيار الشرط; لأن الشارع إنما وضعه لدفع الضرر، والضرر أعم من أن يكون تأخير أداء الثمن وغيره، فالمذكور يكون من فروع خيار الشرط. قوله إنه يجوز: أي فإنه قال بجواز خيار الشرط في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام ومسألة خيار النقد من فروع خيار الشرط فجرى على أصله هاهنا في تجويزه أيضاً في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام. قوله جرى: فإنه قال بعدم جواز خيار الشرط في أكثر من ثلاثة أيام. قوله أما أبو يوسف: حاصله أنه أخذ في الأصل يعني في خيار الشرط بأثر ابن عمر، وهو أنه أجاز الخيار إلى شهرين، وأخذ في خيار النقد بالقياس; لأن القياس في خيار الشرط ما قاله الإمام، وإنما تركه صاحباه بالأثر المذكور، ولا أثر هاهنا فبقيت هذه الصورة على القياس. قوله ولا يخرج: لأن خروجه إنما يكون برضاء البائع، ولا يتم الرضاء مع الخيار; لأنه يفيد عدم الرضاء بزوال ملكه فلا يخرج المبيع عن ملكه، ويصح تصرف البائع في البيع في مدة الخيار: كتصرف الملاك من الهبة والعتق والوطء وغيرها، ويصير فسخاً للبيع.
The sold item does not leave the seller's ownership while he has the option, because it is a branch of the issue of option of condition; for the option of condition was legislated to ward off harm by cancellation, whether the harm is delay in payment of the price or otherwise. So if the option is for harm of delay from the forms of option of condition, then explicit stipulation of it is from the branches of option of condition. And this which is mentioned is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, for he permits it in the majority, so he followed his principle in permitting in the majority, and Abu Hanifa followed his principle in not permitting in the majority. As for Abu Yusuf, he did not permit here following analogy, and permitted there due to the effect of Ibn Umar, for he permitted it up to two months. Then he said: (And the sold item does not leave the seller's ownership while he has the option) here it is from the forms of option of condition; because the legislator only placed it to ward off harm, and harm is more general than being delay of payment of the price or other. So the mentioned is from the branches of option of condition. His saying "he permits": meaning he said permissibility of option of condition for more than three days and the issue of option of payment is from branches of option of condition, so he followed his principle here in permitting also for more than three days. His saying "he followed": meaning he said non-permissibility of option of condition for more than three days. His saying "As for Abu Yusuf": the gist is that he took in the original, meaning in option of condition, the effect of Ibn Umar, and he permitted the option up to two months, and he took in option of payment by analogy; because the analogy in option of condition is what the Imam said, and his two companions only left it due to the mentioned effect, and there is no effect here, so this case remained on analogy. His saying "and does not leave": because its leaving only occurs with the consent of the seller, and consent is not complete with the option; because it indicates non-consent to the removal of his ownership, so the sold item does not leave his ownership, and the seller's disposition in the sale during the option period is valid: like the dispositions of owners such as gift, manumission, intercourse, and others, and it becomes cancellation of the sale.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage opens by stating the ruling that the sold item does not leave the seller's ownership while the seller has an option (خيار). The commentator explains that this is a branch of the broader issue of خيار الشرط (option of condition). The rationale is that the option was legislated to prevent harm (ضرر), and here the harm is the delay in payment of the price. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad permits the option for more than three days (following his general principle of allowing option in the majority of cases), while Abu Hanifa does not permit it beyond three days. Abu Yusuf takes a middle position: he followed the athar (narration) of Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنه) who allowed the option up to two months in the original issue of خيار الشرط, but in the sub-issue of خيار النقد he applied qiyas (analogy) and thus did not permit extension beyond three days. The commentary also clarifies that the seller's consent is incomplete during the option period, so the item remains his property, and he may validly dispose of it (e.g., gift, manumission, intercourse), which would constitute a cancellation of the sale.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract that allows one or both parties to cancel the contract within a specified period.
خيار النقد (khiyar al-naqd): A specific type of option where the buyer is given a period to pay the price; if he fails, the sale is void.
سوم الشراء (sawm al-shira'): A transaction where a buyer takes possession of an item on approval, with an agreement to buy if satisfied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Imam Muhammad regarding the option of payment (خيار النقد)?
A) He does not permit it for more than three days.
B) He permits it for more than three days.
C) He only permits it up to two months following an athar.
D) He follows Abu Hanifa's position.

Key Takeaway
The sold item remains the seller's property during his option period, and within the Hanafi school, khiyar al-naqd is generally limited to three days, with Imam Muhammad permitting a longer period due to his usul.

Liability for Value During Seller's Option
Ruling with proof: liability for value during seller's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a buyer who takes possession during the seller's option period is liable for the value (or the like if fungible) if the item perishes, and explain the reasoning based on the analogy to bargaining purchase (sawm al-shira').

Core Idea
Possession during seller's option guarantees the item—destruction obligates value, not price.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling: when a seller grants the buyer possession during an option period, the buyer becomes liable if the item perishes. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains that the buyer must pay the value (or the like if fungible), drawing an analogy to a bargaining purchase (sawm al-shira'). We will walk through the proofs and a disagreement with Ibn Abi Layla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The seller has the option (khiyar al-ba'i), the buyer takes possession of the sold item, and the item perishes during the option period.
2
State the ruling
The buyer is liable for the value (qima) if the item is non-fungible, or the like (mithl) if it is fungible.
This is the Hanafi position (wajib).
3
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The text states: 'because it is possession on the basis of bargaining purchase, and it is guaranteed with value' (لأنه مقبوض على سوم الشراء، وهو مضمون بالقيمة). This is an analogy (qiyas) to the established ruling of bargaining purchase.
The seller only consented to possession via the contract, not as a trust.
4
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The original case (asl) is bargaining purchase where the buyer takes possession with permission but no ownership yet—if it perishes, he is liable for value. The new case (far') is possession during the seller's option. The shared effective cause (illa) is possession under a contract with a specified price, which creates liability.
If the price is not specified (e.g., 'go with this, if you like it, buy it'), there is no liability.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and response
Ibn Abi Layla held no liability, considering the buyer an amin (trustee). The Hanafi response: the seller's permission was solely via the contract, not a trust, so the item is guaranteed.
The Hanafi view is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قبضه المشتري فهلك يجب عليه بالقيمة: أي بيع بشرط الخيار للبائع فقبضه المشتري فهلك في يده يجب عليه القيمة، لأنه مقبوض على سوم الشراء، وهو مضمون بالقيمة. ويخرج عن ملك البائع مع خيار المشتري، فهلكه في يده بالثمن كتعيبه. قوله فهلك في يده: أي في مدة الخيار; فإنه لو هلك بعدها فيلزمه الثمن لا القيمة; لبطلان الخيار. قوله يجب عليه القيمة: وقال ابن أبي ليلى: لا شيء عليه; لأنه أمين فيه حيث قبضه بإذن صاحبه، وإنا نقول: البائع ما رضي بقبضه إلا بجهة العقد، والمقبوض بجهة العقد يكون مضموناً بالقيمة: كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. كذا في «الكفاية». قوله لأنه مقبوض على سوم الشراء: حاصله: أن البيع لما كان موقوفاً بوجود الخيار فينفسخ بهلاك المبيع، والمعقود عليه ما هلك صار بحيث لا يجوز ابتداء العقد عليه، فلا تكون الإجازة ملحقة به، فالمبيع بقي مقبوضاً في يده على سوم الشراء. قوله وهو مضمون بالقيمة: إذا لم يكن مثلياً، فإن كان مثلياً فعليه المثل، ثم إن المقبوض على سوم الشراء إنما يكون مضموناً إذا كان الثمن مسمى حتى إذا قال: اذهب بهذا الثوب إن رضيته اشتريته، فذهب به فهلك، لا يضمن، ولو قال: إن رضيته اشتريته بعشرة، فذهب به فهلك ضمن قيمته، وعليه الفتوى. كذا في «الكفاية». قوله ويخرج... الخ: لأن البيع من جهة بائعه لازم; لأن الخيار شرع نظراً لمن هو له، فيعمل في حقه دون الآخر. قوله بالثمن: لأن المبيع إذا قرب من الهلاك يكون معيباً، وبالتعيب استحكم العقد، ولا يمكن الرد، ولزم الثمن لهلاكه على ملكه. قوله كتعيبه: كما إذا دخل عيب لا يرتفع كقطع اليد، وإن كان يرتفع [؟]
If the buyer takes possession and it perishes, he is liable for the value: meaning a sale with option of condition for the seller, and the buyer took possession and it perished in his hand, he is liable for the value, because it is a possession on the basis of bargaining purchase, and it is guaranteed with value. And it leaves the seller's ownership when the buyer has the option, so its destruction in his hand is against the price like its becoming defective. His saying "perished in his hand": meaning during the option period; for if it perished after it, then the price is incumbent, not the value, due to the termination of the option. His saying "he is liable for the value": Ibn Abi Layla said: nothing is upon him, because he is a trustee in it since he took possession with the owner's permission. But we say: the seller did not consent to its possession except by way of the contract, and what is taken possession of by way of contract is guaranteed with value: like possession on the basis of bargaining purchase. So in 'al-Kifaya'. His saying "because it is possession on the basis of bargaining purchase": the gist is that since the sale is suspended due to the existence of the option, it is annulled by the destruction of the sold item, and the object of contract has perished such that it is not permissible to initiate the contract upon it, so the authorization is not annexed to it, so the sold item remains in his possession on the basis of bargaining purchase. His saying "and it is guaranteed with value": if it is not a fungible (mithli), for if it is fungible, then the like is upon him; then that which is possessed on the basis of bargaining purchase is only guaranteed if the price is specified, so if he said: go with this garment, if you like it you buy it, and he went with it and it perished, he does not guarantee; but if he said: if you like it you buy it for ten, and he went with it and it perished, he guarantees its value, and upon that is the fatwa. So in 'al-Kifaya'. His saying "and it leaves...": because the sale from the seller's side is binding; because the option was legislated for the benefit of whomever it is for, so it operates in his favor not the other. His saying "against the price": because when the sold item approaches destruction it becomes defective, and by becoming defective the contract becomes firm, and return is not possible, and the price becomes incumbent due to its destruction in his ownership. His saying "like its becoming defective": as when a non-removable defect enters, like cutting off the hand, even if it is removable [?]
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses two scenarios. First: if the seller has the option and the buyer takes possession, and the item perishes in the buyer's hand during the option period, the buyer must pay the value (or the like if fungible). The reasoning is that the sale is suspended (because of the option), and the buyer's possession is akin to possession on the basis of bargaining purchase (سوم الشراء), which is guaranteed. The commentator distinguishes between fungible and non-fungible goods, and also clarifies that the price must be specified for liability. Second: if the buyer has the option (and the seller does not), the sold item leaves the seller's ownership immediately, so if it perishes in the buyer's hand, the buyer owes the price, not the value. This is because the sale is binding on the seller (since the option is for the buyer), so the transfer of ownership is effective. The destruction is then treated like a defect that makes the contract firm.

Key Terms
سوم الشراء (sawm al-shira'): A transaction where a buyer takes possession of an item on approval, with an agreement to buy if satisfied.
مثلي (mithli): A fungible good that has a like counterpart in the market, e.g., grains, oils.
قيمة (qima): The monetary value of an item, determined by market price at the time of destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the buyer has the option (not the seller), what does he pay if the item perishes during the option period?
A) The value (qima) or the like (mithl).
B) The price (thaman).
C) Nothing.
D) Only the value if the price was not specified.

Key Takeaway
During the seller's option, destruction of the item in the buyer's hand obligates payment of its value (or like), not the price, provided the price was specified.

Liability for Price When Buyer Has Option
Ruling: destruction during buyer's option obligates price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that when the buyer has the option (khiyar al-mushtari), the sold item leaves the seller's ownership immediately, so destruction obligates the price, and distinguish this from the seller's option scenario.

Core Idea
Buyer's option transfers ownership; destruction requires payment of the full price.

This lesson covers a distinct scenario: when the buyer holds the option (and the seller does not), the sale is binding on the seller from the outset. As the passage explains, the sold item leaves the seller's ownership, so if it perishes in the buyer's hand, the buyer must pay the price, not the value. This contrasts with the previous lesson on seller's option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The buyer has the option (khiyar al-mushtari). The seller has no right to cancel. The buyer takes possession, and the item perishes during the option period.
This assumes a sale contract with the condition of an option for the buyer.
2
State the ruling
The buyer must pay the price (thaman), not the value.
The text says: 'فهلكه في يده بالثمن' (its destruction in his hand is against the price).
3
Understand the reasoning
Because the sale is binding on the seller from the moment of contract. The option only benefits the buyer. Therefore, the sold item leaves the seller's ownership immediately, and the buyer bears the risk. The destruction is treated like the occurrence of a defect that solidifies the contract.
The commentator says: 'لأن البيع من جهة بائعه لازم' (the sale from the seller's side is binding).
4
Compare with seller's option scenario
In seller's option, ownership does not transfer immediately; the seller retains the right to cancel, so destruction requires value (like bargaining purchase). Here, ownership has transferred, so the full price is due.
This distinction is crucial for practical application.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern example
If a buyer purchases a car with a 3-day inspection option (buyer's option), and the car is stolen, the buyer must still pay the full price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

خيار المشتري (khiyar al-mushtari): The option held by the buyer to cancel the sale within a specified period.
ثمن (thaman): The price agreed upon in the sale contract.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the buyer owe the price when the item perishes during the buyer's option?
A) Because the seller has agreed to sell at that price.
B) Because the sale is binding on the seller and ownership transfers to the buyer.
C) Because the buyer is a trustee.
D) Because the option is only for the seller's benefit.

Key Takeaway
When the buyer holds the option, the sale is binding on the seller, so destruction in the buyer's hand obligates payment of the full price, not the value.

Liability for Destroyed Item during Khiyar al-Shart: Basic Ruling and Proof
Commentary on the ruling of liability when a sold item perishes during the option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a buyer who takes possession of a sold item during khiyar al-shart is liable for its value if it perishes, and explain the qiyas proof using the principle of sawm al-shira'.

Core Idea
Possession under an option sale is guaranteed because it is taken by virtue of the contract, not mere trust.

When a seller grants an option to himself and the buyer takes delivery, the sale is suspended. If the item is destroyed during the option period, the buyer must pay its value, not the contracted price. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the key proof: the buyer is like a person who takes an item on approval with a specified price (sawm al-shira').

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The sale includes a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) for the seller. The buyer takes physical possession during the option period.
The option period is typically three days or as agreed.
2
State the ruling
If the item perishes, the buyer is liable for its value (qimah) if it is non-fungible, or for the like (mithl) if it is fungible.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the proof
The item is 'possessed on the basis of purchase' (sawm al-shira'), meaning it is taken with the intent to buy under a specified price. Such possession creates a guarantee (daman) for the value.
The author compares it to taking a garment with a price: 'If you like it, buy it for ten'.
4
Note the opposing view
Ibn Abi Layla argued the buyer is an amin (trustee) since he took possession with permission, and thus has no liability.
This is rejected by the Hanafi school.
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The buyer took possession 'by virtue of the contract' (bijahat al-aqd), not by mere permission. Possession by virtue of a contract is guaranteed, analogous to sawm al-shira'.
The contract's suspended nature does not remove the guarantee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الخيار - خيار الشرط. 
فإن قبضه المشتري فهلَكَ يَجبُ عليه بالقيمة ، ويخرجُ عن ملك البائع مع خيارِ المشتري ، فهُلْكُهُ في يَدِهِ بِالشَّمنِ كتَعييه
فإن قبضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي فهلَكَ يَجِبُ عليه بالقيمة : أي بيع بشرط الخيار للبائع فقبضَهُ فهلَكَ في يده يجب عليه القيمة ، لأنه مقبوضٌ على سوم الشّراء ، وهو مضمون بالقيمة.
( ويخرج عن ملك البائع مع خيار المشتري ، فهُلْكُهُ فِي يَدِهِ بالثَّمن كتعبيه ) 
قوله : فهلك في يده ؛ أي في مدة الخيار ؛ فإنه لو هلك بعدها فيلزمه الثمن لا القيمة ؛ لبطلان الخيار.
قوله : يجب عليه القيمة ؛ وقال ابن أبي ليلى : لا شيء عليه ؛ لأنه أمين فيه حيث قبضه بإذن صاحبه، وإنّا نقول : البائع ما رضي بقبضه إلا بجهة العقد، والمقبوض بجهة العقد يكون مضموناً بالقيمة : كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. كذا في «الكفاية».
قوله : لأنه مقبوض على سوم الشراء ؛ حاصله : أن البيع لما كان موقوفاً بوجودِ الخيار فينفسخ بهلاك المبيع، والمعقود عليه ما هلك صار بحيث لا يجوز ابتداء العقد عليه ، فلا تكون الإجازة ملحقة به، فالمبيعُ بقي مقبوضاً في يده على سوم الشراء.
قوله : وهو مضمون بالقيمة ؛ إذا لم يكن مثليّاً، فإن كان مثلياً فعليه المثل، ثمّ إن المقبوض على سومِ الشّراءِ إنما يكون مضموناً إذا كان الثمن مسمى حتى إذا قال : اذهب بهذا الثوب إن رضيته اشتريته، فذهب به فهلك، لا يضمن، ولو قال : إن رضيته اشتريته بعشرة ، فذهب به فهلك ضمن قيمته، وعليه الفتوى. كذا في «الكفاية».
قوله : ويخرج ... الخ ; لأنَّ البيع من جهة بائعه لازم ; لأنَّ الخيارَ شُرعَ نظراً لمن هو له، فيعمل في حقه دون الآخر.
قوله : بالثمن ; لأن المبيع إذا قرب من الهلاك يكون معيباً، وبالتعيب استحكم العقد، ولا يمكن الردّ ، ولزم الثَّمن لهلاكه على ملكه.
قوله : كتعيبه ; كما إذا دخلَهُ عيب لا يرتفع كقطع اليد، وإن كان يرتفع كالمرض فهو على خياره ، فإن ارتفع في المدّة لا يلزم، وإلا يلزم، وعن الشافعي أيضاً : يلزم البيع بالتعيب. ذكره العَيْني في «شرح الكنز».
Chapter of Sales, Section on Option - Option of Stipulation. If the buyer takes possession and it perishes, he is liable for the value, and it leaves the seller's ownership with the buyer's option, so its destruction in his hand is [treated] by the price like its defect. If the buyer takes possession and it perishes, he is liable for the value: meaning a sale with a condition of option for the seller, then he takes possession and it perishes in his hand, he is liable for the value, because it is possessed on the basis of purchase (sawm al-shira'), and it is guaranteed by the value. (And it leaves the seller's ownership with the buyer's option, so its destruction in his hand is by the price like its defect.) His saying: 'perishes in his hand' means during the option period, for if it perishes after that, the price is obligatory, not the value, because the option is void. His saying: 'he is liable for the value'; Ibn Abi Layla said: nothing is upon him, because he is an amin since he took possession with the owner's permission. But we say: the seller did not consent to his possession except by virtue of the contract, and what is possessed by virtue of the contract is guaranteed by the value, like what is possessed on the basis of purchase (sawm al-shira'). Thus in al-Kifaya. His saying: 'because it is possessed on the basis of purchase'; its summary: since the sale is suspended due to the existence of the option, it is annulled by the destruction of the sold item, and the object of contract having perished, it becomes such that initiating a contract upon it is not permissible, so the ratification does not attach to it, so the sold item remains possessed in his hand on the basis of purchase. His saying: 'and it is guaranteed by the value'; if it is not a fungible (mithli), but if it is a fungible, then he is liable for the like. Then, what is possessed on the basis of purchase is only guaranteed if the price is specified; so if he says: 'Take this garment, if you like it, buy it,' and he takes it and it perishes, he is not liable; but if he says: 'If you like it, buy it for ten,' and he takes it and it perishes, he is liable for its value, and the fatwa is upon this. Thus in al-Kifaya. His saying: 'and it leaves...' because the sale from the seller's side is binding, because the option is legislated for the benefit of the one for whom it is, so it operates in his favor and not against the other. His saying: 'by the price' because when the sold item is on the verge of destruction, it becomes defective, and by the defect the contract becomes firm, and return is not possible, and the price is obligatory due to its destruction while in his ownership. His saying: 'like its defect' as when a defect that cannot be removed, like cutting off a hand, enters it; if it can be removed like illness, then it remains under his option; if it is removed within the period, it does not become obligatory, otherwise it becomes obligatory. Also from al-Shafi'i: the sale becomes binding by the defect. Mentioned by al-'Ayni in Sharh al-Kanz.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of a sale with an option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) for the seller. The main point is that if the buyer takes possession of the item during the option period and it is destroyed, the buyer is liable to pay the value (qimah) of the item, not the contracted price (thaman). The reasoning is that because the sale is suspended (mawquf) due to the option, the destruction of the item cancels the sale, and the item is considered to be in the buyer's possession on the basis of purchase (sawm al-shira'), similar to taking an item on approval with a specified price. This is distinguished from the case where the option is for the buyer, which will be discussed later. The commentary also notes that if the item is fungible (mithli), the buyer must return the like (mithl). An important condition is that the price must be specified for liability to apply. If a person says 'Take this garment, if you like it, buy it' without specifying a price, there is no liability. But if the price is specified, liability arises. The commentator also addresses an objection by Ibn Abi Layla, who argued that the buyer is an amin (trustee) and thus not liable. The Hanafi response is that the buyer took possession by virtue of the contract, and possessions by virtue of a contract are guaranteed. Additionally, if the item becomes defective (ta'ayyab) instead of being destroyed, the same ruling applies: the contract becomes binding and the price is due, similar to the ruling on destruction.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in the contract allowing one or both parties to cancel the sale within a specified period.
سوم الشراء (sawm al-shira'): Possession of an item for evaluation or approval with the intent to purchase, typically with a specified price.
مثلي (mithli): A fungible item that has standard equivalents in the market, such as grains or currencies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale with an option for the seller, if the buyer takes possession and the item is destroyed during the option period, what is the buyer liable for?
A) The contracted price (thaman)
B) The value (qimah) or the like if fungible
C) Nothing, because he is an amin
D) The value only if the price was not specified

Key Takeaway
The buyer's liability during khiyar al-shart is based on the principle of possession by virtue of contract, not trust, and the measure of compensation is the value or the like, not the price.
