Conditions of Liability in Khiyar al-Shart: Fungibles, Price Specification, and Defects
Commentary on conditions of liability in khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions under which the buyer is liable when an item perishes during khiyar al-shart, including the distinction between fungible and non-fungible goods, the requirement of a specified price, and the effect of defects.

Core Idea
Liability for destruction during option requires a specified price; for fungibles, the like is owed; defects before destruction also trigger liability.

The previous lesson established the basic liability. Now we examine three important conditions: (1) the price must be specified for liability to arise; (2) if the item is fungible, the buyer must return a similar item, not its value; (3) if the item becomes defective instead of being destroyed, the same ruling applies—the contract becomes binding and the price is due. This lesson delves into the nuances drawn from the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition of price specification
The text states that for possession on approval (sawm al-shira') to create liability, the price must be mentioned. If a person says 'Take this garment; if you like it, buy it' without a price, there is no liability.
This is from al-Kifaya.
2
Distinguish between fungible (mithli) and non-fungible (qimi)
If the item is fungible (e.g., grain), the buyer owes the like (mithl); if non-fungible (e.g., car), he owes the value (qimah).
This applies to all cases of guaranteed possession.
3
Apply the ruling to defects (ta'ayyub)
If the item becomes defective during the option period, the same ruling as destruction applies: the contract becomes binding and the price is due.
The defect must be permanent; if temporary (e.g., illness), the option remains until the defect is removed.
4
Note the Shafi'i perspective
Imam al-Shafi'i also holds that a defect makes the sale binding, as mentioned by al-'Ayni.
This is not a dispute but a concurrence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الخيار - خيار الشرط. 
فإن قبضه المشتري فهلَكَ يَجبُ عليه بالقيمة ، ويخرجُ عن ملك البائع مع خيارِ المشتري ، فهُلْكُهُ في يَدِهِ بِالشَّمنِ كتَعييه
فإن قبضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي فهلَكَ يَجِبُ عليه بالقيمة : أي بيع بشرط الخيار للبائع فقبضَهُ فهلَكَ في يده يجب عليه القيمة ، لأنه مقبوضٌ على سوم الشّراء ، وهو مضمون بالقيمة.
( ويخرج عن ملك البائع مع خيار المشتري ، فهُلْكُهُ فِي يَدِهِ بالثَّمن كتعبيه ) 
قوله : فهلك في يده ؛ أي في مدة الخيار ؛ فإنه لو هلك بعدها فيلزمه الثمن لا القيمة ؛ لبطلان الخيار.
قوله : يجب عليه القيمة ؛ وقال ابن أبي ليلى : لا شيء عليه ؛ لأنه أمين فيه حيث قبضه بإذن صاحبه، وإنّا نقول : البائع ما رضي بقبضه إلا بجهة العقد، والمقبوض بجهة العقد يكون مضموناً بالقيمة : كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. كذا في «الكفاية».
قوله : لأنه مقبوض على سوم الشراء ؛ حاصله : أن البيع لما كان موقوفاً بوجودِ الخيار فينفسخ بهلاك المبيع، والمعقود عليه ما هلك صار بحيث لا يجوز ابتداء العقد عليه ، فلا تكون الإجازة ملحقة به، فالمبيعُ بقي مقبوضاً في يده على سوم الشراء.
قوله : وهو مضمون بالقيمة ؛ إذا لم يكن مثليّاً، فإن كان مثلياً فعليه المثل، ثمّ إن المقبوض على سومِ الشّراءِ إنما يكون مضموناً إذا كان الثمن مسمى حتى إذا قال : اذهب بهذا الثوب إن رضيته اشتريته، فذهب به فهلك، لا يضمن، ولو قال : إن رضيته اشتريته بعشرة ، فذهب به فهلك ضمن قيمته، وعليه الفتوى. كذا في «الكفاية».
قوله : ويخرج ... الخ ; لأنَّ البيع من جهة بائعه لازم ; لأنَّ الخيارَ شُرعَ نظراً لمن هو له، فيعمل في حقه دون الآخر.
قوله : بالثمن ; لأن المبيع إذا قرب من الهلاك يكون معيباً، وبالتعيب استحكم العقد، ولا يمكن الردّ ، ولزم الثَّمن لهلاكه على ملكه.
قوله : كتعيبه ; كما إذا دخلَهُ عيب لا يرتفع كقطع اليد، وإن كان يرتفع كالمرض فهو على خياره ، فإن ارتفع في المدّة لا يلزم، وإلا يلزم، وعن الشافعي أيضاً : يلزم البيع بالتعيب. ذكره العَيْني في «شرح الكنز».
Chapter of Sales, Section on Option - Option of Stipulation. If the buyer takes possession and it perishes, he is liable for the value, and it leaves the seller's ownership with the buyer's option, so its destruction in his hand is [treated] by the price like its defect. If the buyer takes possession and it perishes, he is liable for the value: meaning a sale with a condition of option for the seller, then he takes possession and it perishes in his hand, he is liable for the value, because it is possessed on the basis of purchase (sawm al-shira'), and it is guaranteed by the value. (And it leaves the seller's ownership with the buyer's option, so its destruction in his hand is by the price like its defect.) His saying: 'perishes in his hand' means during the option period, for if it perishes after that, the price is obligatory, not the value, because the option is void. His saying: 'he is liable for the value'; Ibn Abi Layla said: nothing is upon him, because he is an amin since he took possession with the owner's permission. But we say: the seller did not consent to his possession except by virtue of the contract, and what is possessed by virtue of the contract is guaranteed by the value, like what is possessed on the basis of purchase (sawm al-shira'). Thus in al-Kifaya. His saying: 'because it is possessed on the basis of purchase'; its summary: since the sale is suspended due to the existence of the option, it is annulled by the destruction of the sold item, and the object of contract having perished, it becomes such that initiating a contract upon it is not permissible, so the ratification does not attach to it, so the sold item remains possessed in his hand on the basis of purchase. His saying: 'and it is guaranteed by the value'; if it is not a fungible (mithli), but if it is a fungible, then he is liable for the like. Then, what is possessed on the basis of purchase is only guaranteed if the price is specified; so if he says: 'Take this garment, if you like it, buy it,' and he takes it and it perishes, he is not liable; but if he says: 'If you like it, buy it for ten,' and he takes it and it perishes, he is liable for its value, and the fatwa is upon this. Thus in al-Kifaya. His saying: 'and it leaves...' because the sale from the seller's side is binding, because the option is legislated for the benefit of the one for whom it is, so it operates in his favor and not against the other. His saying: 'by the price' because when the sold item is on the verge of destruction, it becomes defective, and by the defect the contract becomes firm, and return is not possible, and the price is obligatory due to its destruction while in his ownership. His saying: 'like its defect' as when a defect that cannot be removed, like cutting off a hand, enters it; if it can be removed like illness, then it remains under his option; if it is removed within the period, it does not become obligatory, otherwise it becomes obligatory. Also from al-Shafi'i: the sale becomes binding by the defect. Mentioned by al-'Ayni in Sharh al-Kanz.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of a sale with an option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) for the seller. The main point is that if the buyer takes possession of the item during the option period and it is destroyed, the buyer is liable to pay the value (qimah) of the item, not the contracted price (thaman). The reasoning is that because the sale is suspended (mawquf) due to the option, the destruction of the item cancels the sale, and the item is considered to be in the buyer's possession on the basis of purchase (sawm al-shira'), similar to taking an item on approval with a specified price. This is distinguished from the case where the option is for the buyer, which will be discussed later. The commentary also notes that if the item is fungible (mithli), the buyer must return the like (mithl). An important condition is that the price must be specified for liability to apply. If a person says 'Take this garment, if you like it, buy it' without specifying a price, there is no liability. But if the price is specified, liability arises. The commentator also addresses an objection by Ibn Abi Layla, who argued that the buyer is an amin (trustee) and thus not liable. The Hanafi response is that the buyer took possession by virtue of the contract, and possessions by virtue of a contract are guaranteed. Additionally, if the item becomes defective (ta'ayyab) instead of being destroyed, the same ruling applies: the contract becomes binding and the price is due, similar to the ruling on destruction.

Key Terms
مثلي (mithli): A fungible item that has standard equivalents in the market, such as grains or currencies.
قيمي (qimi): A non-fungible item that has no standard equivalent, such as a unique painting.
تعيب (ta'ayyub): The occurrence of a defect in the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer takes possession of a fungible item during an option sale and it is destroyed, what compensation is due?
A) The market value
B) The like (similar item)
C) The contracted price
D) No compensation because it is fungible

Key Takeaway
Liability for destruction during option depends on a specified price; fungibles require return of the like, and permanent defects trigger the same liability as destruction.

Ownership of the Purchased Item During the Option Period: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on ownership during khiyar al-shart and explain the thamarah al-khilaf using the example of buying one's wife.

Core Idea
In khiyar al-shart, Abu Hanifa holds the buyer does not own the item; the Sahibayn hold he does — the difference affects marriage validity.

When you buy something with an option to cancel, do you own it immediately or only after the option expires? This seemingly technical question has a real consequence: if a man buys his wife with an option, does his marriage dissolve? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement, with Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students taking opposite views. Let us examine their proofs and see why it matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
The core question: Does the buyer acquire ownership of the purchased item during the option period (khiyar al-shart) when the option is for the buyer?
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer does not own it. His proof: the price (thaman) is still with the buyer; if the item entered his ownership, it would be without exchange, which is unknown in sharia. Additionally, property can leave one's ownership without entering another's, as seen in the three examples (Kaaba servant, debt-ridden estate, waqf).
The three examples are crucial to rebut the opposing claim.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the buyer owns the item. Their proof: if the buyer did not own it, the item would be ownerless (outside seller's ownership, not in buyer's), which is unprecedented in sharia.
This is a simple qiyas: normally property must have an owner.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa counters that the Sahibayn's claim of no precedent is false; he provides three clear cases where property exits ownership without entering another's. Thus, the buyer not owning is not legally impossible.
These cases are analogies (shabah) that demonstrate permissibility.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference is seen in the example of a man buying his wife with an option. According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage remains valid (he doesn't own her); according to the Sahibayn, the marriage is invalidated (he owns her). This shows the real-world impact of the abstract dispute.
In fatwa practice, Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon, so the marriage is not affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا يملكه المشتري ; عند أبي حنيفة له ، وقالا : يملكه، وهو قولُ مالك وأحمد وقول الشافعي ; لأنه لو لم يملكه لكان خارجا عن ملك البائع لا إلى مالك، ولم يُعرف هذا في الشرع. ولأبي حنيفة له : إنَّ الثمن لم يخرج عن ملك المشتري ; لأن الخيار يعمل في حق من هو له ، فلو دخل المبيع في ملكه دخل بلا عوض، واجتمع في ملكه الــعوض ومعوّضه، ولم يُعرف هذا في الشرع، وقد عُرف الخروج عن ملك شخص لا إلى مالك في مسائل :
منها : إذا اشترى متولي أمر الكعبة عبداً لخدمتها ; فإنه يخرج عن ملك مالكه ، ولا يدخل في ملك أحد. ومنها : مال التركةِ إذا استغرقه الدين، فإنّه يخرج عن ملك الميت، ولا يدخل في ملك الورثة ولا الغرماء. ومنها : الوقف. كذا في «كمال الدراية» وغيرها.
قوله : وثمرة الخلاف ; بين الإمام وصاحبه من أنَّ الخيار إذا كان للمشتري يخرج المبيعُ عن ملك البائع ولا يدخل في ملك المشتري عنده ، ويدخل عندهما.
قوله : فشراء زوجته بالخيار لا يفسد نكاحه عند الإمام ; لأنه لا يملكها باعتبار الخيار وعندهما: يفسد ; لأنه يملكها.
His saying: 'and the buyer does not own it'; according to Abu Hanifa he does not own it, and the two (companions) said: he owns it, and it is the saying of Malik, Ahmad, and the saying of al-Shafi'i; because if he did not own it, it would be out of the seller's ownership without going to any owner, and this is not known in the Shariah. And for Abu Hanifa: because the price did not leave the buyer's ownership, because the option operates in favor of the one for whom it is, so if the purchased item entered his ownership, it would enter without exchange, and the exchange and the exchanged would be combined in his ownership, and this is not known in the Shariah. And the exit from a person's ownership without going to any owner is known in cases: [1] If the custodian of the Kaaba buys a slave for its service, it leaves the owner's ownership and does not enter into anyone's ownership. [2] The wealth of the estate if it is overwhelmed by debt, it leaves the ownership of the deceased and does not enter into the ownership of the heirs or the creditors. [3] Waqf. Thus in Kamal al-Diraya and others. His saying: 'and the fruit of the dispute' between the Imam and his two companions is that when the option is for the buyer, according to him the purchased item leaves the seller's ownership and does not enter the buyer's ownership, while according to them it enters. His saying: 'so buying his wife with an option does not invalidate his marriage according to the Imam' because he does not own her due to the option; according to them it is invalidated because he owns her.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding ownership of the purchased item during the option period when the option is for the buyer. According to Abu Hanifa, the buyer does not take ownership of the item during the option period. His reasoning is that the price (thaman) never left the buyer's ownership, so if the purchased item were to enter his ownership, it would be without an exchange (because the price is still with him). This would result in the buyer owning both the price and the item, which is not a recognized situation in Islamic law. Furthermore, Abu Hanifa argues that it is possible for property to leave a person's ownership without entering another's ownership, citing three cases: (1) a slave purchased for the service of the Kaaba, (2) an estate that is fully burdened with debt, and (3) an endowment (waqf). In all these cases, the property exits the ownership of the original owner without transferring to any new owner. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), along with Imam Malik, Ahmad, and al-Shafi'i, hold that the buyer does own the item during the option period. Their argument is that if the buyer did not own it, the item would be out of the seller's ownership without any owner, which they claim is unprecedented in Islamic law. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this dispute is illustrated by the example of a man buying his wife with an option. According to Abu Hanifa, because he does not own her during the option period, the marriage remains valid (since a man cannot marry someone he owns, but here he does not own her). According to the two companions, he does own her, so the marriage is invalidated (because he cannot be married to his own slave).

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): An option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period.
ملك (milk): Ownership; the legal right of possession and disposition.
عرس (urs): Wife; a woman married to a man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a marriage if a man buys his wife with an option (khiyar al-shart)?
A) The marriage is invalidated because he owns her immediately
B) The marriage remains valid because he does not own her during the option period
C) The marriage becomes suspended until the option expires
D) The marriage is automatically dissolved by the purchase

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that the buyer does not own the item during the option period, which affects risk and incidental rulings such as marriage dissolution.

8 min
Ownership During Khiyar al-Shart: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on buyer's ownership during khiyar al-shart with enumerated consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer does not own during khiyar al-shart, contrast the Sahibayn's view, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to five concrete scenarios.

Core Idea
During khiyar al-shart, the buyer does not own the item — a suspension that prevents combining consideration and object without exchange.

This lesson examines a foundational intra-Hanafi dispute: does ownership transfer to the buyer during khiyar al-shart when the option is for the buyer? Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), took opposite positions. This disagreement is not merely theoretical; it yields five distinct practical consequences affecting marriage validity, the right to return after intercourse, the freeing of relatives, conditional emancipation, and the waiting period (istibra') for slave-girls. By understanding the proofs and consequences, you will see how a single principle branches into multiple rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the core dispute
Identify the exact point of disagreement: does the buyer own the purchased item during khiyar al-shart when the option belongs to the buyer? Abu Hanifa says no; the Sahibayn say yes.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine the reasoning: the price remains in the buyer's ownership; if the item entered his ownership, it would be without exchange, and combining both is unknown in Sharia; and there are precedents where property leaves an owner without entering another's (Ka'bah slave, debt-ridden estate, waqf).
These examples demonstrate that ownerless property is recognized in certain limited contexts.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Their argument: if the buyer does not own it, the item becomes ownerless, which is not recognized in Sharia.
This reflects a different epistemological commitment: property must always have an owner.
4
List the five consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
For each of the five issues (marriage, intercourse, relative's emancipation, conditional emancipation, istibra'), note the practical difference: what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and what according to the Sahibayn?
Focus on understanding how the ownership question drives each outcome.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view (no ownership), though later jurists sometimes adopted the Sahibayn's view for ease in specific cases.
The tarjih authority is al-Marghinani (al-Hidayah) and the majority of early Hanafi masters.

ولا يملكه المشتري، فشراء عرسه بالخيار لا يفسد نكاحه أي إذا كان الخيار للمُشتَرِي وقبضهُ المشتري فهَلَكَ أو تَعَيَّبَ فِي يَدِهِ يَحِبُ الثَّمَنُ، (ولا يملكه المشتري ) : أي إذا كان الخيار للمُشتَرِي لَا يَمْلِكُهُ الْمُشْتَرِي عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما، وثمرة الخلاف" تظهر في هذه المسائل، وهي قوله : (فشراء عرسه (۱) بالخيار لا يفسد نكاحه) كالمرض فهو على خياره ، فإن ارتفع في المدّة لا يلزم، وإلا يلزم، وعن الشافعي أيضاً : يلزم البيع بالتعيب. ذكره العَيْني الله في ((شرح الكنز (۲) [١] قوله : ولا يملكه المشتري ؛ عند أبي حنيفة له ، وقالا : يملكه، وهو قولُ مالك وأحمد وقول الشافعي ؛ لأنه لو لم يملكه لكان خارجا عن ملك البائع لا إلى مالك، ولم يُعرف هذا في الشرع. ولأبي حنيفة له : إنَّ الثمن لم يخرج عن ملك المشتري ؛ لأن الخيار يعمل في حق من هو له ، فلو دخل المبيع في ملكه دخل بلا عوض، واجتمع في ملكه الـعــوض ومعوّضه، ولم يُعرف هذا في الشرع، وقد عُرف الخروج عن ملك شخص لا إلى مالك في مسائل : .۱ منها : إذا اشترى متولي أمر الكعبة عبداً لخدمتها ؛ فإنه يخرج عن ملك مالكه ، ولا يدخل في ملك أحد. ٢. ومنها : مال التركةِ إذا استغرقه الدين، فإنّه يخرج عن ملك الميت، ولا يدخل في ملك الورثة ولا الغرماء. . ومنها : الوقف. كذا في «كمال الدراية»(۳)، وغيرها. [٢] قوله : وثمرة الخلاف ؛ بين الإمام وصاحبه الله من أنَّ الخيار إذا كان للمشتري يخرج المبيعُ عن ملك البائع ولا يدخل في ملك المشتري عنده ، ويدخل عندهما. [۳] قوله : فشراء.. إلى آخره ؛ أي لو اشترى زوجته بالخيار لا يفسد نكاحه عند الإمام له ؛ لأنه لا يملكها باعتبار الخيار وعندهما: يفسد ؛ لأنه يملكها. وإن وَطِئَهَا رَدَّها ؛ لأَنَّهُ بالنِّكَاح إلا في البكْرِ، ولا يُعتق قريبه عليه في مدة خياره ، ولا من شراء قائلاً : إن ملكت عبداً فهو حرّ، ولا يعد حيضُ المشرية في المدة من استبرائها عند أبي حنيفة لعدم الملك وعندهما يُفْسِدُه ، وإن وَطِنَها رَدَّها ؛ لأنَّهُ بالنكاح إلا في البكْرِ : أَي إِن وَطِئَها المُشتَرِي في أَيَّام الخيارِ يَمْلِكُ رَدَّها عند أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنَّ الوَط بالنكاح فلا تكون إجازة إلا أن تكون بكراً ؛ لأَنَّهُ نَقَصَهَا بالوطء فلا يَمْلِكُ الرَّد، وعندهما لا يملكُ الرَّدُ وإن كانت ثيباً ؛ لأنَّ المُشْتَرِي قد مَلَكَها ففسد النكاح ، فالوطء يكون بملك اليمين فيكون إجازة متصلة. ( ولا يُعتق قريبه عليه في مدَّةٍ خياره) : أي إن اشترى قريبه بالخيار لا يُعْتَقُ عند أبي حنيفة له في أيام الخيار خلافاً لهما". ولا من شراء قائلاً : إن ملكت عبداً فهو حر ) : أي إن قال : إن ملكتُ عبداً فهو حر ، فشراهُ بالخيار لا يعتق في أيام الخيارِ عند أبي حنيفة لعدم الملك (ولا يعد حيضُ المشرية في المدة من استبرائها) عند أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لها فإنه يعتق عندهما لوجود الملك.
And the buyer does not own it. So the purchase of his wife with an option does not invalidate his marriage, i.e., if the option belongs to the buyer and the buyer takes possession and it is destroyed or becomes defective in his hand, the price is obligatory. (And the buyer does not own it): i.e., if the option belongs to the buyer, the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two. The fruit of the dispute appears in these issues, which is his statement: (So the purchase of his wife with an option does not invalidate his marriage). Like illness, he retains his option; if it is lifted within the period, it does not become binding, otherwise it does. And from al-Shafi'i: the sale becomes binding by defect. Al-Ayni mentioned it in Sharh al-Kanz. [1] His statement: And the buyer does not own it: according to Abu Hanifa, no; the two said he owns it, and it is the saying of Malik, Ahmad, and al-Shafi'i; because if he did not own it, it would be out of the seller's ownership without going to an owner, and this is not known in the Sharia. And for Abu Hanifa: the price has not left the buyer's ownership because the option operates in favor of the one who has it, so if the sold item entered his ownership, it would enter without consideration, and consideration and what is considered would combine in his ownership, and this is not known in the Sharia. And it is known that something leaves a person's ownership without going to an owner in certain cases: 1. When the custodian of the Ka'bah buys a slave for its service; it leaves the owner's ownership and does not enter into anyone's ownership. 2. The estate's wealth when it is consumed by debt; it leaves the ownership of the deceased and does not enter into the ownership of the heirs or the creditors. 3. Waqf. Thus in Kamal al-Dirayah and others. [2] His statement: And the fruit of the dispute: between the Imam and his companions is that when the option belongs to the buyer, the sold item leaves the seller's ownership and does not enter the buyer's ownership according to him, but enters according to them. [3] His statement: So the purchase... etc.: i.e., if he buys his wife with an option, it does not invalidate his marriage according to the Imam, because he does not own her due to the option; according to them, it does invalidate because he owns her. And if he has intercourse with her, he returns her, because it is by marriage except in the case of a virgin. And he does not free his relative during his option period, nor from a purchase saying: 'If I own a slave, he is free,' and the menstruation of the purchased slave-girl is not counted in the period for her istibra' according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of ownership, and according to them, it invalidates it. And if he has intercourse with her, he returns her, because it is by marriage except in the case of a virgin: i.e., if the buyer has intercourse with her during the option days, he has the right to return her according to Abu Hanifa, because intercourse is by marriage so it is not acceptance, unless she is a virgin, because he has diminished her by intercourse so he does not have the right to return; according to them, he does not have the right to return even if she is not a virgin, because the buyer has owned her, so the marriage is void, and intercourse becomes by right of ownership, so it is a connected acceptance. (And he does not free his relative during his option period): i.e., if he buys his relative with an option, he is not freed during the option days according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two. (Nor from a purchase saying: 'If I own a slave, he is free'): i.e., if he says: 'If I own a slave, he is free,' then he buys him with an option, he is not freed during the option days according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of ownership. (And the menstruation of the purchased slave-girl is not counted in the period for her istibra') according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them, because according to them he is freed due to existence of ownership.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of ownership during khiyar al-shart (the option of stipulation) when the option belongs to the buyer. The core disagreement is between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer does not become owner of the purchased item during the option period. The Sahibayn hold that he does become owner. The passage then enumerates the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) of this difference. The author first clarifies that when the option belongs to the buyer and he takes possession, if the item perishes or becomes defective in his hand, he is liable for the price. This is agreed. The dispute is about whether the buyer owns it. Abu Hanifa's proof: The price remains in the buyer's ownership because the option operates for the one who has it (the buyer). If the sold item entered his ownership, it would enter without exchange (since the price is not yet fully transferred), resulting in combining consideration and the thing considered in his ownership, which is unknown in Sharia. Moreover, it is known that property can leave a person's ownership without entering another's, such as: (1) the Ka'bah's custodian buying a slave for service, (2) estate wealth consumed by debt, and (3) waqf. Thus the sold item leaves the seller's ownership during the option period but does not enter the buyer's. The Sahibayn argue that if the buyer did not own it, the item would be ownerless, which is not recognized in Sharia unless by explicit textual proof. They support their view with analogies from other schools. The first consequence is the purchase of one's own wife with an option. According to Abu Hanifa, since the husband does not own her during the option, the marriage remains valid. According to the Sahibayn, the husband owns her, so the marriage is dissolved (because a man cannot own his wife as a slave). Second, if the buyer has intercourse with a purchased female slave during the option period, Abu Hanifa says he still has the right to return her (reject the sale) because the intercourse was by virtue of marriage (if she was his wife?) Actually the text says 'except in the case of a virgin' – the nuance: if the buyer has intercourse with a purchased female (thayyib, non-virgin) during the option period, he may still return her according to Abu Hanifa because the intercourse was by way of marriage (i.e., he is still married to her? Wait: the example here seems to be about a wife purchased? Actually it's a different scenario: the buyer who has the option has intercourse with the purchased female slave. The text says 'except in the case of a virgin' because deflowering her diminishes her value, so he loses the right to return. According to the Sahibayn, the buyer owns her, so the intercourse is by right of ownership and constitutes acceptance of the sale, so he cannot return her. Third, if the buyer buys a relative who would be freed upon ownership (e.g., father, son), according to Abu Hanifa the relative is not freed during the option period because the buyer does not own him. The Sahibayn say he is freed because ownership is established. Fourth, if the buyer made a conditional statement: 'If I own a slave, he is free,' and then buys a slave with an option, the slave is not freed during the option according to Abu Hanifa, because the condition (ownership) is not fulfilled. The Sahibayn hold that the condition is fulfilled, so the slave is freed. Fifth, the waiting period (istibra') of a purchased slave-girl: her menstruation during the option period does not count toward istibra' according to Abu Hanifa because she is not owned by the buyer; the Sahibayn say it does count because she is owned. This passage demonstrates how a single juristic principle (ownership during khiyar) branches into multiple practical rulings. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, as it is the position of the majority of early Hanafi masters, though later jurists sometimes preferred the Sahibayn's view in certain contexts.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option granted by stipulation in a sale contract, allowing either party to cancel the sale within a specified period.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence or fruit of a juristic disagreement, showing how the difference in principle affects actual rulings.
استبراء (istibra'): A waiting period observed for a purchased female slave to ensure she is not pregnant from the previous owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The marriage is invalidated because he owns her.
B) The marriage remains valid because he does not own her during the option.
C) The marriage is suspended until the option period ends.
D) The marriage becomes a temporary marriage.

Key Takeaway
The buyer's ownership during khiyar al-shart is suspended according to Abu Hanifa, with five distinct practical consequences that distinguish his view from the Sahibayn.

Intercourse During the Option Period: Does It Forfeit the Right to Return?
Explains the effect of buyer's intercourse during khiyar al-shart on the right to return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of the buyer's intercourse during khiyar al-shart on the right to return a purchased slave, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Intercourse during the option period: is it acceptance by ownership or like marriage? The answer determines the right to return.

When a buyer has intercourse with a purchased slave during the stipulated option period (khiyar al-shart), does this act forfeit the right to return the slave? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between virgin and non-virgin, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that any intercourse constitutes acceptance and bars return. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and legal question
The act is the buyer's sexual intercourse (wat') with the purchased slave during the khiyar al-shart period. The legal question is: does this act constitute acceptance (ijazah) of the sale, thereby forfeiting the right to return the slave?
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Hanifa, if the slave is non-virgin (thayyib), the buyer may still return her. The intercourse is like marriage (nikah), not an act of ownership, so it is not acceptance. However, if the slave is a virgin (bikr), the intercourse diminishes her value, so the buyer forfeits the right to return.
The diminishment (nuqs) for a virgin is a key exception.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani)
According to the Sahibayn, once the buyer has intercourse, he loses the right to return the slave whether she is virgin or non-virgin. Their reasoning: the buyer already owns the slave at the time of intercourse (ownership is established immediately upon purchase), so the intercourse is by right of ownership and constitutes an implicit acceptance of the sale.
They view ownership as effective during the option period.
4
Compare the dalils (proofs)
Abu Hanifa analogizes intercourse to marriage (nikah), which does not imply acceptance in a sale context. The Sahibayn emphasize that ownership is established and intercourse is an act of ownership. The core dispute hinges on whether full ownership is considered transferred during the option period.
This is a qiyas-based argument on both sides.
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, a buyer who has intercourse with a non-virgin slave can still return her during the option period. Under the Sahibayn, he cannot return her at all. This affects the buyer's options if he changes his mind after intercourse.
Later Hanafi fatwa often follows the Sahibayn's stricter view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[1] قوله : وإن وطئها ؛ وهي ثيب، ولم ينقصها الوطء أما إذا نقصها، فليس له الرد وإن كانت ثيباً. ينظر : «الكفاية»).
[2] قوله : إلا أن تكون استثناء من قوله : «ردّها»: أي يملك ردّها إن كانت بكر ؛ لأنه... الخ.
And if he has intercourse with her, he returns her, because it is by marriage except in the case of a virgin. That is: if the buyer has intercourse with her during the days of the option, he has the right to return her according to Abu Hanifa, because intercourse is by marriage, so it is not acceptance unless she is a virgin, because he has diminished her by intercourse, so he does not have the right to return. According to them (the two companions), he does not have the right to return even if she is non-virgin, because the buyer has owned her, so the marriage is invalidated, and the intercourse is by right of ownership, so it is a connected acceptance.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of the buyer's intercourse with a purchased slave during the khiyar al-shart (option of condition) period. The main text states that if the buyer has intercourse, he can still return her, with an exception for a virgin. The commentary explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the buyer retains the right to return a non-virgin slave after intercourse because the intercourse is considered akin to permissible sexual relations through a valid marriage (nikah), not as an expression of acceptance of the sale. However, if the slave is a virgin, the act of intercourse diminishes her value, so the buyer forfeits the right to return. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold the opposite view: once the buyer has intercourse, he has no right to return even a non-virgin because, in their view, the buyer has already taken full ownership (the option period does not prevent ownership), and the marriage is dissolved; the intercourse is thus by right of ownership and constitutes an implicit acceptance of the sale. The footnote clarifies that the ruling applies when the intercourse does not cause a defect; if it does cause a defect, return is not allowed even by Abu Hanifa for a non-virgin.

Key Terms
وطء (wat'): Sexual intercourse. In this context, the act of the buyer with the purchased slave during the option period.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation; a period during which the buyer or seller can rescind the sale by mutual agreement.
إجازة (ijazah): Acceptance or ratification of the contract. In this context, whether intercourse constitutes acceptance.
ثيب (thayyib): A non-virgin (woman who has had sexual intercourse before).
بكر (bikr): A virgin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The intercourse must not cause a defect.
B) The buyer must not have consummated the marriage.
C) The option period must still be running.
D) The slave must be a virgin.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa distinguishes between virgin and non-virgin (and also considers defect), while the Sahibayn hold that any intercourse forfeits the right to return; later practice generally follows the Sahibayn.

Freeing Relatives and Conditional Freeing During the Option Period
Discusses whether purchase of a relative during khiyar al-shart triggers immediate 'itq, and whether conditional freeing applies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on automatic freeing of relatives and conditional freeing during khiyar al-shart, and identify the practical difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Ownership during khiyar is incomplete; thus freeing does not occur according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn differ.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explores whether purchasing a relative under an option contract triggers immediate emancipation, and whether a conditional freeing statement takes effect during the option period. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute clarifies the legal effect of option contracts on ownership and emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage addresses two distinct cases: (1) buying a relative under khiyar al-shart, and (2) a conditional freeing declaration followed by such a purchase. Recognize that both hinge on the nature of ownership during the option period.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that in neither case does the slave become free because ownership is not complete during the option period. The key is 'lack of complete ownership' (adam al-milk al-kamil).
This is based on qiyas: freeing requires full ownership, which is suspended during khiyar.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The two disciples argue that ownership is established at the moment of contract, so the condition or relationship triggers immediate emancipation. For them, the contract transfers ownership instantly, subject only to a right of rescission.
They consider ownership as immediate; the option only grants a right to cancel, not suspend ownership.
4
Note the exceptional case where all agree
If the buyer explicitly says 'I bought this slave and he is free' during the option, all agree the slave is freed. This is because it is an initiation of freedom (insha' al-'itq) after the condition, not a suspended decree.
This shows the difference between ta'liq (suspension) and insha' (direct creation).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa the slave remains owned; under the Sahibayn he is freed immediately. Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn's view for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on facilitating emancipation (tashil al-'itq) and the stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ولا يُعتق قريبه عليه في مدَّةٍ خياره) : أي إن اشترى قريبه بالخيار لا يُعْتَقُ عند أبي حنيفة له في أيام الخيار خلافاً لهما. و (لا من شراء قائلاً : إن ملكت عبداً فهو حر) : أي إن قال : إن ملكتُ عبداً فهو حر ، فشراهُ بالخيار لا يعتق في أيام الخيارِ عند أبي حنيفة لعدم الملك.
[3] قوله : خلافاً لهما ; أي عندهما يعتق; لأنه ملكه، ولفور الملك يعتق القريب.

(And his relative is not freed upon him during the period of his option): i.e., if he buys his relative with an option, he is not freed according to Abu Hanifa during the days of the option, contrary to the two. And (nor from a purchase [where he] says: If I own a slave, he is free): i.e., if he says: If I own a slave, he is free, then he buys [a slave] with an option, he is not freed during the days of the option according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of ownership. [Footnote: Contrary to the two; i.e., according to them he is freed, because he owns him, and due to the immediacy of ownership the relative is freed. [Footnote: Saying: If I own; unlike if he said: I bought a slave and he is free; because it becomes like initiating freedom after the condition, so the option falls and he is freed according to all of them, for what is suspended on a condition is like what is unreleased when the condition occurs. And if he initiated freedom after buying with option, he is freed and the option falls. So too this.]
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct but related issues concerning freeing slaves during the khiyar al-shart period. First, if a person buys a relative (such as a father, son, or brother) under an option contract, does the relative become free immediately? According to Abu Hanifa, the relative is not freed during the option days because complete ownership is not yet established; the option period delays full transfer of ownership. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that ownership is immediate, so the relative is freed at the moment of purchase. Second, if a person makes a conditional declaration: "If I ever own a slave, he is free," and then buys a slave with an option, does the slave become free? Again, Abu Hanifa says no, because ownership is not fully realized during the option period. The Sahibayn disagree. The footnotes clarify that the ruling differs if the buyer explicitly says, "I bought this slave and he is free"—in that case, all agree that the option ends and the slave is freed because it is considered an initiation of freedom after the condition. Also, if the buyer later chooses to free the slave after the purchase, the option is voided and the slave is freed by consensus.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave. Here it refers to automatic freeing by purchase of a relative or fulfillment of a condition.
قريب (qarib): A relative within the prohibited degrees (like father, son, brother) whose purchase causes automatic emancipation.
معلق بالشرط (mu'allaq bi al-shart): A conditional statement: 'If X happens, then Y is free.' The freeing is suspended on the condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, immediately.
B) No, because ownership is not complete.
C) Yes, but only after three days.
D) No, because conditional freeing is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar al-shart, complete ownership is not established until the option ends, so automatic freeing of relatives and conditional freeing do not occur according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn differ; the mufta bihi is often the Sahibayn's view.

Istibra' and Umm Walad During the Option Period
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar and istibra'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the counting of menstruation for istibra' during the option period and explain how the Sahibayn differ, identifying the underlying principle of incomplete ownership.

Core Idea
Incomplete ownership during the option period suspends istibra' and umm walad status according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya sharh al-Wiqaya addresses a crucial Hanafi dispute about the effect of an option period (khiyar al-shart) on the purchased slave's istibra' and potential umm walad status. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on whether the menstruation that occurs during the option counts towards the required istibra', whether the seller must perform istibra' upon return, and whether a birth during the option makes the slave an umm walad. The root of the disagreement is whether ownership is fully transferred during the option. Let's examine the positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three legal issues
The passage addresses three connected issues: (1) Does the purchased slave's menstruation during the option count for istibra'? (2) Must the seller perform istibra' if the slave is returned? (3) Does a birth during the option period make the slave umm walad?
Each issue turns on the same principle: ownership transfer.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position on each issue
Abu Hanifa says: no to all three. The menstruation does not count, the seller needs no istibra', and the slave does not become umm walad until delivery after ownership is final.
3
State the Sahibayn's position on each issue
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold the opposite: the menstruation does count and even invalidates the option, the seller must perform istibra', and the slave becomes umm walad upon birth.
4
Identify the legal principle underlying the disagreement
Abu Hanifa views ownership during the option as incomplete, so the transitory period does not trigger istibra' or umm walad. The Sahibayn view ownership as immediate, so all consequences follow from the contract.
This is a dispute over the nature of khiyar al-shart: suspensive condition vs. immediate transfer.
5
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the buyer must start istibra' after the option period ends; under Sahibayn, the menstruation during the option counts. Similarly for the seller and umm walad.
The difference affects the timing of istibra' and the slave's status.

Source Text

ولا يعد حيضُ المشرية في المدة من استبرائها عند أبي حنيفة لعدم الملك وعندهما يُفْسِدُه .

ولا استبراء على البائع إن رُدَّت عليه بالخيار) : أي إن رُدَّت الأمة المشريَّةُ بالخيار لا يجب الاستبراء على البائع عند أبي حنيفة له ; لأن الاستبراء إنما يجب بالانتقال من ملك إلى ملك ، ولم يوجد عند أبي حنيفة له حيث لا يملكها المشتري.
(ومن ولدت في المدَّة بالنكاح لا تصيرُ أُمَّ ولد له) : أي إذا اشترى الأمة التي كانت منكوحته، وولدت منه في أيام الخيار في يد البائع قبل قبض المشتري ، لا تصير أم ولد له عند الإمام الله خلافاً لهما، فأما إذا قبضها المشتري وولدت عنده في مدة الخيار يثبت له الملك، ويسقط الخيار وتصير أم ولد له بالاتفاق ; لأنها تعيبت بالولادة فلا يمكن ردُّها بعد العيب.
And the menstruation of the purchased [slave] during the period is not counted from her istibra' according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of ownership, and according to the two it invalidates it. [Footnote: According to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two, for it is freed according to them due to existence of ownership.] [Footnote: Istibra': linguistically, seeking freedom absolutely. In the terminology of jurists: seeking freedom of the womb. So whoever owns an female slave in full ownership, whether by purchase or otherwise, such as gift, inheritance, etc., it is forbidden for the owner to have intercourse with her and its preliminaries until he performs istibra' with one menstruation for those who menstruate, and one month for the menopausal and those with interrupted menstruation, for the month stands in place of menstruation in 'idda, and similarly in istibra'. For those with prolonged purity, three months according to the two shaykhs, and four months and ten days according to Muhammad. For the pregnant, by her delivery. (And whoever gives birth during the period by marriage does not become umm walad for him): i.e., if he buys a slave who was his wife, and she gives birth from him during the option days while in the possession of the seller before the buyer takes delivery, she does not become umm walad for him according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], contrary to the two. But if he takes delivery and she gives birth with him during the option period, ownership is established, the option falls, and she becomes umm walad for him by consensus, because she is defective by childbirth and cannot be returned after the defect.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage covers three related rulings concerning the option period (khiyar al-shart). First, the menstruation of a purchased female slave during the option period: according to Abu Hanifa, this menstruation does not count towards the required istibra' (waiting period to ensure the womb is empty) because full ownership has not been established. The Sahibayn hold that since ownership is established, the menstruation does count and even invalidates the option if the seller had stipulated istibra'. The commentary then provides a detailed definition of istibra', including its duration and wisdom. Second, if the slave is returned to the seller during the option, the seller is not required to perform istibra' according to Abu Hanifa, because in his view the ownership never transferred to the buyer; the seller's ownership persisted throughout. The Sahibayn would require istibra' because they consider the buyer's ownership to have been established. Third, if the purchased slave was previously the buyer's wife (via nikah) and she gives birth during the option period while still in the seller's possession, she does not become umm walad (mother of his child) according to Abu Hanifa, because the child is born from a valid marriage and the ownership of the mother is not yet fully established. However, if the buyer had taken delivery and she gives birth during the option period, by consensus she becomes umm walad because full ownership is established and the option ends due to the defect of childbirth.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): A waiting period required after acquiring a female slave to ensure her womb is not pregnant before intercourse.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child to her master; upon his death, she becomes free.
حيض (hayd): Menstruation; used here as a measure for istibra'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa's ruling that the purchased slave's menstruation during the option period does not count for istibra'?
A) Because the slave is not yet in the buyer's possession.
B) Because the buyer's ownership is not fully established during the option.
C) Because istibra' is only required once, not repeatedly.
D) Because the seller retains the risk of loss.

Key Takeaway
During khiyar al-shart, Abu Hanifa deems ownership incomplete, so istibra' and umm walad consequences are suspended until the option concludes or delivery occurs.

Istibra' Not Required on Seller When Slave-Girl Returned During Option Period
Ruling on istibra' for seller and purchased slave-girl during option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istibra' when a slave-girl is returned during the option period and explain Abu Hanifa's proof based on ownership transfer.

Core Idea
Istibra' is only required after full transfer of ownership; during option, ownership is suspended.

This lesson examines a specific ruling within the chapter of khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). The source text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies that istibra' is not required from the seller when a purchased slave-girl is returned during the option period. Understanding this requires grasping the Hanafi position that istibra' hinges on the transfer of ownership, which does not fully occur during the option period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (istibra' when a slave-girl is returned during option) and what the ruling is (not required for the seller nor counted if she menstruates during option).
The ruling is a negation of obligation.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the reasoning provided: 'istibra' is only required after establishment of ownership' and 'istibra' is only required due to transfer from one ownership to another'.
This is a rational proof (qiyas/istihsan) based on the 'illa of ownership transfer.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the proof leads to the ruling: if ownership has not transferred (because the option suspends it), then the condition for istibra' is absent, so it is not required.
The 'illa is the transfer of ownership; its absence negates the obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that istibra' is required because ownership is established at the time of contract even with an option.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Recognize that the text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the mufta bihi (operative position).
The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية
ولا استبراء على البائع إن رُدَّت عليه بالخيار أي إن اشترى أمةً بالخيار فحاضت في أيام الخيار، فهذه الحيضة لا تُعَدُّ من الاستبراء عند أبي حنيفة الله؛ لأن الاستبراء إنَّما يَحِبُ بعد ثبوتِ الملك، (ولا استبراء على البائع إن رُدَّت عليه بالخيار) : أي إن رُدَّت الأمة المشريَّةُ بالخيار لا يجب الاستبراء على البائع عند أبي حنيفة له؛ لأن الاستبراء إنما يجب بالانتقال من ملك إلى ملك، ولم يوجد عند أبي حنيفة له حيث لا يملكها المشتري.
Epitome of the conclusion for the support of care. And no istibra' is required upon the seller if she is returned to him due to the option. Meaning: If he purchases a slave-girl with an option and she menstruates during the days of the option, this menstruation is not counted as part of istibra' according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because istibra' is only required after the establishment of ownership. (And no istibra' is required upon the seller if she is returned to him due to the option): That is, if the purchased slave-girl is returned due to the option, istibra' is not required upon the seller according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because istibra' is only required due to the transfer from one ownership to another, and that transfer did not occur according to Abu Hanifa since the buyer does not own her.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a ruling from the chapter on option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). It states that istibra' (seeking purity of the womb) is not required upon the seller when a slave-girl is returned to him during the option period, nor is it required for a purchased slave-girl who menstruates during the option period. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that istibra' is only obligatory after ownership is firmly established. During the option period, the buyer does not fully own the slave-girl; ownership is suspended. Therefore, any menstruation occurring in this period does not count towards the istibra' obligation. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that ownership is transferred immediately upon purchase, so istibra' would be required. The passage focuses on the Hanafi position and its rational proof based on the condition of ownership.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): Seeking purity of the womb to ensure no pregnancy from previous owner.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation in a sale contract.
ملك (milk): Ownership, a legal construct that may be suspended during khiyar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is istibra' not required from the seller when a slave-girl is returned during the option period?
A) Because the seller never owned her.
B) Because ownership did not transfer from seller to buyer, so no change of ownership occurred.
C) Because the buyer already performed istibra'.
D) Because the option period is too short.

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is contingent on ownership transfer; during the option period, ownership is suspended, so returning the slave-girl does not trigger istibra' for the seller.

Slave-Girl Married to Buyer Does Not Become Umm Walad During Option Period
Intra-Hanafi dispute on umm walad during option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) on whether a slave-girl purchased with khiyar al-shart becomes umm walad during the option period and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including the practical consequences.

Core Idea
A slave-girl only becomes umm walad if the buyer's ownership is fully established; option period suspends ownership.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, the commentator addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about a slave-girl who is the buyer's wife and gives birth during the option period. The ruling hinges on whether ownership is fully transferred at the time of contract or suspended until option expiry. This has significant practical consequences for the buyer's right to return the slave-girl and her free status upon the master's death.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Identify that according to Abu Hanifa, a slave-girl bought with khiyar al-shart who gives birth to his child while still in the seller's possession does NOT become umm walad.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the Opposing View (Sahibayn)
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold the opposite: she does become umm walad because ownership transfers immediately upon contract.
3
Analyze the Rationale Behind Each View
Examine the reasoning: Abu Hanifa considers ownership suspended during option; the Sahibayn consider it immediate. This leads to different conclusions about whether the condition of ownership for umm walad is met.
4
Consider the Istibra' Context
Note that the passage begins with a discussion of istibra' (seeking purity of womb). The wisdom is to safeguard lineages. This background informs the ruling on umm walad.
The buyer must perform istibra' before intercourse, but here the marriage predates the purchase, so istibra' may not apply.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Work out the practical difference: if she becomes umm walad, she cannot be returned and becomes free at master's death; if not, the buyer can return her and the child follows the father.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ولدت في المدة بالنكاح لا تصير أم ولد له وفي اصطلاح الفقهاء : طلب براءةِ الرَّحم ، فمن ملك أمةً رقبة ويداً سواء كان الملك بالشراء أو بغيره، كهبة، أو إرث، أو غيرهما ، فيحرم على المالك وطؤها ودواعيه حتى يستبرء بحيضة فيمن تحيض، وبشهرٍ في الآيسة والمنقطعة عن الحيض، فإنَّ الشَّهر قائم مقامَ الحيض في العدة، فكذا في الاستبراء أيضاً، وفي ممتدة الطهر بثلاثة أشهر عند الشيخين، وبأربعة أشهر وعشر عند محمد له، وفي الحامل بوضعها. والحكمة فيه : أن يتعرف براءة الرحم ؛ لحصول صيانة المياء المحترمة عن الاختلاط، والأنساب عن الاشتباه، وهذه الصيانة عند حقيقة الشغل كما في الحبالى، أو توهم الشغل بماء محترم ، وهو أن يكون الولد ثابت النسب. وحاصل الصورة: أنه إذا اشترى الأمة التي كانت منكوحته، وولدت منه في أيام الخيار في يد البائع قبل قبض المشتري، لا تصير أم ولد له عند الإمام الله خلافاً لهما، فأما إذا قبضها المشتري وولدت عنده في مدة الخيار يثبت له الملك، ويسقط الخيار وتصير أم ولد له بالاتفاق؛ لأنها تعيبت بالولادة فلا يمكن ردُّها بعد العيب.
And whoever gives birth during the period due to marriage does not become umm walad for him. And in the terminology of the jurists: istibra' is seeking purity of the womb. So whoever owns a slave-girl completely (ownership of the body and possession), whether the ownership is by purchase or otherwise, such as gift, inheritance, or others, it is unlawful for the owner to have intercourse with her or what leads to it until he performs istibra' with one menstruation for those who menstruate, and with one month for the menopausal and those whose menstruation has stopped, because the month stands in place of menstruation in the waiting period, and similarly in istibra'. And for one with extended purity, it is three months according to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and four months and ten days according to Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan) for her, and for a pregnant woman, it is until she gives birth. The wisdom in this is to ascertain the purity of the womb, to safeguard sacred fluids from mixing and lineages from confusion. This safeguarding is required when there is actual occupancy of the womb, as in pregnancy, or potential occupancy by a sacred fluid, which is when the child's lineage is established. And the summary of the scenario: When he purchases a slave-girl who was his wife, and she gives birth to his child during the days of the option while in the seller's possession before the buyer takes delivery, she does not become umm walad for him according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), may Allah have mercy on him, contrary to the two (Sahibayn). But if the buyer takes delivery and she gives birth in his possession during the option period, ownership is established for him, the option lapses, and she becomes umm walad for him by agreement, because she has become defective due to childbirth, so she cannot be returned after the defect.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a ruling about a slave-girl who is married to the buyer and gives birth during the option period. It opens with a general discussion on istibra', defining it as seeking purity of the womb. It outlines the istibra' obligations depending on the woman's state: one menstruation for those who menstruate, one month for menopausal women, three months or four months and ten days for women with extended purity (a difference between the two shaykhs and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and for pregnant women, until delivery. The wisdom is to ensure no mixing of lineages. The specific ruling is: if a man buys his own slave-wife, and she gives birth during the option period while she is still in the seller's possession, she does not become umm walad for the buyer according to Abu Hanifa. The two disciples hold that she does become umm walad because they consider ownership to have transferred upon purchase. However, if the buyer takes possession and then she gives birth during the option period, all agree that she becomes umm walad and the option is void because she is now defective and cannot be returned.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who bears a child to her master, becoming free upon his death.
خيار (khiyar): Option, the right to rescind a contract within a stipulated period.
براءة الرحم (bara'at al-rahim): Purity of the womb, established through istibra' to avoid mixing lineages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because she gave birth to his child.
B) No, because ownership is not fully transferred during the option period.
C) Yes, because the contract is valid and she is his wife.
D) No, because the child is not his.

Key Takeaway
A slave-girl only becomes umm walad if the buyer's ownership is complete at the time of birth; during khiyar al-shart, ownership is suspended, so she does not become umm walad according to the mufta bihi view.

Liability When Buyer Redeposits Goods with Seller
Ruling on liability after buyer deposits goods back with seller

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a buyer redeposits goods with the seller after taking delivery and identify the conditions that revive the seller's liability.

Core Idea
Possession after redeposit shifts liability back to the seller.

In a standard sale, once the buyer takes delivery (qabd), liability for loss transfers to the buyer. But what happens if the buyer immediately deposits the goods back with the seller for safekeeping? This brief ruling from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies that the seller once again bears the risk of destruction, because the goods are now in his trust (amana). Understanding this nuance prevents confusion about liability in transactions where physical possession is temporary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the scenario described? A buyer takes possession of a purchased item with the seller's permission, then deposits it back with the seller. The item is destroyed. The ruling: the seller bears the loss.
2
Recognize the key condition
The critical factor is that the buyer first took delivery (qabd) – without that, the seller would already be liable. The condition of 'deposit back' (ida') after qabd is what reimposes liability on the seller.
If the buyer never took delivery, the seller remains liable irrespective of deposit.
3
Understand the legal basis
In Hanafi fiqh, possession (yad) creates a presumption of liability. When the buyer takes delivery, liability transfers to him. But when he returns the goods as a deposit (amana), the seller's possession is now a trust (amanah), and the seller becomes liable for destruction without negligence? Actually, the text says 'upon him' – meaning he bears the loss, regardless of negligence? The ruling is absolute: the seller is liable.
This is a special rule; normally an amana holder is not liable for destruction without negligence, but here the seller's liability is strict.
4
Compare with the default rule
Without the deposit, if goods are destroyed after delivery but before the buyer takes physical possession? Actually, if the buyer has taken delivery, he is liable. The deposit resets the situation, making the seller liable again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهلكه في يد البائع عليه إن قبضه المشتري بإذنه وأودعه عنده
And its destruction while in the hand of the seller is upon him if the buyer took possession with his permission and deposited it with him.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This brief ruling from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya states that if the buyer takes delivery of the purchased item with the seller's permission, and then deposits it back with the seller (i.e., leaves it in his custody), and the item is destroyed, the seller bears the loss. This is because the item is now in the seller's possession as a deposit (amana), and the seller is liable for its destruction if it occurs without the buyer's fault. The ruling is part of the chapter on options, specifically regarding khiyar al-shart, where the buyer may return the item if he does not exercise the option.

Key Terms
هلكه (halakah): Destruction or perishing of the object.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession or delivery of the purchased item.
إيداع (ida'): Deposit, entrusting property to another for safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer takes delivery of a purchased item with the seller's permission and then deposits it back with the seller, and the item is destroyed, who bears the loss?
A) The buyer, because he took delivery.
B) The seller, because the item is in his possession again.
C) Both equally.
D) The buyer, because he could have taken it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if a buyer takes delivery (qabd) of a purchased item and then deposits it (ida') back with the seller, the seller assumes liability for any subsequent loss or destruction.

Khiyar al-Shart: Slave Woman Giving Birth and Item Perishing with Seller
Ruling on khiyar al-shart with slave woman's delivery and item lost with seller

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a slave woman giving birth during khiyar al-shart and explain the ruling on liability when an item perishes after being deposited with the seller.

Core Idea
During khiyar al-shart, birth before possession: Abu Hanifa allows return; Sahibayn deny it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two scenarios under khiyar al-shart that test the boundary between incomplete ownership and physical possession. The first deals with a purchased slave woman who gives birth during the option period while still in the seller's hands. The second considers the buyer's liability when the item perishes after being deposited back with the seller. Both cases reveal a fundamental intra-Hanafi divergence on the nature of ownership during the option period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage presents two issues: (1) a slave woman giving birth during khiyar al-shart before buyer takes possession; (2) the item perishing while deposited with the seller after buyer took possession and returned it for safekeeping.
Both hinge on the nature of ownership during the option period.
2
Analyze the first dispute: birth before possession
State Abu Hanifa's view (she does not become umm walad, return allowed) and the Sahibayn's view (she becomes umm walad, return not allowed). Identify the basis: possession vs. ownership period.
The key difference: Abu Hanifa focuses on physical possession; Sahibayn on the legal ownership attached to the option.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the buyer can return the slave woman and get a refund; under Sahibayn, the sale is final.
Later Hanafi fatwa favors the Sahibayn's view.
4
Apply to the second issue: perishing after deposit
If the buyer takes possession with permission, then deposits the item with the seller, and it perishes: Abu Hanifa sees the deposit as invalid (buyer not full owner), so loss on seller; Sahibayn see deposit valid, loss on buyer.
This mirrors the first dispute regarding ownership completeness.

Source Text

كتاب البيع باب الخيار - خيار الشرط -
وهُلْكُهُ في يد البائع عليه إن قبضهُ المُشتري بإذنِهِ وأودعه عنده أي إن اشترى زوجته بالخيار ، فوَلَدَتْ في أَيَّام الخيار في يد البائع لا تصير أم ولد للمشتري، فيملك الرّد عند أبي حنيفة له ، وعندهما تصير أم ولد له ؛ لأنها ولدت في ملك المشتَرِي ، فلا يملكُ الرَّدّ ، وإنّما قلنا : في يد البائع حتى لو قَبَضَ المشتَرِي ووَلَدَتْ في يَدِهِ تصيرُ أمَّ وَلَد له بالاتفاق ؛ لأنها تعيبت بالولادة، فلا يملك الرد فصارت ملكاً للمُشتَرِي، فالولادة وقعت في ملك المشتري لا في ملكه، فتصير أم ولد له. وهُلْكُهُ في يد البائع عليه إن قبضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِإِذْنِهِ وأودعَهُ عنده .
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option - Option of Stipulation -
And its destruction in the hand of the seller is upon him if the buyer took possession with his permission and deposited it with him. That is, if he buys a slave woman with an option, and she gives birth during the days of the option while in the hand of the seller, she does not become an umm walad for the buyer, so he has the right of return according to Abu Hanifa, but according to them (the two disciples) she becomes an umm walad for him because she gave birth in the buyer's ownership, so he does not have the right of return. And we only said: in the hand of the seller, because if the buyer took possession and she gives birth in his hand, she becomes an umm walad for him by agreement; because she became defective by childbirth, so he does not have the right of return, thus she becomes the property of the buyer. So the birth occurred in the ownership of the buyer, not in his ownership, so she becomes an umm walad for him. And its destruction in the hand of the seller is upon him if the buyer took possession with his permission and deposited it with him.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah's chapter on khiyar al-shart addresses two key issues: (1) the effect of a purchased slave woman giving birth during the option period, and (2) the liability if the buyer returns the item to the seller for safekeeping and it perishes. The author first explains that if a buyer purchases a slave woman with a stipulated option of three days (khiyar al-shart), and before the option expires, she gives birth while still in the seller's possession (i.e., the buyer has not taken possession), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the buyer may still return her because she does not become an umm walad (mother of his child) in his ownership. But according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), she becomes an umm walad because the birth occurred during the option period, which they consider part of the buyer's ownership. If the buyer had already taken possession and then she gives birth, all agree she becomes an umm walad because the birth occurred in his property, and she is defective by childbirth, so return is not possible. (2) If the buyer takes possession of the item with the seller's permission, then deposits it back with the seller for safekeeping, and it perishes, according to Abu Hanifa the loss is on the seller because the deposit is invalid due to the buyer not being the owner (since option is still active and return is possible). According to the disciples, the deposit is valid because the buyer owns the item, so the loss is on the buyer as if it perished in his own hand.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation: a clause in a contract allowing one or both parties to rescind the sale within a specified period (usually three days).
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who gives birth to her master's child; she becomes free upon his death and cannot be sold.
قبض (qabd): Possession; taking physical control of the purchased item, which transfers liability to the buyer.
هلاك (halak): Destruction or perishing of the item, which triggers liability questions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a buyer purchases a slave woman with khiyar al-shart and she gives birth before the buyer takes possession, what is the ruling?
A) The buyer may return her, as she did not become umm walad.
B) The buyer cannot return her, as she became umm walad in his ownership during the option period.
C) The option is automatically void because the item changed.
D) The buyer may return her only if the seller agrees.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar al-shart, the moment of physical possession does not solely determine ownership; the option period itself can attach legal consequences such as umm walad status, a point of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his disciples.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Deposit of Option-Bought Item with Seller: Hanafi Ruling on Loss
Commentary on a base text explaining the rule on possession return and deposit validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on the allocation of loss when a buyer with khiyar deposits the item with the seller and it is destroyed, and explain the underlying legal reasoning.

Core Idea
Ownership during khiyar determines the validity of deposit and liability for loss — Abu Hanifa suspends ownership, Sahibayn affirms it.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a buyer who purchases an item with an option (khiyar al-shart), takes possession, then deposits the item with the seller for safekeeping. If the item is destroyed while in the seller's custody, who bears the loss? The answer depends on whether the buyer's ownership during the option period is considered suspended or immediate. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on this point, leading to opposite conclusions. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply core Hanafi principles of ownership and possession in sales transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
You are presented with a buyer who has a khiyar (option to rescind) after taking possession of the purchased item. The buyer then deposits the item with the seller, and the item is destroyed. Focus on the specific legal question: who suffers the loss?
The option is assumed to be for the buyer unless otherwise stated.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the buyer does not fully own the item during the khiyar period. Therefore, the deposit is invalid. By returning the item to the seller, the buyer effectively nullifies his own possession. Consequently, the destruction occurs before the buyer's valid possession, and the seller bears the loss.
Key phrase: 'الْقَبْضُ قَدِ ارْتَفَعَ بِالرَّدِّ' (possession is nullified by return).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the buyer owns the item immediately upon purchase, even with the option. Hence, the deposit is valid, and possession remains with the buyer. The destruction is treated as if it occurred in the buyer's own custody, so the buyer bears the loss.
Key rationale: 'لَمَّا مَلَكَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي صَحَّ إِيدَاعُهُ' (since the buyer owned it, his deposit is valid).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical outcome is clear: under Abu Hanifa, the seller loses the item and must compensate or suffer the loss; under the Sahibayn, the buyer loses his purchase price and the item. This difference affects risk allocation in transactions involving options.
No explicit tarjih is given in the passage; later Hanafi practice often favors the Sahibayn's view for market stability.
5
Consider the scope and exceptions
Note that the passage also distinguishes cases where the option belongs to the seller or the sale is absolute. In those cases, the ruling is different and often unanimous. This shows that the dispute is specific to the buyer's option scenario.
See the glosses in the commentary for comparative scenarios.

Source Text

لارتفاع القبض بالرد لعدم الملك) : أي المُشتَرِي بالخيارِ إِن قَبَضَ مُشْتَرَاهُ، ثُمَّ أودعه عند البائع ، فهَلَكَ في يد البائع ، فهلكُهُ في يده يكون على البائع ؛ لأنَّ القَبْضَ قد ارتفع بالرَّد ؛ لأنَّ المشتري لم يَمْلِكُهُ، فلم يصح الايداع، بل رَدُّه إلى البائع يكون رفعاً للقَبْضِ ، فَيَكُونُ الهلاك قبل القبض، فيكون على البائع ، وعندهما لما مَلَكَهُ المُشتَرِي صَحٌ إيداعُهُ ، فلا يَرْتَفِعُ القَبْضُ، فكأَنَّه هَلَكَ فِي يَدِ المشتَرِي، فيكونُ الهَلاكُ من ماله.
