قالوا ذلك ؛ لأن شرط الخيار لغير العاقدِ إنَّما يثبت بطريق النيابة عن العاقد، فيثبت له اقتضاء. أقول : إذا اشترى على أن الغير بالخيار لا يثبت الخيار إلا برضاء المتعاقدين، فيكون نائباً عن المتعاقدين، ثمَّ رضاء البائع يخيار الغير لا يقتضي رضاه بخيار المشتري. وأجيب : بأن الترجيح محتاج إليه عند تنافي الفعلين كالفسخ والإجازة، وأما إذا اتحدا فالمطلوب حاصل بدونه فلا حاجة إليه. ووجه القول الأول : وهو الفسخ أولى : أنّ المجاز يلحقه الفسخ كمـا لـو أجاز والمبيع هالك عند البائع، والمفسوخ لا تلحقه الإجازة، فإنَّ العقد إذا انفسخ بهلاك المبيع عند البائع لا تلحقه الإجازة ولا خفاء في قوّة ما يطرأ على غيره على ما ليس كذلك. كذا في «المنح». [ ١ ] قوله : فيثبت له اقتضاء ؛ فيه بحث ؛ لأنّ شرط الاقتضاء أن يكون المقتضى أدنى منزلة من المقتضي، ألا ترى أن من قال لعبد له حنث في يمينه : كفّر عن يمينيك بالمال، لا يكون ذلك تحريراً اقتضاء؛ لأنَّ التحرير أقوى من تصرف التكفير؛ لكونه أصلاً فلا يثبت تبعاً لفرعه، ولا خفاء أنّ العاقد أعلى مرتبة، فكيف يثبت له الخيار اقتضاء ؟ وأجيب عنه : بأن الاعتبار للمقاصد، والغير هو المقصود باشتراط الخيار فكان هو الأصل نظراً إلى الخيار، والعاقد أصل من حيث التمليك لا من حيث الخيار، فلا يلزم ثبوتُ الأصل بتبعيّة فرعه، وأمّا التحرير فإنّه الأصل في الكفّارة المالية، فلا يثبت تبعاً لفرعه. كذا في «ذخيرة العقبى»(٢). (٢) قوله : أقول ؛ هذا نقض على ثبوت الخيار للمشتري اقتضاء ، حاصله : أن الرضاء لهذا الغير لا يثبتُ ما لم يوجد رضاءُ المتعاقدين، فكان هذا الغير نائباً عنهما، والظاهرُ أنَّ رضاء البائع بخياره لا يقتضي رضاءه بخيار المشتري ، فلا يثبت خيار المشتري اقتضاء.
They said that; because the condition of option for a non-contracting party is only established by way of deputyship from the contracting party, so it is established for him by requisition (iqtiḍā'). I said: If he purchases on the condition that a third party has the option, the option is not established except with the consent of the two contracting parties, so he becomes a deputy for the two contracting parties. Then the seller's consent to the option of the third party does not necessitate his consent to the option of the buyer. And it was answered: That preference (tarjih) is needed when two actions conflict like revocation and ratification, but if they are united, the desired result is achieved without it, so there is no need for it. And the basis of the first statement—that revocation is better—is that what is ratified can be affected by revocation, as if he ratified while the sold item was destroyed in the seller's possession, and what is revoked cannot be subject to ratification. Indeed, if the contract is dissolved due to the destruction of the sold item in the seller's possession, ratification cannot follow it. There is no doubt in the strength of that which occurs upon another over that which is not so. Thus in 'al-Minaḥ'. [1] His statement: 'So it is established for him by requisition'—there is a discussion in it; because the condition of requisition is that the requested (muqtaḍā) should be of a lower status than the requester (muqtaḍī). Do you not see that if someone says to a slave of his who has broken an oath: 'Expiate for your oath with property,' that does not constitute manumission by requisition; because manumission is stronger than the act of expiation, since it is a primary act, so it cannot be established as a subsidiary to its branch. And there is no doubt that the contracting party is of a higher rank, so how can the option be established for him by requisition? And it was answered: That consideration is for intentions, and the third party is the intended one in stipulating the option, so he is the original with respect to the option, while the contracting party is the original in terms of ownership, not in terms of option, so the establishment of the original by way of being subsidiary to its branch is not necessary. As for manumission, it is the original in monetary expiation, so it cannot be established as a subsidiary to its branch. Thus in 'Dhakhīrat al-'Uqbā' (2). (2) His statement: 'I say; this is a refutation of the establishment of option for the buyer by requisition, its summary is that the consent for this third party is not established unless the consent of the two contracting parties exists, so this third party is a deputy for both of them, and it is apparent that the seller's consent to his option does not necessitate his consent to the option of the buyer, so the option of the buyer is not established by requisition.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement within the Hanafi school regarding khiyar al-shart for a third party. The early opinion states that khiyar for a non-contracting party is established by way of iqtiḍā' (requisition) from the contracting parties. A later objection argues that iqtiḍā' requires the secondary item to be lower in rank than the primary; since the contracting party is higher in rank than the third party (the non-contracting party), how can khiyar be established for the contracting party via iqtiḍā'? The response clarifies that the hierarchy of iqtiḍā' depends on intention (maqāṣid). In khiyar, the third party is the intended principal; the contracting party is merely the owner of the subject matter, not of the option itself. Hence, iqtiḍā' is valid. The analogy with manumission is rejected because there the principal (manumission) is inherently stronger than expiation. This reasoning ensures coherence in Hanafi khiyar rulings.

Key Terms
اقتضاء (iqtiḍā'): Establishment of a ruling or right impliedly as a requisite of something else
نيابة (niyāba): Deputyship where one acts on behalf of another in a legal capacity
المقاصد (al-maqāṣid): Intents or objectives behind a legal stipulation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the respondent in this passage, why is the analogy between khiyar and manumission invalid?
A) Manumission is a stronger act than expiation, so it cannot be iqtiḍā'.
B) In khiyar, the third party is the intended principal; in manumission, manumission itself is the purpose.
C) The hierarchy is the same in both cases.
D) The objection only applies to khiyar, not manumission.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, intention (maqṣad) can override formal hierarchical requirements in iqtiḍā', validating khiyar for the contracting party when a third party's option is stipulated.

Conditions for Valid Sale of Two Items with Option in One
Ruling with conditions and exceptions for option in one of two items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sale of two distinct items with an option in one and distinguish between valid, invalid, and exceptional cases.

Core Idea
Sale of two slaves with option in one is valid only if price per slave and option slave are specified.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, the Hanafi ruling is explained: when selling two distinct items (like two slaves) with a condition allowing option in one, the sale is only valid if both the price of each item and which item carries the option are clearly identified. Otherwise, the contract is fasid due to ignorance (jahalah). The text also addresses a subtle point about the seller's consent to a third party's option and an exception for fungible goods and single items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is a sale of two distinct items (slaves) with a condition that the buyer has an option in one of them. The general ruling is that such a sale is valid (sahih) only when specific conditions are met; otherwise it is invalid (fasid).
2
List the two essential conditions for validity
The text states two conditions: (1) the price of each slave is specified (tafsil al-thaman), and (2) the slave subject to the option is identified (ta'yin mahall al-khiyar). Both must be present.
Without both, ignorance (jahalah) arises, which invalidates the contract.
3
Enumerate the three cases of invalidity
The text lists three scenarios where the sale is fasid: (a) neither price specified nor option subject identified, (b) price specified but option subject not identified, (c) option subject identified but price not specified.
Each case involves jahalah of the price or the object or both.
4
Understand the exception for fungible goods or a single item
The footnote clarifies that the ruling is specific to two distinct slaves. For a single slave or goods measured by volume/weight, selling with an option in half is valid even without specifying price, because half of a single thing is known and does not cause jahalah.
The exception is based on the principle that parts of a single fungible item are identical.
5
Analyze the nuance of third-party option
Ya'qub Pasha explains that when the seller consents to a third party's option, that consent is from the buyer's perspective, not the seller's own. The third party acts as a deputy for the buyer, and the seller's consent is to validate the transaction. This resolves any apparent contradiction.
This is a fine point but not essential for the basic ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيع عبدين بالخيار في أحدِهِما صح إن فَصَّلَ ثَمَنَ كُلِّ، وعَيْنَ مَحَلَّ الخيار، وفسد في الأوجه الباقية) : وهي : ١ . ما إذا لم يُفصلِ الثَّمَنَ، ولم يُعَيِّنْ مَحَلَّ الخيار. ٢. أو فَصَّلَ ولم يُعَيِّن. ٣. أو عَيَّنَ ولم يُفصل ؛ لجهالة الثَّمَن والمبيع، أو جهالة أحدهما. وفيه كلام نفيس، وهو ما ذكره يعقوب باشا (۳) : من أن رضاء البائع في هذه الصورة بخيار الأجنبي من جهة المشتري لا من جهة نفسه أيضاً، فلا ينوب إلا عن المشتري، ثم إن رضاء البائع بخيار الغير لتصحيح تصرفه، فالخيار إنما يثبت له نيابة عن المشتري ضرورة ارتضائه وتصحيح تصرفه أن يقدّر الرضاء للمشتري ، ثم يجعل الغير نائباً عنه، وحينئذ لا مجال لتوهم الأشكال. [١] قوله : على أربعة أوجه : حاصله : أن بيع عبدين على أنه بالخيار بما في أحدهما وبيع . عبدين ؛ ١. إما أن يُفصل ثمن كل منهما، ويُعين محل الخيار. ٢ . أو لم يُفصل ولم يُعين. ٣. أو يُفصل ولم يُعين. ٤. أو يُعين ولم يُفصل. ففي الصورة الأولى صح البيع ؛ لأنَّ كلاً من البيع والثمن معلوم. فإن قيل : : قد جعل قبولُ العقدِ في الذي فيه الخيار شرطاً لانعقاد البيع في الذي لا خيار فيه، فيفسد كما لو جمع بين حر وقن وفَصَّلَ الثَّمن حيث جعل قبول العقد في الحر شرطاً للانعقاد في القن. (۱) قيد بالعبدين ؛ لأن شراء الكيلي والوزني أو العبد الواحد على أنه بالخيار في نصفه جائز، سواء فصل الثمن أو لم يفصل ؛ لأن النصف من الشيء الواحد لا يتفاوت. ينظر : «فتح باب العناية (٢ : ٣١٤).
Selling two slaves with option in one of them is valid if he specifies the price of each and identifies the subject of the option, and it is invalid (fasid) in the remaining cases, which are: 1. When he does not specify the price and does not identify the subject of the option. 2. Or he specifies but does not identify. 3. Or he identifies but does not specify; due to ignorance of the price and the sold item, or ignorance of one of them. And in that there is a fine discussion, which is what Ya'qub Pasha mentioned: that the seller's consent in this form to the option of a third party is from the perspective of the buyer, not from his own perspective, so he is only a deputy for the buyer. Then the seller's consent to the option of the third party is to validate his transaction, so the option is only established for him (the third party) as a deputy for the buyer by necessity of his satisfaction and validation of his transaction, so that the buyer's satisfaction is assumed, then the third party is made his deputy. At that point, there is no room for misunderstanding of the problem. [1] His statement: 'In four ways.' Its summary is: The sale of two slaves on the condition that he has the option in one of them, and the sale of two slaves: 1. Either he specifies the price of each and identifies the subject of the option. 2. Or he does not specify and does not identify. 3. Or he specifies but does not identify. 4. Or he identifies but does not specify. In the first case the sale is valid because both the sale and the price are known. If it is said: He has made the acceptance of the contract in that which has the option a condition for the validity of the sale in that which has no option, so it becomes invalid just as if he combined a free man and a slave and specified the price, where he made the acceptance of the contract in the free man a condition for the validity in the slave. (1) It is restricted to two slaves because the purchase of measured or weighed items or a single slave on the condition of option in half of it is valid, whether he specified the price or not, because half of a single thing does not vary. See: 'Fath Bab al-'Inayah' (2:314).
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the sale of two slaves with a stipulated option in one. The ruling is straightforward: the sale is valid only if the price of each slave is specified and the slave subject to the option is identified. Otherwise, the sale is fasid (invalid) due to ignorance (jahalah) of the price or the subject matter. The text then presents a nuanced analysis by Ya'qub Pasha on how the seller's consent to the third party's option works. He clarifies that the seller's consent is given from the buyer's perspective, not his own, to validate the transaction, thus avoiding the misunderstanding that the seller is consenting to a stranger's option. Finally, a footnote explains that this ruling is specific to two distinct slaves; for a single slave or measurable goods, option in half is valid even without specifying the price, because half of a single thing is known. The passage ends with a qiyas objection comparing the case to combining a free man and a slave, but the answer is not provided here.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahālah): Ignorance about the price or subject matter that makes the contract invalid
فسد (fasada): The contract is invalid (fasid) due to a defect that may be rectified unlike batil
الكيلي والوزني (al-kaylī wa al-waznī): Goods measured by volume or weight

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the sale of two slaves with option in one valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the price of each slave is specified and the slave subject to option is identified
B) When only the total price is specified
C) When only the option subject is identified
D) When the option is for a third party

Key Takeaway
The sale of two distinct items with option in one is only valid if the price of each is specified and the option subject is identified; otherwise the contract is fasid due to jahalah.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Selling Two Slaves with Khiyar in One: Validity Conditions
Ruling on validity conditions for khiyar in sale of two slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sale of two slaves with khiyar al-shart in one and identify which scenario leads to fasid due to jahalah.

Core Idea
A sale with option in part of multiple items is valid only if both the price of each and the subject of the option are specified.

This passage from the Hidayah examines a specific scenario of khiyar al-shart where two slaves are sold but the option applies to only one. The core challenge is avoiding jahalah (ignorance) that would invalidate the contract. We will see how the Hanafi school analyzes the four logical possibilities and why specification of both price and subject is necessary. Additionally, we will explore the qiyas used to distinguish this case from invalid analogies.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the four scenarios
List the four logical possibilities regarding whether the price of each slave is specified and whether the subject of the option is identified.
The four are: (1) both specified, (2) neither specified, (3) price specified but not subject, (4) subject specified but not price.
2
Identify the valid scenario
Recognize that only scenario (1) — both specified — yields a valid sale. The other three are invalid due to jahalah.
Jahalah can be in price, subject, or both.
3
Examine the objection
Understand the qiyas argument that compares this case to combining a free person and a slave, where conditioning acceptance on the free person invalidates the sale.
The objector claims a similar conditional acceptance here should invalidate.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Grasp the distinction: the free person is not a subject of sale at all (neither in'an nor hukman), while the slave with option is a valid subject in inception (in'an) even if not in effect (hukman).
Therefore, the condition on the option slave is valid, not corrupting.
5
Apply the mudabbar analogy
See how the mudabbar (slave with contingent freedom) is also a valid subject in inception, reinforcing that the condition does not corrupt.
The mudabbar can be sold if a judge permits, so he enters the contract in inception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الخيار - خيار الشرط -
وبيع عبدين بالخيار في أحدِهِما صح إن فَصَّلَ ثَمَنَ كُلِّ، وعَيْنَ مَحَلَّ الخيار، وفسد في الأوجه الباقية ( وبيع عبدينِ ) بالخيار في أحدِهِما صح إن فَصَّلَ ثَمَنَ كُلِّ، وعَيَّنَ مَحَلَّ الخيار، وفسد في الأوجه الباقية) : وهي :
١ . ما إذا لم يُفصلِ الثَّمَنَ، ولم يُعَيِّنْ مَحَلَّ الخيار.
٢. أو فَصَّلَ ولم يُعَيِّن.
٣. أو عَيَّنَ ولم يُفصل ؛ لجهالة الثَّمن والمبيع، أو جهالة أحدهما. وفيه كلام نفيس، وهو ما ذكره يعقوب باشا : من أن رضاء البائع في هذه الصورة بخيار الأجنبي من جهة المشتري لا من جهة نفسه أيضاً، فلا ينوب إلا عن المشتري، ثم إن رضاء البائع بخيار الغير لتصحيح تصرفه، فالخيار إنما يثبت له نيابة عن المشتري ضرورة ارتضائه وتصحيح تصرفه أن يقدّر الرضاء للمشتري ، ثم يجعل الغير نائباً عنه، وحينئذ لا مجال لتوهم الأشكال.
حاصله : أن بيع عبدين على أنه بالخيار بما في أحدهما وبيع . عبدين ؛
١. إما أن يُفصل ثمن كل منهما، ويُعين محل الخيار.
٢ . أو لم يُفصل ولم يُعين.
٣. أو يُفصل ولم يُعين.
٤. أو يُعين ولم يُفصل.
ففي الصورة الأولى صح البيع ؛ لأنَّ كلاً من البيع والثمن معلوم.
فإن قيل : : قد جعل قبولُ العقدِ في الذي فيه الخيار شرطاً لانعقاد البيع في الذي لا خيار فيه، فيفسد كما لو جمع بين حر وقن وفَصَّلَ الثَّمن حيث جعل قبول العقد في الحر شرطاً للانعقاد في القن.
أجيب : بأنَّ الحرَّ غير داخل في العقدِ لا انعقاداً ولا حكماً ؛ لأنه ليس بمحل للبيع أصلاً ، فكان قبوله شرطاً مفسداً بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإنّه محل للبيع، ويدخل فيه انعقاداً وإن لم يدخل حكماً، فكان قبوله شرطاً صحيحاً.
وصار كما لو جمع بين مدبّر وقنّ حيث صح العقد في القنّ بصحته من الثمن ، مع أنَّ قبول العقد فيه مشروطاً بقبوله في المدير ؛ لأنَّ المدير داخل تحت البيع، حتى لو قضى القاضي بجواز بيعه نفذ ، فلم يكن شرط قبولِ العقد فيه مفسد للعقد في الآخر.
وفي الصور الباقية فسد البيع :
أما في الصورة الثانية فلجهالةِ الثَّمن والمبيع.
وأما في الصورة الثالثة فلجهالة المبيع. وأما في الصورة الرابعة فلجهالة الثمن.
فإن قيل : لو كان عدم التفصيل مفسد للعقد في الآخر لفسد في القنّ إذا جمع بينه وبين المدبّر أو أم الولد، ولم يفصل الثمن.
أجيب : بأن عدم التفصيل مفسد إذا أدى إلى البيع بالحصة ابتداءً فيما إذا منع عن انعقاد العقد في حق الحكم مانع كشرط الخيار ، فإنّه يجعلُ العقد فيما شرط فيه الخيار في حق الحكم كالمعدوم، فلو انعقد في حق الآخر انعقد بالحصة ابتداء، وهي مجهولة. وليس فيما إذا جمع بين القن والمدير ما يمنع عن انعقاده في حق الحكم ؛ ولهذا لو قضى القاضي بجوازه نفذ وكان قسمةُ الثَّمن في البقاء صيانة لحق محترم عند فسخ العقدِ على المدبّر وأم الولد لا ابتداءً بالحصة كما في «المنح»، و«العناية». وإنما قال : عبدين؛ لأنه لو باع عبداً واحداً أو كيلياً أو وزنياً على أنه بالخيار في نصفه صار فضلُ الثّمن له ؛ لأنَّ النصف من الشيء لا يتفاوت، فقيمته أيضاً لا تتفاوت، فإذا كان ثمن الكلِّ معلوماً كان ثمن النّصف أيضاً معلوماً، فالبيع معلوم؛ إذ الشيوعُ لا يمنعُ الجواز، ولا فرق بين أن يكون الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري. كذا في «الكافي».
Book of Sales, Chapter of Option - Option of Condition
And selling two slaves with option in one of them: it is valid if he specifies the price of each and specifies the subject of the option, and it is invalid in the remaining aspects. (And selling two slaves with option in one of them: valid if he specifies the price of each and specifies the subject of the option, and invalid in the remaining aspects). They are:
1. When he does not specify the price and does not specify the subject of the option.
2. Or he specifies but does not specify the subject.
3. Or he specifies the subject but does not specify the price; due to ignorance of the price and the sold item, or ignorance of one of them. In this is a fine discussion, which is what Ya'qub Pasha mentioned: that the seller's consent in this scenario to a third party's option is from the buyer's side, not from his own side also, so he (the third party) only represents the buyer. Then the seller's consent to a third party's option is to validate his transaction; the option is only established for him as representing the buyer due to necessity of his approval and to validate his transaction: that approval is considered for the buyer, then the third party is made his representative. Then there is no room to imagine difficulty.
Its summary: that selling two slaves on the condition that he has option in one of them:
1. Either he specifies the price of each and specifies the place of option.
2. Or he does not specify and does not specify.
3. Or he specifies but does not specify.
4. Or he specifies but does not specify.
In the first scenario, the sale is valid because both the sale and the price are known.
If it is said: He made acceptance of the contract in that which has the option a condition for the contract's conclusion in that which has no option, so it is invalid like when combining a free person and a slave and specifying the price: where he makes acceptance of the contract in the free person a condition for conclusion in the slave.
Answer: The free person is not included in the contract, neither in inception nor in effect, because he is not a subject for sale at all, so his acceptance was a corrupting condition. Unlike our case: he (the slave with option) is a subject for sale and enters into the contract in inception even if not in effect, so his acceptance is a valid condition.
And it becomes like combining a mudabbar and a slave: where the contract in the slave is valid with the validity of its share of the price, even though acceptance of the contract in him is conditioned on acceptance in the mudabbar; because the mudabbar is included in the sale, so much so that if a judge rules to permit his sale it is executed, so the condition of acceptance of the contract in him did not corrupt the contract in the other.
In the remaining scenarios, the sale is invalid:
As for the second scenario: due to ignorance of the price and the sold.
As for the third scenario: due to ignorance of the sold.
As for the fourth scenario: due to ignorance of the price.
If it is said: If lack of specification were to invalidate the contract in the other, then it would be invalid in the slave when he combines between him and a mudabbar or umm walad, and he does not specify the price.
Answer: Lack of specification is invalidating when it leads to sale by share ab initio in a situation where a preventive factor prevents the contract from taking effect in respect of effect, like the condition of option; for it makes the contract in that which has the option, in respect of effect, as if non-existent. So if it takes effect in the other, it takes effect by share ab initio, and it is unknown. In the case of combining a slave and a mudabbar, there is nothing preventing the contract from taking effect in respect of effect; hence if a judge rules to permit his sale, it executes, and division of price is at the survival stage to protect a respected right upon rescission of the contract regarding the mudabbar and umm walad, not ab initio by share, as in al-Minh and al-Inaya. And he said "two slaves" because if he sells a single slave or a measured or weighed item with option in half of it, then the remaining of the price is for him; because half of a thing does not differ, so its value also does not differ. So if the price of the whole is known, the price of the half is also known, so the sale is known; since common ownership does not prevent validity. And there is no difference whether the option is for the seller or the buyer. So in al-Kafi.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary discusses the ruling on selling two slaves with a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in one of them. The author presents the base ruling: the sale is valid only if the price of each slave is specified and the specific slave subject to the option is identified. Otherwise, in the remaining three logical possibilities (neither specified, price specified but not the subject, subject specified but not price), the sale is invalid due to ignorance (jahalah) of the price or the sold item. The text then addresses an objection comparing this case to combining a free person and a slave: in that case, making acceptance conditional on the free person's contract invalidates the slave's sale because the free person is not a valid subject of sale. The response distinguishes that here, the slave with option is a valid subject in inception (in'an) even if not in effect (hukman), so the condition is valid. A second analogy with a mudabbar (slave with contingent freedom) and an ordinary slave is given: the mudabbar enters the contract in inception, so the condition is not corrupting. The remaining scenarios are invalid due to ignorance. Finally, the text explains why the ruling specifically mentions 'two slaves': for a single slave or fungible goods, half of the thing is uniform, so the price of the half is known even without specification. The option can be for either party.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option to rescind a sale stipulated by one or both parties for a specified period.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance (of price or subject matter) that leads to invalidity of the sale.
انعقاداً وحكماً (in'an wa hukman): In inception (in'an) meaning the contract legally begins to exist; and in effect (hukman) meaning the rulings of the contract apply (e.g., ownership transfer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the sale of two slaves with khiyar al-shart in one of them valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the price of each slave is specified, even if the subject of the option is not identified.
B) When the subject of the option is identified, even if the price of each is not specified.
C) When both the price of each slave and the specific subject of the option are specified.
D) The sale is always invalid regardless of specification.

Key Takeaway
The sale of multiple items with option in part requires specification of each item's price and identification of the option subject to avoid invalidity due to jahalah.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Khiyar al-Shart and Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Conditions for Valid Options in Sale
Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin with objections and answers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and corrupting conditions of option (khiyar) in a sale and apply the Hanafi rules for khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin to determine a sale's validity.

Core Idea
A condition of option does not corrupt a sale if the subject matter and price are known and no fatal ignorance (jahalah) arises.

In Hanafi fiqh, the permissibility of stipulating an option (khiyar) in a sale is nuanced. While a condition that introduces ignorance (jahalah) into the price or subject matter renders the sale corrupt (fasid), a condition that merely delays the finality of the contract—such as khiyar al-shart or khiyar al-ta'yin—can be valid if the essential elements are known. This lesson unpacks the commentary on al-Hidayah, guiding you through the key distinctions and the intra-Hanafi dispute on time limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Conditions
State the general rule: a sale with a valid option is sahih when both price and subject matter are known; it is fasid when jahalah exists. Note the exception for khiyar al-ta'yin where the unchosen items are not sold but treated as trusts.
The ruling hinges on knowledge (ma'rifah) vs. ignorance (jahalah).
2
Analyze the Objection and Answer Regarding Inclusion of Non-Sale Items
Trace the objection that accepting a condition (e.g., option on a slave) which is not fully sold should corrupt the contract. The Hanafi answer: the item under option is sold in formation but not in effect, so the condition is valid—unlike including a free person which is never a subject of sale.
Key analogy: combination of mudabbar and qinn.
3
Examine the Cases Where Sale is Corrupt Due to Jahalah
List the four cases of combined sales and identify which type of jahalah (price, subject matter, or both) causes corruption. Understand why lack of detail corrupts only when it leads to sale by unknown share at inception.
The distinction between initial division (ibtida') and post-contract division is crucial.
4
Apply the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Time Limit for Khiyar al-Ta'yin
State Abu Hanifa's view (three days) and the Sahibayn's view (any specified period). Work through the thamarah al-khilaf: a sale with a period longer than three days is fasid according to Abu Hanifa but sahih according to the Sahibayn.
This ikhtilaf is recorded in al-Hidayah and other sources.

Source Text

أجيب : بأنَّ الحرَّ غير داخل في العقدِ لا انعقاداً ولا حكماً ؛ لأنه ليس بمحل للبيع أصلاً ، فكان قبوله شرطاً مفسداً بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإنّه محل للبيع، ويدخل فيه انعقاداً وإن لم يدخل حكماً، فكان قبوله شرطاً صحيحاً. وصار كما لو جمع بين مدبّر وقنّ حيث صح العقد في القنّ بصحته من الثمن ، مع أنَّ قبول العقد فيه مشروطاً بقبوله في المدير ؛ لأنَّ المدير داخل تحت البيع، حتى لو قضى القاضي بجواز بيعه نفذ ، الثمن. فإن قيل : لو كان عدم التفصيل مفسد للعقد في الآخر لفسد في القنّ إذا جمع بينه وبين المدبّر أو أم الولد، ولم يفصل الثمن. أجيب : بأن عدم التفصيل مفسد إذا أدى إلى البيع بالحصة ابتداءً فيما إذا منع عن انعقاد العقد في حق الحكم مانع كشرط الخيار ، فإنّه يجعلُ العقد فيما شرط فيه الخيار في حق الحكم كالمعدوم، فلو انعقد في حق الآخر انعقد بالحصة ابتداء، وهي مجهولة. وليس فيما إذا جمع بين القن والمدير ما يمنع عن انعقاده في حق الحكم ؛ ولهذا لو قضى القاضي بجوازه نفذ وكان قسمةُ الثَّمن في البقاء صيانة لحق محترم عند فسخ العقدِ على المدبّر وأم الولد لا ابتداءً بالحصة كما في «المنح»، و«العناية». وإنما قال : عبدين؛ لأنه لو باع عبداً واحداً أو كيلياً أو وزنياً على أنه بالخيار في نصفه صار فضلُ الثّمن له ؛ لأنَّ النصف من الشيء لا يتفاوت، فقيمته أيضاً لا تتفاوت، فإذا كان ثمن الكلِّ معلوماً كان ثمن النّصف أيضاً معلوماً، فالبيع معلوم؛ إذ الشيوعُ لا يمنعُ الجواز، ولا فرق بين أن يكون الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري. كذا في «الكافي». ثم قال: وشراء أحدِ الثَّوبين، أو أحد ثلاثة على أن يُعَيِّنَ أَيَّاً شاء في ثلاثةِ أيام. بَقِي أَنَّ في صورة الجواز، وإن لم يوجد الجهالة لكنَّ قبول ما ليس بمبيع جُعِلَ شرطاً لقبول ما هو مبيع، فينبغي أَنْ يَفْسُدَ بالشَّرط الفاسد عنده. والجواب : إنَّ المبيع بشرط الخيارِ داخل في الإيجاب لا في الحكم ، فـلا يصدق عليه أنه ما ليس بمبيع من كل وجه بل هو مبـيـع مـن وجـه ، فاعتبرنا الوجهين، ففي صورة الجهالة اعتبرنا ما ليس بمبيع حتى يفسد العقد، وفي صورة أن يكون كلُّ واحدٍ منهما معلوماً اعتبرنا أنه مبيع حتى لا يفسد العقد. وشراء أحد النوبين ، أو أحد ثلاثة على أن يُعَيِّنَ أَيَّا شاء في ثلاثة أيام. فإنَّ العبد الذي فيه الخيار غير داخل حكماً، كما إذا جمع بين حر وقن، فإنه لا يجوز العقد في القنّ وإن فَصَّلَ الثَّمَنَ لِمَا أَنه جعل قبول العقد في الحر شرطاً لصحة العقد في القن فكذا هذا. والجواب حاصله : أنّ البيع بشرط الخيار مبيع من وجه وغير مبيع من وجه، ففي صورة كون كل من الثَّمن والمحل معلوماً جعل مبيعاً، وفي صورة الجهالة غيرُ مبيع، وتقريره مر آنفا. قوله : لا يفسد العقد ؛ لقائل أن يقول : هو شرط لا يقتضيه العقد فكان مفسداً. والجواب: أنه ليس فيه نفع لأحد العاقدين ولا للمعقود عليه فلا يكون فاسداً. وشراء أحد النوبين، أو أحد ثلاثة على أن يعين في ثلاثة أَيَّامٍ أَيَّا شاء ورضي البائعُ بهذا الخيار صح هذا البيع، وإن لم يشترط تعيينه ؛ أو شرط لكن في أحد أربعة أثواب أو عبيد لم يصح البيع. أحد النوبين، أو أحد ثلاثة ؛ هذا أولى مما في بعض المتون : من يشتري ثوبين ؛ لأن البيع في الحقيقة أحدهما والآخر أمانة. قال في «الهداية»: «إذا لم يذكر خيار الشرط لا بد من توقيت خيارِ التَّعيين بالثلاث عنده ، وبمدة معلومة أيتها كانت عندهما».
It was answered: The free person is not included in the contract, neither in formation nor in effect, because he is not a subject of sale at all. So accepting him as a condition is a corrupting condition, unlike our case, for here the slave is a subject of sale and enters the contract in formation even if not in effect, so accepting him as a condition is valid. It becomes like the case where a mudabbar and a qinn (ordinary slave) are combined, where the contract is valid for the qinn with the price being sound, even though acceptance of the contract for it is conditional upon acceptance in the mudabbar, because the mudabbar is included in the sale such that if the judge permits its sale, it is effective. So the condition of acceptance in it does not corrupt the contract for the other. In the remaining cases, the sale is corrupt: in the second case due to ignorance of price and subject matter; in the third due to ignorance of subject matter; in the fourth due to ignorance of price. If it is said: If lack of detail were corruptive for the contract in the other, then it would be corrupt for the qinn when combined with a mudabbar or umm walad without detailing the price. The answer: Lack of detail is corruptive when it leads to sale by share initially, when a hindrance prevents the contract from taking effect regarding the ruling, like a condition of option (khiyar). For it renders the contract in which option is stipulated as non-existent in terms of effect. So if the contract is concluded for the other, it is concluded by share initially, which is unknown. But in the combination of qinn and mudabbar there is nothing preventing its conclusion in effect; therefore if the judge permits its sale, it is effective, and the division of the price later is a preservation of a protected right upon rescission of the contract for the mudabbar and umm walad, not initially by share, as in al-Minah and al-Inayah. He only said 'two slaves' because if one sells a single slave or a measured or weighed item on condition of option in half of it, the surplus of price goes to him, because half of a thing does not vary, so its value does not vary; if the total price is known, the half price is also known, so the sale is known, since common ownership does not prevent validity. There is no difference whether the option is for the seller or buyer; so in al-Kafi. Then he said: 'And the purchase of one of two garments, or one of three, on condition to specify whichever he wishes within three days.' There remains the point that in the case of validity, even though ignorance is absent, yet acceptance of what is not sold is made a condition for acceptance of what is sold, so the contract should be corrupt due to the corrupt condition in his (Abu Hanifa's) view. The answer: The item sold with option is included in the offer but not in the effect, so it cannot be said that it is not sold in every respect; rather it is sold in one respect. So we consider both aspects: in the case of ignorance we regard it as not sold so the contract is corrupt; in the case where each is known we regard it as sold so the contract is not corrupt. And the purchase of one of two slaves, or one of three, on condition to specify whichever he wishes within three days. For the slave subject to option is not included in effect, just as when a free person and a slave are combined, the contract is not valid for the slave even if the price is detailed, because acceptance of the contract for the free person is made a condition for the validity of the contract for the slave; so here likewise. The summary of the answer: The sale with option is sold in one respect and not sold in another. So in the case where both price and subject matter are known, it is considered sold; in the case of ignorance, not sold. Its explanation has passed. His statement: 'It does not corrupt the contract' — someone may say: It is a condition not required by the contract, so it would be corruptive. The answer: It does not benefit either contracting party nor the subject matter, so it is not corrupt. And the purchase of one of two garments or one of three on condition to specify whichever he wishes within three days, with the seller's consent to this option, makes the sale valid, even if he did not stipulate its specification; but if he stipulates for one of four garments or slaves, the sale is not valid. The phrase 'one of two garments or one of three' is better than what is in some texts: 'who buys two garments', because in reality the sale is of one and the other is a trust. He said in al-Hidayah: 'If khiyar al-shart is not mentioned, it is necessary to specify a time for khiyar al-ta'yin: three days according to Abu Hanifa, and any known period according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).' End.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a discussion from a commentary (sharh) on the rulings of khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) and khiyar al-ta'yin (option of determination) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by addressing an objection: why is the condition of option valid when included in a sale of a slave who is a proper subject of sale, whereas including a free person as a condition corrupts the contract? The answer: a free person is not a subject of sale at all, so the condition is corrupting; but a slave with khiyar is a subject of sale in formation, though not in effect, so the condition is valid. The author then compares this to selling a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is deferred after the master's death) together with a regular slave (qinn): the contract is valid for the qinn, because the mudabbar is included in the sale's formation. The passage then lists cases where the sale is corrupt due to jahalah (ignorance) of price or subject matter. A further objection is raised: if lack of detail (i.e., not specifying which item has khiyar) corrupts the contract, then combining a qinn with a mudabbar or umm walad without detailing the price should also corrupt. The answer: lack of detail corrupts only when it leads to sale by an unknown share at the outset, which happens when a hindrance (like khiyar) prevents the contract from taking effect. In the case of mudabbar, there is no such hindrance because the mudabbar's sale can be executed by the judge, so the price is divided later, preserving the rights. The author then explains that selling a single item with khiyar on half is valid because half of a known thing is known. Next, the passage moves to khiyar al-ta'yin: buying one of two or three items with the option to choose within three days. The author notes a potential issue: accepting what is not sold (the unchosen items) as a condition for the sale of the chosen one should corrupt the contract. The rebuttal: the item with option is sold in one respect (formation) but not in another (effect), so it is not entirely unsold. Thus, if the price and subject matter are known, the sale is valid; if there is jahalah, it is corrupt. The passage also clarifies that the purchase of one of two or three items with the right to choose is valid only if the period is specified: three days according to Abu Hanifa, any specified period according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Furthermore, if the seller consents to the option, the sale is valid even without explicit stipulation; but if the option is among four or more items, the sale is invalid due to excessive jahalah.

Key Terms
الخيار (al-khiyar): The legal option or right to rescind or confirm a contract within a specified period.
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option in a sale where the buyer selects one item from a group of similar items within a fixed time.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Legal ignorance or uncertainty about a essential element of the contract, such as price or subject matter, that can cause the contract to be fasid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following cases renders the sale fasid due to jahalah?
A) Selling a mudabbar and a qinn together without detailing the price.
B) Selling one of two garments with a three-day option to choose.
C) Selling a single slave with option on half of it.
D) Selling one of three items without specifying the option period.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a conditional option in a sale hinges on the knowledge of price and subject matter; jahalah corrupts, but a known option with a specified time is valid.

Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Purchasing One of a Set with Option to Specify
Ruling and istihsan basis for khiyar al-ta'yin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin and identify the two conditions (specified time, up to three items) that make the sale valid by istihsan.

Core Idea
The sale of an unspecified item from a set is valid by istihsan for up to three items due to need.

This lesson examines a specific type of sale: buying one of two or three garments (or similar items) with the condition that the buyer will specify which one within a set period. While straightforward analogy (qiyas) would invalidate such a contract due to uncertainty (jahalah), the Hanafi school permits it through istihsan (juristic preference) because of practical necessity. We will explore the reasoning, the limitation to three items, and the intra-madhhab difference on the duration of the option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contract
Recognize that this is a sale of one unspecified item from a known set (e.g., one of three garments) with a condition that the buyer will specify within a time limit. The items are individually known but the specific item is not yet determined.
2
Note the General Qiyas Rule
Understand that by strict analogy (qiyas), this sale would be invalid because the object of sale (mabi') is unknown at the time of contract (jahalah), which leads to potential dispute and thus invalidates the contract.
This is the default position of other schools like the Shafi'i.
3
Understand the Istihsan Justification
See why the Hanafis depart from qiyas: necessity (hajah). The buyer may need to choose an item for someone else (e.g., wife, daughter) or trust his own later judgment. Also, the uncertainty does not lead to dispute because the option holder will resolve it. Thus, the sale is valid by istihsan.
The cause of the concession (rukhsah) is twofold: need and non-dispute.
4
Identify the Limit of Three Items
Note that the concession applies only up to three items. Why? Because with three items (good, medium, bad), the need for choice is satisfied. With four or more, the need is not pressing, so the original prohibition remains.
Beyond three, the ruling returns to the qiyas-based prohibition.
5
Recognize Intra-Hanafi Difference on Duration
Abu Hanifa requires the option period to be three days. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) allow any known duration. The mufta bihi (operative view) is up to three items with a specified time, following Abu Hanifa's three-day limit.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the validity of the contract per se.

Source Text

وشراء أحد الثوبين، أو أحد ثلاثة على أن يعين أيا شاء في ثلاثة أيام. بقى أن في صورة الجواز، وإن لم يوجد الجهالة لكن قبول ما ليس بمبيع جعل شرطا لقبول ما هو مبيع، فينبغي أن يفسد بالشرط الفاسد عنده. والجواب: إن المبيع بشرط الخيار داخل في الإيجاب لا في الحكم، فلا يصدق عليه أنه ما ليس بمبيع من كل وجه بل هو مبيع من وجه، فاعتبرنا الوجهين، ففي صورة الجهالة اعتبرنا ما ليس بمبيع حتى يفسد العقد، وفي صورة أن يكون كل واحد منهما معلوما اعتبرنا أنه مبيع حتى لا يفسد العقد. لا إن لم يشترط تعيينه، ولا في أحد أربعة: لأن القياس عدم الجواز، لكن استحسنًا في الثلاثة لمكان الحاجة؛ لأن الثلاثة مشتملة على الجيد والرديء والمتوسط، وفي الزائد على الثلاثة أبقينا الحكم على الأصل، وهو عدم الجواز. قوله: لأن ... الخ؛ حاصله: أن القياس يقتضي عدم جواز هذا البيع لجهالة المبيع؛ لأن المبيع أحد الأثواب وهو غير معين، فصار مجهولا، وجهالته تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لتفاوت الأثواب في أنفسها، وكل ما هو كذلك مفسد للبيع. لكنا أثبتنا الجواز بالاستحسان، وهو أن الخيار إنما شرع للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن؛ ليختار ما هو الأرفق والأوفق، والحاجة إلى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى اختيار من يثق برأيه، أو اختيار من يشتريه لأجله من الزوجة والبنت وغيرهما، ولا يمكنه البائع من الحمل إلا بالشراء؛ كي لا يبقي أمانة، فكان معنى خيار الشرط. وهذه الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لتعيين من له الخيار، فلا يمنع الجواز، غير أن هذه الحاجة تندفع بالثلاثة؛ لوجود الجيد والرديء والمتوسط، ولا حاجة إلى الأربعة؛ لأنه زائد غير محتاج إليه، فانتفى جزء العلة، فإن علة الرخصة أمران: الحاجة، وكون الجهالة مفضية إلى النزاع، فلا يثبت الرخصة بأحدهما، فإن الحكم لا يثبت إلا أن تتم علته.
And purchasing one of two garments, or one of three, on condition that he specifies whichever he wishes within three days. There remains that in the case of permissibility, even if there is no uncertainty, accepting what is not sold is made a condition for accepting what is sold, so it would be invalid due to the corrupt condition according to him. The answer: The item sold with a condition of option is included in the offer not in the ruling, so it does not apply to it that it is not sold in every respect, rather it is sold in one respect, so we consider both aspects. In the case of uncertainty we consider it not sold so the contract is void, and in the case where each of them is known we consider it sold so the contract is not void. No if he did not stipulate specification, nor in one of four: because analogy is non-permissibility, but we approved by istihsan in three due to need; because the three include good, bad, and medium, and beyond three we keep the ruling on the original, which is non-permissibility. His statement: 'Because...' etc.; its summary: analogy requires non-permissibility of this sale due to uncertainty of the sold item; because the sold item is one of the garments and it is unspecified, so it becomes unknown, and its uncertainty leads to dispute; due to the variation of the garments themselves, and everything like that invalidates the sale. But we established permissibility by istihsan, which is that option was legislated for the need to prevent loss; so that he chooses what is most suitable and agreeable, and the need for this type of sale is realized; because he needs to choose someone whose opinion he trusts, or to choose someone for whom he buys such as the wife or daughter, and the seller cannot let him take the item except by sale, so that it does not remain as a trust, so it is similar to the meaning of option condition. And this uncertainty does not lead to dispute because of the specification of the one who has the option, so it does not prevent permissibility, but this need is fulfilled by three; because there is good, bad, and medium, and there is no need for four; because it is an excess not needed, so part of the cause is absent, because the cause of the concession is two things: need, and that uncertainty leads to dispute, so the concession is not established by one of them, for the ruling is not established unless its cause is complete.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the permissibility of purchasing one of a set of items (e.g., two garments, three slaves) with a condition that the buyer has the right to specify which one within three days. The author first states the ruling, then addresses an objection: that this involves accepting something not yet sold as a condition, which should invalidate the contract. The response clarifies that the item with the option is considered sold from one perspective and not sold from another, so the ruling depends on whether there is uncertainty. If the items are known (each individually known), the contract is valid; if unknown (like saying 'one of these' without specification), it is invalid. Then the text explains that the sale is valid only if the specification is stipulated within a time (three days by Abu Hanifa), and only up to three items. The reason is that analogy (qiyas) would forbid it due to uncertainty (jahalah), but istihsan (juristic preference) permits it for up to three items because of need (hajah). The need is that a buyer may want to choose an item for someone else or trust his own selection later, and the seller cannot part with the goods except by sale. The uncertainty does not lead to dispute because the option holder can resolve it. But the need is only satisfied with three items (good, medium, bad); beyond that, the need is not pressing, so analogy applies again. The passage concludes that the cause of the concession consists of both need and that the uncertainty does not lead to dispute; if one is missing, the concession does not apply.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): An option to specify which item among a set of items the buyer will purchase, within a specified time.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, such as need or custom.
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or ignorance about the specific item being sold, which normally invalidates a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is purchasing one of four unspecified items invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because four items involve more gharar.
B) Because the need is only satisfied with three items, and beyond that the need is absent.
C) Because the buyer cannot choose properly among four.
D) Because the seller's consent is not valid for more than three.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits khiyar al-ta'yin by istihsan for up to three items with a specified time, because the need for choice is satisfied and the uncertainty does not lead to dispute.

The Seller's Option to Specify: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Reporting an intra-Hanafi dispute on the seller's khiyar al-ta'yin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on khiyar al-ta'yin for the seller and explain the basis (istihsan vs. qiyas) for each.

Core Idea
The seller's option to specify is disputed within the Hanafi school: permitted by istihsan or rejected for lack of need.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the seller, like the buyer, can have the option to specify which item among a set to deliver (khiyar al-ta'yin). The source passage reports two conflicting positions — one allowing it by istihsan (juristic preference), another disallowing it because the concession was only granted to the buyer due to need. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how istihsan and qiyas operate within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is about khiyar al-ta'yin (option to specify) when stipulated for the seller, not the buyer. The buyer's option is already established as valid.
Khiyar al-ta'yin is a special option allowing selection from multiple items after the contract.
2
State the first position (Al-Karkhi)
Al-Karkhi, in his Mukhtasar, holds that it is permissible by istihsan. This means he departs from strict analogy (qiyas) because of a perceived need or general benefit.
Istihsan is a key Hanafi principle: preferring a weaker analogy or abandoning analogy due to stronger evidence of need.
3
State the second position (Al-Mujarrad)
The author of al-Mujarrad holds it is not permissible. The reasoning: khiyar al-ta'yin was permitted for the buyer as a concession contrary to analogy due to the buyer's need (to avoid loss or gharar). The seller has no such need, so the concession does not extend to him.
This position relies on the principle that concessions (rukhsas) are not analogically extended beyond their rationale.
4
Note the subsidiary issue: combination with khiyar al-shart
There is a further difference: some require that khiyar al-shart (option of condition) be present alongside khiyar al-ta'yin in the contract. Shams al-A'immah considers this requirement correct, while others do not require it.
This subsidiary issue affects the validity of the condition: if khiyar al-shart is required but missing, the contract may be fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: صح؛ أي الشراء أو خيار التعيين للمشتري، أما لو شرط خيار التعيين للبائع فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه: فذكر الكرخي في مختصره: إنه يجوز استحساناً، وذكر في المجرد: إنه لا يجوز؛ لأنه جوز للمشتري للحاجة مخالفاً للقياس، ولا حاجة إليه للبائع. كذا ذكره العيني في شرح الكنز. ثم قيل: يشترط أن يكون في هذا العقد خيار الشرط مع خيار التعيين، وهو المذكور في الجامع الصغير، قال شمس الأئمة: هو الصحيح، وقيل: لا.
His statement: 'It is valid'; i.e., the purchase or the option of specification belongs to the buyer. As for if he stipulates the option of specification for the seller, the mashayikh differed: Al-Karkhi in his Mukhtasar mentioned that it is permissible by istihsan, and in al-Mujarrad it is mentioned that it is not permissible; because it was permitted for the buyer due to need contrary to analogy, and there is no need for it for the seller. Thus mentioned by al-Ayni in Sharh al-Kanz. Then it was said: It is required that in this contract there be the option of condition together with the option of specification, and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir; Shams al-A'immah said: this is the correct view, and it was said: no.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the seller can have khiyar al-ta'yin (option to specify which item to sell among a set). The author notes that the option of specification is originally for the buyer. If it is stipulated for the seller, there are two positions: Al-Karkhi in his Mukhtasar allows it by istihsan, while the author of al-Mujarrad disallows it, arguing that the concession was granted to the buyer due to need (to avoid gharar and loss), and the seller has no such need. Al-Ayni in his Sharh al-Kanz reports this difference. Then there is a subsidiary issue: whether khiyar al-shart (condition option) must be combined with khiyar al-ta'yin. The text from al-Jami' al-Saghir states that it is required, and Shams al-A'immah says this is the correct view, but there is also a view that it is not required. The passage does not resolve which view is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option to specify which item among a set is the subject of the sale.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference justifying departure from analogy due to need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Mujarrad, why is khiyar al-ta'yin not valid for the seller?
A) Because it leads to gharar for the seller.
B) Because it was permitted for the buyer due to need, and the seller has no such need.
C) Because it is against the consensus of the companions.
D) Because the seller cannot specify after the contract.

Key Takeaway
The seller's option to specify is a disputed issue in the Hanafi school; the preponderant view is that it is not valid because the original concession was specific to the buyer's need.

Khiyar al-Ta'yin: The Option of Specification – Istihsan and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin with istihsan justification and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin, explain the istihsan justification based on the 'illa of need and dispute prevention, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of khiyar al-shart and the seller's option.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid by istihsan for three items only because the 'illa of need and dispute prevention is complete in three but not more.

When a buyer cannot decide among multiple items, Islamic commercial law provides the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin). But how many items are allowed, and what conditions must be met? This lesson unpacks a detailed Hanafi ruling from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, where the author explains the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the istihsan that permits this option for three items, the dispute over its prerequisites, and the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
From the matn: 'Sah (valid) if the option of specification is stipulated, and not in one of four.' Determine what this means for khiyar al-ta'yin: it is valid only when stipulated and limited to three items.
The phrase 'not in one of four' means it is not valid for four items.
2
Understand the qiyas vs istihsan conflict
Qiyas would prohibit the sale because the sold item is unspecified (jahala), leading to dispute. But istihsan permits it due to need. Identify the two elements of the 'illa for istihsan: (1) need (haja) and (2) that the ignorance does not lead to dispute (because the chooser is specified).
The 'illa is composite: both need and non-dispute must be present.
3
Analyze why three items suffice
Three items (good, medium, poor) cover the range of quality, fulfilling the buyer's need. Adding a fourth item introduces jahala without additional benefit, so part of the 'illa is negated, and the ruling reverts to qiyas (invalid).
The need is met by three; four is extra and unnecessary.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart
The text reports a dispute: Some scholars, including the author of al-Jami' al-Saghir and Shams al-A'imma, require khiyar al-shart (stipulated option) alongside khiyar al-ta'yin. Others do not. The mufta bihi view is that khiyar al-shart is required.
This is a dispute among Hanafi imams, not between schools.
5
Consider the seller's option dispute
Another dispute: Can the seller be granted khiyar al-ta'yin? Al-Karkhi permits by istihsan; al-Mujarrad prohibits because need only applies to the buyer. The relied-upon view prohibits it.
Practical consequence: khiyar al-ta'yin is only for the buyer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سح ، لا إن لم يشترط تعيينه ، ولا في أحد أربعة
[۱]
زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية
، لا إن لم يشترط تعيينه ولا في أحدٍ أربعة : لأن القياس عدم الجواز،
لكن استحسنًا في الثَّلاثة لمكان الحاجة ؛ لأنّ الثَّلاثة مشتملة على الجيد والرديء والمتوسط، وفي الزَّائد على الثلاثة أبقينا الحكم على الأصل، وهو عدم الجواز. 11 ] قوله : صح ؛ أي الشَّراءُ أو خيارُ التَّعيين للمشتري ، أما لو شرط خيارَ التَّعيين للبائع فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه : فذكر الكرخى » في «مختصره»: إنه يجوز استحساناً، وذكر في «المجرد»: إنه لا يجوز؛ لأنه جُوِّزَ للمشتري للحاجة مخالفاً للقياس، ولا حاجة إليه للبائع. كذا ذكره العيني في «شرح الكنز»).
(٢) قوله : لأن ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن القياس يقتضي عدم جواز هذا البيع الجهالة المبيع ؛ لأنَّ المبيع أحد الأثواب وهو غير معين، فصار مجهولاً ، وجهالته تفضي إلى المنازعة ؛ لتفاوتِ الأثواب في أنفسها ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك مفسد للبيع.
لكنا أثبتنا الجواز بالاستحسان، وهو أنّ الخيار إنما شرع للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن ؛ ليختار ما هو الأرفق والأوفق ، والحاجة إلى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة ؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى اختيار من يثق برأيه، أو اختيار من يشتريه لأجله من الزوجة والبنت وغيرهما، ولا يمكنه البائع من الحمل إلا بالشراء ؛ كي لا يبقي أمانة، فكان معنى خيار الشرط. وهذه الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة ؛ لتعيين من له الخيار، فلا يمنعُ الجواز، غير أن هذه الحاجة تندفع بالثلاثة ؛ لوجود الجيد والرديء والمتوسط، ولا حاجة إلى الأربعة ؛ لأنـه زائـد غير محتاج إليه، فانتفى جزء العلة، فإن علة الرخصة أمران : الحاجة، وكون الجهالة مفضية إلى النّزاع، فلا يثبت الرخصة بأحدهما ، فإنَّ الحكم لا يثبت إلا أن يتم علته. ثم قيل : يشترط أن يكون في هذا العقد خيار الشرط مع خيار التعيين، وهو المذكور في «الجامع الصغير») ، قال شمس الأئمة له : هو الصحيح ، وقيل : لا
Sah (valid): not if he did not stipulate its specification, and not in one of four (items). The summary of al-Nihayah for 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah: not if he did not stipulate its specification, and not in one of four: because by qiyas it is not permissible. But we ruled by istihsan for three due to need; because three contain good, bad, and medium, and for more than three we keep the ruling on the original (qiyas), which is impermissibility. [Commentator] said: "Sah" means the purchase or the option of specification is for the buyer. But if he stipulates the option of specification for the seller, the mashayikh differed: Al-Karkhi in his Mukhtasar said it is permissible by istihsan, while in al-Mujarrad it is said not permissible because it was allowed for the buyer due to need contrary to qiyas, and there is no need for the seller. Thus mentioned by al-'Ayni in Sharh al-Kanz. (2) His statement: "because..." its summary: that qiyas requires the impermissibility of this sale due to ignorance of the sold item, because the sold item is one of the garments and it is unspecified, so it becomes unknown, and its ignorance leads to dispute due to the disparity of the garments themselves, and everything like that invalidates the sale. But we established permissibility by istihsan, which is that the option was legislated for the need to prevent loss, so that one may choose what is more beneficial and suitable, and the need for this type of sale is realized because he needs the choice of one whose opinion he trusts, or the choice of one for whom he buys (like wife, daughter, etc.), and the seller cannot hand over except by purchase so that it does not remain a trust. So it is like the meaning of khiyar al-shart. And this ignorance does not lead to dispute because the one with the option is specified, so it does not prevent validity. However, this need is fulfilled by three because they contain good, bad, and medium, and there is no need for four because it is extra and not needed. Thus part of the 'illa is negated. The 'illa of the dispensation is two matters: need and that the ignorance leads to dispute. So the dispensation is not established by one of them alone, because the ruling is only established when its 'illa is complete. Then it is said: it is required that in this contract there be khiyar al-shart along with khiyar al-ta'yin, and that is what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Shams al-A'imma said: that is the correct view. And it is said: no (it is not required).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) in a sale. The matn states: 'It is valid (sah) if the option of specification is stipulated, but not if it is not stipulated, and it is not valid for four items.' The commentary (sharh) explains that qiyas would prohibit such a sale entirely due to ignorance (jahala) of the exact item, but istihsan permits it for three items due to need—since three items can represent good, medium, and poor quality, allowing the buyer to choose. For more than four items, the need is not compelling, so the original qiyas of prohibition applies. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: Does the option of specification require the simultaneous stipulation of khiyar al-shart (stipulated option)? According to al-Jami' al-Saghir and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, it does require khiyar al-shart; this is the relied-upon (sahih) view. On the other hand, some scholars (like al-Karkhi in one narration) hold that the option of specification alone suffices. Additionally, there is a dispute regarding whether this option can be granted to the seller: al-Karkhi allows it by istihsan, while al-Mujarrad disallows it since the need exists only for the buyer. The commentary clarifies the 'illa (legal cause) for the dispensation: two factors—need and avoidance of dispute—must both be present for the ruling of permissibility to apply. With three items, both are present; with four, the need is absent, so the dispensation fails.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): An option granted to the buyer to specify which item he will take from among multiple items (e.g., garments) within a specified period.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a contract that allows the party to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that deviates from qiyas due to a stronger evidence or need.
علة ('illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that gives rise to a legal ruling; here, it comprises need and prevention of dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, which of the following is required for khiyar al-ta'yin to be valid?
A) The option must be stipulated, but khiyar al-shart is not required.
B) The option must be accompanied by khiyar al-shart.
C) The option can be granted to either buyer or seller.
D) The number of items must be at least two.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid by istihsan for three items because the 'illa of need and dispute prevention is complete; it must be accompanied by khiyar al-shart and is only for the buyer.

Taking Pre-emption During Option Period: Effect on the Option
Ruling on shuf'a during khiyar and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking shuf'a while having khiyar, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding ownership during khiyar.

Core Idea
Taking shuf'a drops the khiyar by consensus; the disagreement is over ownership at the time.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a buyer with an option (khiyar) on a property takes pre-emption (shuf'a) on an adjacent property. The act is considered evidence of satisfaction, thereby dropping the option. However, the underlying reasoning differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, centered on whether ownership transfers during the khiyar period. Understanding this dispute clarifies key Hanafi principles on the interaction of options and property rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Core Ruling
Recognize the hypothetical: a buyer purchases a house with an option (khiyar). Later, an adjacent house is sold, and the buyer takes it via shuf'a. The core ruling: this act drops the buyer's original option by consensus (ijma'). This is the starting point.
The consensus is across the Hanafi school, not necessarily between madhahib.
2
Trace the Reasoning: Two Intra-Hanafi Views
Understand that Imām Abu Hanīfa holds ownership does not transfer during khiyar, so the demand for shuf'a implies a choice to own, thereby dropping the option retroactively. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that ownership transfers immediately, so taking shuf'a is a direct exercise of ownership that drops the option.
Both views reach the same outcome regarding the option.
3
Contrast with Khiyar al-Ru'ya
Note that the ruling is specific to khiyar al-shart or khiyar al-ta'yin. The text explicitly distinguishes khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight), where taking shuf'a does not drop the option, even if explicitly stated, because the option of sight is not subject to implication.
This contrast highlights the limited scope of the consensus.
4
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Difference)
Although the option drops in both views, the ownership status differs. Under Imam's view, the buyer was not the owner at the time of shuf'a, yet the act retroactively establishes ownership. Under Sahibayn, the buyer was already owner. This affects related rulings, e.g., risk of loss during the option period.
The dispute is largely theoretical for this case but has implications for other scenarios.
5
Locate the Source Authority
Recognize that the ruling is attributed to al-Jami' al-Kabir (a zahir al-riwayah text) and supported by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. The text also references al-Karkhi's view on combining options, linking to broader debates on khiyar al-ta'yin.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah, reinforcing the reliability.

Source Text

(وأخذه بالشفعة داراً بيعت بجنب ما شُرِطَ فيه الخيارُ رِضاً ) : أي اشترى داراً على أنه بالخيار، فبيعت دار بجنب تلك الدار ، فأخذها المشتري بالشفعة، فهذا الأخذ دليل رضاه بشراء تلك الدار ؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة يقتضي إجازة في شراء المشفوع به يشترط ، وهو المذكورُ في «الجامع الكبير»، قال فخر الإسلام له له له : هو ا الصحيح، فعلى قول هذا القائل إذا لم يشترط خيار الشرط يلزم العقد بأحدهما حتى لا يرد إلا أحدهما. وعلى قول الكرخي له : له أن يردهما ؛ لأن هذا الخيار عنده بمنزلة خيار الشرط، وإن شرط خيار الشرط مع خيارِ التّعيين جاز ، فإن ردَّهما بخيار الشرط في المدة، أو ردّ أحدهما بخيار التعيين كان له ذلك ، وإذا مضت المدة بطل خيار الشرط فلا يمكن ردّهما جميعاً، ويبقى له خيار التعيين، فيرد أحدهما ، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إلى «رمز الحقائق»(۱) ، و«منح الغفار»)، والله أعلم بحقيقة الأسرار. [1]قوله : رضاً ؛ يسقط به الخيار إجماعاً، بخلاف خيار الرؤية، حيث لا يسقط بأخذ الشفعة، فإنه لا يسقط بالصراحة، فكذا بالدلالة. كذا ذكره الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز (۳).
(-4)
(٢) قوله : لأن ...الخ ؛ حاصله : أن الأخذ بالشفعة إنما يحصل بعد طلبها، وطلبها [٢] دليل على أن يختار المشتري ملكه في الدار المشتراة بالخيار ؛ لأنه لم يطلبها إلا لدفع ضرر الجوار، والجوار لا يثبت إلا باستدامة الملكِ في الدَّارِ المشتراة بالخيار، واستدامة الملكِ يقتضي الملك، ولا ملك مع الخيار. فيتضمن ذلك الطلب سقوط الخيارِ سابقاً عليه، فيثبت الملك من وقت شراء الدار ، فظهر أن الجوار كان ثابتاً عند بيع الدَّارِ الثانية، وهو يوجب الشفعة، وهذا بناءً على مذهب الإمام. وأما عندهما : فالمبيعُ يدخلُ في ملكه فيجوز أن يأخذ بالشفعة، ويسقط بذلك خياره ؛ لأن الشفعة لدفع ضرر الجار الدخيل، والإنسان لا يدفع ضرر الجار في دار يريد ردّها
And his taking by pre-emption of a house sold adjacent to that in which the option was stipulated is satisfaction: meaning, he bought a house with the stipulation that he has the option (khiyar). Then a house adjacent to that house was sold, and he took it by shuf'a. This taking is evidence of his satisfaction with the purchase of that house. Because taking by shuf'a requires ratification of the purchase of the thing with which the right of pre-emption is established (the property sold with khiyar). It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. Fakhr al-Islam said: that is the correct (view). So according to this proponent, if he did not stipulate khiyar al-shart, the contract becomes binding with one of them (the two options) so he may only return one. And according to al-Karkhi, he may return both because this option in his view is like khiyar al-shart. And if he stipulates khiyar al-shart along with khiyar al-ta'yin, it is valid. Then if he returns both by khiyar al-shart within the period, or returns one by khiyar al-ta'yin, that is permissible. And if the period ends, khiyar al-shart becomes void so he cannot return both, and his khiyar al-ta'yin remains, so he may return one. If you desire more detail, refer to Ramz al-Haqa'iq and Manh al-Ghaffar. And Allah knows best. [1] His statement: 'satisfaction'; by it the option is dropped by consensus (ijma'), unlike khiyar al-ru'ya where it is not dropped by taking shuf'a, because it is not dropped explicitly, so likewise by implication. Thus mentioned by al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz. (-4) (2) His statement: 'because...' its summary: that taking by shuf'a only occurs after its demand, and its demand is evidence that the buyer chooses his ownership in the house bought with option; because he only demanded it to repel the harm of adjacency, and adjacency is only established by the continuation of ownership in the house bought with option, and continuation of ownership implies ownership, and there is no ownership with an option. So this demand includes the dropping of the option prior to it, so ownership is established from the time of purchase of the house, so it becomes apparent that adjacency was established at the time of the sale of the second house, and it necessitates shuf'a. And this is based on the doctrine of Imam Abu Hanifa. As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the sold item enters into his ownership, so it is permissible for him to take by shuf'a, and by it his option drops, because shuf'a is to repel the harm of an intervening neighbor, and a person does not repel the harm of a neighbor in a house he intends to return.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where a buyer has a khiyar (option) in a house purchase, and then another adjacent house is sold, which he takes by shuf'a (pre-emption). The ruling is that this act of taking shuf'a indicates his satisfaction (rida) with the original purchase, thereby dropping his option by consensus (ijma'). The commentary explains the reasoning: by demanding shuf'a, the buyer demonstrates his desire to retain ownership of the first house (since shuf'a is only for a neighbor), and that requires that his option be dropped retroactively. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, during the khiyar period, ownership has not transferred to the buyer, so he technically cannot be considered a neighbor for shuf'a; yet the act of demanding shuf'a implies a choice to own, thereby dropping the option. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the sold item enters the buyer's ownership even with khiyar, so he can validly take shuf'a, and doing so drops his option. The passage also contrasts this with khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight), where taking shuf'a does not drop the option, even if explicitly stated, because the option of sight is not subject to such implication. The text also ties back to the earlier discussion on khiyar al-ta'yin and the dispute between al-Karkhi and others regarding the combination of options.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property adjacent to his own, to prevent harm from a new neighbor.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The option to cancel a sale after seeing the purchased item which was not previously seen.
رضا (rida): Satisfaction or consent; in this context, the act of taking shuf'a is considered evidence of satisfaction with the original purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of taking shuf'a on khiyar al-ru'ya?
A) It drops the option by consensus.
B) It does not drop the option, even if explicitly stated.
C) It drops the option only if the buyer also explicitly states satisfaction.
D) It drops the option because adjacency implies ownership.

Key Takeaway
Taking shuf'a during a khiyar (except khiyar al-ru'ya) drops the option by consensus; the intra-madhhab dispute on ownership does not affect this practical outcome.
