Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Taking Pre-emption Cancels the Option of Condition by Consensus
Explains legal effect of taking shuf'a during khiyar al-shart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that exercising pre-emption during khiyar al-shart cancels the option, explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and distinguish it from khiyar al-ru'ya.

Core Idea
Taking shuf'a during khiyar al-shart is legally deemed consent that cancels the option by ijma.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya addresses a key interaction between two major concepts in Hanafi sales law: khiyar al-shart and shuf'a. When a buyer with a stipulated option exercises pre-emption over an adjacent property, his action is not neutral—it is taken as proof of his satisfaction with the original purchase, thereby canceling his right to rescind. The ruling is agreed upon by consensus (ijma), though the underlying reasoning differs between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly applying both options and pre-emption rights in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A buyer purchases a house with khiyar al-shart (e.g., a three-day option to cancel). Another adjacent house is sold, and the buyer takes shuf'a (pre-emption). The question is: what happens to the option?
2
State the ruling
By consensus (ijma), this act cancels the option. The taking of shuf'a is legally considered evidence of consent (rida) to the original purchase.
The ruling applies only to khiyar al-shart, not to khiyar al-ru'ya.
3
Understand the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam holds that during khiyar al-shart, ownership does not transfer to the buyer. Shuf'a requires permanent adjacency, which requires ownership. So taking shuf'a implies the buyer has chosen to confirm the purchase, establishing ownership retroactively and thereby canceling the option.
Thus, adjacency is deemed to have existed at the time of the second sale.
4
Understand the reasoning of the Sahibayn
The two disciples hold that ownership transfers immediately even with an option. Therefore, taking shuf'a is directly valid, and it cancels the option because a person does not seek to repel an intrusive neighbor from a property he intends to return.
Both lines of reasoning lead to the same conclusion.
5
Note the exception: Khiyar al-Ru'ya
Unlike khiyar al-shart, taking shuf'a does not cancel khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection), even if done explicitly. The reason is that khiyar al-ru'ya is not a right to cancel at will but a right to inspect, and taking shuf'a does not constitute consent to the sale.
This exception is highlighted in the text by contrast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الخيار - خيار الشرط.
وأخذه بالشفعة داراً بيعت بجنب ما شرط فيه الخيار رضاً
(وأخذه بالشفعة داراً بيعت بجنب ما شُرِطَ فيه الخيارُ رِضاً ) : أي اشترى داراً على أنه بالخيار، فبيعت دار بجنب تلك الدار ، فأخذها المشتري بالشفعة، فهذا الأخذ دليل رضاه بشراء تلك الدار ؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة يقتضي إجازة في شراء المشفوع به يشترط ، وهو المذكورُ في «الجامع الكبير»، قال فخر الإسلام له : هو الصحيح، فعلى قول هذا القائل إذا لم يشترط خيار الشرط يلزم العقد بأحدهما حتى لا يرد إلا أحدهما. وعلى قول الكرخي له : له أن يردهما ؛ لأن هذا الخيار عنده بمنزلة خيار الشرط، وإن شرط خيار الشرط مع خيارِ التّعيين جاز ، فإن ردَّهما بخيار الشرط في المدة، أو ردّ أحدهما بخيار التعيين كان له ذلك ، وإذا مضت المدة بطل خيار الشرط فلا يمكن ردّهما جميعاً، ويبقى له خيار التعيين، فيرد أحدهما ، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إلى «رمز الحقائق» و «منح الغفار»، والله أعلم بحقيقة الأسرار. [1]قوله : رضاً ؛ يسقط به الخيار إجماعاً، بخلاف خيار الرؤية، حيث لا يسقط بأخذ الشفعة، فإنه لا يسقط بالصراحة، فكذا بالدلالة. كذا ذكره الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز». [۲] قوله : لأن ...الخ ؛ حاصله : أن الأخذ بالشفعة إنما يحصل بعد طلبها، وطلبها دليل على أن يختار المشتري ملكه في الدار المشتراة بالخيار ؛ لأنه لم يطلبها إلا لدفع ضرر الجوار، والجوار لا يثبت إلا باستدامة الملكِ في الدَّارِ المشتراة بالخيار، واستدامة الملكِ يقتضي الملك، ولا ملك مع الخيار. فيتضمن ذلك الطلب سقوط الخيارِ سابقاً عليه، فيثبت الملك من وقت شراء الدار ، فظهر أن الجوار كان ثابتاً عند بيع الدَّارِ الثانية، وهو يوجب الشفعة، وهذا بناءً على مذهب الإمام. وأما عندهما : فالمبيعُ يدخلُ في ملكه فيجوز أن يأخذ بالشفعة، ويسقط بذلك خياره ؛ لأن الشفعة لدفع ضرر الجار الدخيل، والإنسان لا يدفع ضرر الجار في دار يريد ردّها
Kitab al-Bay', Chapter of Option – Option of Condition. And his taking by pre-emption a house sold adjacent to that in which the option was stipulated is consent. (And his taking by pre-emption a house sold adjacent to that in which the option was stipulated is consent) meaning: he bought a house with the condition that he has the option, then a house was sold adjacent to that house, so the buyer took it by pre-emption. So this taking is evidence of his consent to purchasing that house because taking by pre-emption implies authorization in the purchase of the subject of pre-emption that is stipulated. It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. Fakhr al-Islam said: it is correct. According to the statement of this proponent, if he did not stipulate the option of condition, the contract becomes binding with one of them such that he cannot return except one. According to al-Karkhi, he may return both because in his view this option is like the option of condition. If he stipulates the option of condition along with the option of determination, it is valid. If he returns both by virtue of the option of condition within the period, or returns one by virtue of the option of determination, that is permitted. When the period expires, the option of condition becomes void, so it is not possible to return both; his option of determination remains, so he returns one. If you desire more detail, refer to Ramz al-Haqa'iq and Minah al-Ghaffar, and Allah knows best the reality of secrets. [1] His statement: 'consent' – the option is cancelled by it by consensus, unlike the option of inspection, which is not cancelled by taking pre-emption, because it is not cancelled explicitly, so likewise by implication. Thus al-Zayla'i mentioned it in Sharh al-Kanz. [۲] His statement: 'because... etc.' – its summary: taking by pre-emption only occurs after demanding it, and demanding it is evidence that the buyer chooses ownership of the house purchased with the option because he only demands it to repel the harm of adjacency, and adjacency is only established by continuation of ownership in the house purchased with the option, and continuation of ownership necessitates ownership, and there is no ownership with the option. So that demand entails the cancellation of the option prior to it, so ownership is established from the time of purchasing the house. Thus it becomes clear that adjacency was established at the time of sale of the second house, and it necessitates pre-emption. This is based on the doctrine of Imam (Abu Hanifa). As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the sold item enters his ownership, so he may take by pre-emption, and his option is thereby cancelled because pre-emption is to repel the harm of an intrusive neighbour, and a person does not repel the harm of a neighbour in a house he intends to return.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya addresses the interaction between khiyar al-shart (option of condition) and shuf'a (pre-emption). The core ruling is that if someone buys a property with a stipulated option (e.g., a three-day option to cancel or confirm) and then exercises pre-emption over an adjacent property that is sold, that act of taking shuf'a is legally considered proof of his consent (rida) to the original purchase, thus canceling his option. This is by consensus (ijma). The reasoning, based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view, is that shuf'a is only valid if the claimant has a permanent right of adjacency (jiwar). Adjacency requires continuous ownership; during the option period, the buyer does not have full ownership (according to Imam), so if he takes shuf'a, it implies he has chosen to confirm the purchase and establish ownership retroactively from the contract date, thereby canceling his option. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the sold item enters the buyer's ownership immediately even with an option, so taking shuf'a is also valid and cancels the option because one would not seek to repel a neighbour's harm from a property they intend to return. The passage also discusses the combination of khiyar al-shart with khiyar al-ta'yin (option of determining which of two items to keep). According to some (Fakhr al-Islam), if no option of condition is stipulated, the contract becomes binding on one item and only one can be returned. According to al-Karkhi, if both options are stipulated, the buyer can return both items during the option period because khiyar al-ta'yin is analogous to khiyar al-shart. Once the period expires, khiyar al-shart lapses and only khiyar al-ta'yin remains, allowing the return of one item. This intra-Hanafi difference is noted but the relied-upon view is not explicitly declared. The passage concludes by directing to other texts for further detail.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption held by a co-owner or neighbour to purchase a property sold to a third party, to prevent harm from an intrusive neighbour
رضا (rida): Consent or satisfaction; in this context, the buyer's act of taking shuf'a is taken as evidence of his consent to the original purchase, thereby cancelling his option
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of inspection; the right to inspect a purchased item and return it if not satisfied, without a stipulated period

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer has a 5-day option (khiyar al-shart) on a house. He takes pre-emption on an adjacent plot. What is the effect on his option?
A) His option remains, because taking shuf'a is a separate transaction.
B) His option is cancelled by consensus.
C) His option is only cancelled if he explicitly confirms the house purchase.
D) His option becomes a khiyar al-ru'ya.

Key Takeaway
Exercising pre-emption (shuf'a) during khiyar al-shart cancels the option by consensus, as it is deemed implicit consent to the original purchase.

Combining Option of Condition and Option of Determination: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on returning both items with combined options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on returning both items when khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin are combined, and identify the practical consequence.

Core Idea
When both options are present, the buyer may return both items during the option period according to al-Karkhi, but only one according to Fakhr al-Islam.

This portion of the passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a sale with both khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin. The question is whether the buyer can return all items during the option period or only one. Two authoritative Hanafi scholars, Fakhr al-Islam and al-Karkhi, offer differing views. Understanding this nuance is important for correctly applying sales with multiple options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A buyer purchases two items with both khiyar al-shart (option of condition, i.e., a period to cancel) and khiyar al-ta'yin (option of determination, i.e., the right to choose which item to keep). The question: can he return both items during the option period?
2
State the two views
Fakhr al-Islam holds that if no separate option of condition is stipulated, then the contract becomes binding on one item, so only one can be returned. If both options are stipulated, then during the period both can be returned. Al-Karkhi holds that even without a separate option of condition, the buyer can return both because khiyar al-ta'yin is analogous to khiyar al-shart. After the period expires, khiyar al-shart lapses, and only khiyar al-ta'yin remains, so only one can be returned.
The text does not provide a definitive tarjih.
3
Understand the reasoning
Al-Karkhi draws an analogy (qiyas) between khiyar al-ta'yin and khiyar al-shart in terms of flexibility. Fakhr al-Islam sees the default as the contract being binding on one item and thus restricts the return.
The difference stems from how to interpret the nature of khiyar al-ta'yin.
4
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, if a buyer has both options and follows al-Karkhi's view, he can return both items within the option period. After the period, he can only return one. According to Fakhr al-Islam, if no separate option of condition, he can only return one from the start.
The consequence affects the buyer's flexibility.
5
Note the unresolved nature
The passage does not resolve the dispute; it directs the reader to other works (Ramz al-Haqa'iq, Minah al-Ghaffar) for more detail. This indicates that the issue remains a point of ijtihad within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وأخذه بالشفعة داراً بيعت بجنب ما شُرِطَ فيه الخيارُ رِضاً ) : أي اشترى داراً على أنه بالخيار، فبيعت دار بجنب تلك الدار ، فأخذها المشتري بالشفعة، فهذا الأخذ دليل رضاه بشراء تلك الدار ؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة يقتضي إجازة في شراء المشفوع به يشترط ، وهو المذكورُ في «الجامع الكبير»، قال فخر الإسلام له : هو الصحيح، فعلى قول هذا القائل إذا لم يشترط خيار الشرط يلزم العقد بأحدهما حتى لا يرد إلا أحدهما. وعلى قول الكرخي له : له أن يردهما ؛ لأن هذا الخيار عنده بمنزلة خيار الشرط، وإن شرط خيار الشرط مع خيارِ التّعيين جاز ، فإن ردَّهما بخيار الشرط في المدة، أو ردّ أحدهما بخيار التعيين كان له ذلك ، وإذا مضت المدة بطل خيار الشرط فلا يمكن ردّهما جميعاً، ويبقى له خيار التعيين، فيرد أحدهما ، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إلى «رمز الحقائق» و «منح الغفار»، والله أعلم بحقيقة الأسرار. [1]قوله : رضاً ؛ يسقط به الخيار إجماعاً، بخلاف خيار الرؤية، حيث لا يسقط بأخذ الشفعة، فإنه لا يسقط بالصراحة، فكذا بالدلالة. كذا ذكره الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز». [۲] قوله : لأن ...الخ ؛ حاصله : أن الأخذ بالشفعة إنما يحصل بعد طلبها، وطلبها دليل على أن يختار المشتري ملكه في الدار المشتراة بالخيار ؛ لأنه لم يطلبها إلا لدفع ضرر الجوار، والجوار لا يثبت إلا باستدامة الملكِ في الدَّارِ المشتراة بالخيار، واستدامة الملكِ يقتضي الملك، ولا ملك مع الخيار. فيتضمن ذلك الطلب سقوط الخيارِ سابقاً عليه، فيثبت الملك من وقت شراء الدار ، فظهر أن الجوار كان ثابتاً عند بيع الدَّارِ الثانية، وهو يوجب الشفعة، وهذا بناءً على مذهب الإمام. وأما عندهما : فالمبيعُ يدخلُ في ملكه فيجوز أن يأخذ بالشفعة، ويسقط بذلك خياره ؛ لأن الشفعة لدفع ضرر الجار الدخيل، والإنسان لا يدفع ضرر الجار في دار يريد ردّها
Kitab al-Bay', Chapter of Option – Option of Condition. And his taking by pre-emption a house sold adjacent to that in which the option was stipulated is consent. (And his taking by pre-emption a house sold adjacent to that in which the option was stipulated is consent) meaning: he bought a house with the condition that he has the option, then a house was sold adjacent to that house, so the buyer took it by pre-emption. So this taking is evidence of his consent to purchasing that house because taking by pre-emption implies authorization in the purchase of the subject of pre-emption that is stipulated. It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. Fakhr al-Islam said: it is correct. According to the statement of this proponent, if he did not stipulate the option of condition, the contract becomes binding with one of them such that he cannot return except one. According to al-Karkhi, he may return both because in his view this option is like the option of condition. If he stipulates the option of condition along with the option of determination, it is valid. If he returns both by virtue of the option of condition within the period, or returns one by virtue of the option of determination, that is permitted. When the period expires, the option of condition becomes void, so it is not possible to return both; his option of determination remains, so he returns one. If you desire more detail, refer to Ramz al-Haqa'iq and Minah al-Ghaffar, and Allah knows best the reality of secrets. [1] His statement: 'consent' – the option is cancelled by it by consensus, unlike the option of inspection, which is not cancelled by taking pre-emption, because it is not cancelled explicitly, so likewise by implication. Thus al-Zayla'i mentioned it in Sharh al-Kanz. [۲] His statement: 'because... etc.' – its summary: taking by pre-emption only occurs after demanding it, and demanding it is evidence that the buyer chooses ownership of the house purchased with the option because he only demands it to repel the harm of adjacency, and adjacency is only established by continuation of ownership in the house purchased with the option, and continuation of ownership necessitates ownership, and there is no ownership with the option. So that demand entails the cancellation of the option prior to it, so ownership is established from the time of purchasing the house. Thus it becomes clear that adjacency was established at the time of sale of the second house, and it necessitates pre-emption. This is based on the doctrine of Imam (Abu Hanifa). As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the sold item enters his ownership, so he may take by pre-emption, and his option is thereby cancelled because pre-emption is to repel the harm of an intrusive neighbour, and a person does not repel the harm of a neighbour in a house he intends to return.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya addresses the interaction between khiyar al-shart (option of condition) and shuf'a (pre-emption). The core ruling is that if someone buys a property with a stipulated option (e.g., a three-day option to cancel or confirm) and then exercises pre-emption over an adjacent property that is sold, that act of taking shuf'a is legally considered proof of his consent (rida) to the original purchase, thus canceling his option. This is by consensus (ijma). The reasoning, based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view, is that shuf'a is only valid if the claimant has a permanent right of adjacency (jiwar). Adjacency requires continuous ownership; during the option period, the buyer does not have full ownership (according to Imam), so if he takes shuf'a, it implies he has chosen to confirm the purchase and establish ownership retroactively from the contract date, thereby canceling his option. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the sold item enters the buyer's ownership immediately even with an option, so taking shuf'a is also valid and cancels the option because one would not seek to repel a neighbour's harm from a property they intend to return. The passage also discusses the combination of khiyar al-shart with khiyar al-ta'yin (option of determining which of two items to keep). According to some (Fakhr al-Islam), if no option of condition is stipulated, the contract becomes binding on one item and only one can be returned. According to al-Karkhi, if both options are stipulated, the buyer can return both items during the option period because khiyar al-ta'yin is analogous to khiyar al-shart. Once the period expires, khiyar al-shart lapses and only khiyar al-ta'yin remains, allowing the return of one item. This intra-Hanafi difference is noted but the relied-upon view is not explicitly declared. The passage concludes by directing to other texts for further detail.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option of determination; the right of the buyer to choose which of two or more items to keep in a single sale
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Honorific title for a Hanafi scholar, likely referring to Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH)
الكرخي (al-Karkhi): Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH), a leading Hanafi jurist

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale with both khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin, according to al-Karkhi, how many items can the buyer return during the option period?
A) None.
B) One.
C) Both.
D) It depends on the seller's consent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an unresolved dispute on whether a buyer with combined khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin can return both items during the option period; al-Karkhi allows it, Fakhr al-Islam restricts it.
